Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Rulings on Eid Prayer: The Dispute on Additional Takbirs, Thana, and Silence
Describes the Eid prayer rulings and disputes on takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the number of additional takbirs in Eid prayer, the recitation of thana before them, and the silence between takbirs, and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i arguments.

Core Idea
Hanafi: three takbirs per rak'ah, thana before, silence between. Shafi'i: five/four takbirs, no thana, dhikr between.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on the Eid prayer, focusing on three contested issues: the number of additional takbirs, whether the opening supplication (thana) precedes them, and the practice between takbirs. The passage presents the Hanafi position supported by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, contrasting it with the views of Imam al-Shafi'i and others. Understanding these differences clarifies the practical implementation of Eid prayer in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on additional takbirs
State that the Hanafi school holds three additional takbirs in each rak'ah after the opening thana, before qira'ah, based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.
The takbirs are called 'zawa'id' and are sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
Refer to the narration in Athar al-Tahawi from Ibn Mas'ud describing the Prophet's practice: opening takbir, then three takbirs, then recitation, etc.
This is a hadith ahad, but accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Identify the opposing view and its evidence
State that Imam al-Shafi'i follows the narration of Ibn Abbas: five takbirs in the first rak'ah and four in the second, beginning with takbir (no thana).
Ali's view is also mentioned: four in Fitr, one in Adha.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school considers the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud more authentic and acted upon by the salaf, thus preferred over other narrations.
The silence between takbirs (indicated by the Hanafi 'saktah') is also preferred over dhikr to avoid confusion in large congregations.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, Hanafis perform three takbirs with thana first, Shafi'is five/four without thana. The khutbah is after the prayer, unlike Jumu'ah.
This difference affects the actual performance of the Eid prayer in each madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلي ركعتين مثنياً قبل الزوائد، وهي ثلاث في كل ركعة، ويوالي بين القراءتين، ويرفع يديه في الزوائد، ويخطب بعدها خطبتين، يعلم فيها أحكام. مثنياً: حال كونه مثنياً، أي آتيا بالثناء يعني سبحانك اللهم إلخ خلافاً للشافعي ومالك. [رمز الحقائق: ١٠٢/١] ثلاث: لما في آثار الطحاوي عن ابن مسعود له أنه سئل عن كيفية صلاة العيد فقال: يفتتحها بتكبيرة، ثم يكبر بعدها ثلاثاً، ثم يقرأ، ثم يكبر تكبيرة يركع بها، ثم يسجد، ثم يقوم يقرأ، ثم يكبر ثلاثاً، ثم يكبر تكبيرة يركع بها، وقال علي الله أربع في كل ركعة في الفطر، وفي الأضحى واحدة في كل ركعة، ويبدأ بالقراءة فيهما، وقال ابن عباس ما خمس في كل ركعة ويبدأ بالتكبير فيهما، وفي رواية عنه: خمس في الأولى، وأربع في الثانية، وأخذ الشافعي بقول ابن عباس اما. ويسكت بين كل تكبيرتين عندنا، وقال الشافعي: يقول بينهما: سبحان الله، والحمد الله، ولا إله إلا الله، والله أكبر.
He prays two rak'ahs, doing thana before the additional (takbirs), and they are three in each rak'ah, and he maintains continuity between the two recitations, and he raises his hands in the additional (takbirs), and he delivers two khutbahs after it, teaching therein the rulings. 'Muthanniyan': a state of being one who does thana, i.e., saying 'Subhanaka Allahumma' etc., contrary to al-Shafi'i and Malik. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/102] 'Three': as in Athar al-Tahawi from Ibn Mas'ud that he was asked about the manner of the Eid prayer, so he said: he opens with a takbir, then he says three takbirs after it, then he recites, then he says a takbir with which he bows, then he prostrates, then he stands and recites, then he says three takbirs, then he says a takbir with which he bows. And Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: four in each rak'ah in Fitr, and in Adha one in each rak'ah, and he begins with recitation in both. And Ibn Abbas said: five in each rak'ah and he begins with takbir in both, and in one narration from him: five in the first and four in the second. And al-Shafi'i adopted the saying of Ibn Abbas. And we are silent between every two takbirs, while al-Shafi'i says: one says between them: Subhan Allah, wa al-Hamdu lillah, wa la ilaha illa Allah, wa Allahu Akbar.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the rulings of Eid prayer, specifically the number of additional takbirs, the opening supplication (thana'), and the silence or dhikr between takbirs. The text first states the Hanafi position: in the Eid prayer, one prays two rak'ahs, begins with the thana (the opening supplication 'Subhanaka Allahumma') before the additional takbirs, indicating that the thana is recited before the takbirs, not after, which differs from Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik who hold that one should begin with takbirs. The Hanafi evidence is drawn from a narration of Ibn Mas'ud in Athar al-Tahawi, where he describes the Prophet's practice: he would open with the takbir of ihram, then say three additional takbirs, then recite, then bow with a takbir, and similarly in the second rak'ah. The text then presents the views of Ali and Ibn Abbas: Ali reportedly said there are four takbirs in each rak'ah in Eid al-Fitr and one in Eid al-Adha, beginning with recitation; Ibn Abbas said five in each, beginning with takbir, with a variant of five in the first and four in the second. Imam al-Shafi'i adopted Ibn Abbas's view. The Hanafi school follows the narration of Ibn Mas'ud, which is considered stronger. As for the silence between takbirs, the Hanafi position is to pause silently for a duration equal to three tasbihs, while al-Shafi'i recommends saying glorifications between them. The commentary explains that this silence is to avoid confusion for those far away, as the prayer is performed in a large congregation.

Key Terms
الزوائد (al-zawā'id): The additional takbirs in the Eid prayer beyond the obligatory ones.
المثنّي (al-muthannī): The one who recites the thana (the opening supplication) after the first takbir.
الموالاة (al-muwālāh): Continuity between the two recitations (qira'ah) in the two rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many additional takbirs are recited in each rak'ah of the Eid prayer?
A) Four in each
B) Three in each
C) Five in the first and four in the second
D) One in each

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes three additional takbirs per rak'ah in Eid prayer, recited after the opening thana, with silence between them, based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, differing from Shafi'i practice.

Rulings for Latecomer, Missed Prayer, and Differences Between Eids
Rulings on latecomers, missed Eid prayer, and distinctions between the two Eids

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for a latecomer joining the Eid prayer and explain why missed Eid prayer is not made up individually.

Core Idea
The masbuq joins immediately; missed Eid prayer is not made up alone.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses key practical questions about the Eid prayer: how a latecomer should join, what to do if the imam is already bowing, and what happens if one misses the prayer entirely. It also clarifies distinctions between the two Eids and the rulings on sadaqat al-fitr taught in the khutbah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings for the masbuq
Understand that the latecomer must say the opening takbir immediately upon arrival, and if the imam is in ruku, he may join in ruku to catch the rak'ah.
2
Trace the proof for joining in ruku
The ruling is based on the practice of the Companions and the need to preserve congregation. The proof is the hadith that the Prophet said: 'When you come to the prayer and we are in sajdah, then prostrate with us, but do not count it' – similar principle.
3
Analyse the ruling on missed prayer
The text states that if one misses the Eid prayer with the imam, he does not make it up individually because the prayer is legislated with conditions of congregation. This is supported by the consensus of the Companions.
4
Understand the dispute with al-Shafi'i
Al-Shafi'i allows individual performance of the missed Eid prayer by analogy to regular prayers. The Hanafi response is that Eid prayer loses its character when performed alone.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Extract practical differences between the two Eids
In Eid al-Adha, it is recommended to delay eating until after the prayer and to say takbir loudly on the way to the musalla. These practices are based on the Prophet's example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن فاته أول صلاة الإمام يكبر في الحال. ولو خشي المدرك في الركوع أن يرفع الإمام رأسه لو كبر قائماً أتى به راكعاً. ولو ركع الإمام قبل أن يكبر لا يعود إلى القيام ليكبر ولا يكبر في الركوع في ظاهر الرواية، والمسبوق بركعة إذا قام إلى القضاء يقرأ، ثم يكبر؛ لأنه لو بدأ بالتكبير يصير مواليا بين التكبيرات، ولم يقل به أحد الصحابة، ولو بدأ بالقراءة يصير فعله موافقا لقول علي الله ؛ لأنه يقول بالبدء فيهما بالقراءة، والموالاة مستحب حتى لو لم يوال فقد ترك الأولى. (فتح) القراءتين: ندباً بأن يكبر للافتتاح، ثم يستفتح، ثم يكبر ثلاثاً قبل القراءة، ثم إذا قام إلى الثانية يقرأ، فإذا فرغ من القراءة يكبر ثلاثاً، ثم يكبر للركوع. (ع) ويرفع يديه إلخ أي في التكبيرات الزوائد مطلقاً، رفع الإمام أم لا، ولا يضعهما، وعن أبي يوسف لا يرفع في شيء منهما، وصلى أبو يوسف بالناس حين قدم بغداد صلاة العيد، وكبر تكبير ابن عباس لما فإنه صلى خلفه هارون الرشيد فأمره بذلك، والمسألة مجتهدة فيها، وطاعة الإمام فيما ليس بمعصية واجبة، وهذا ليس بمعصية؛ لأنه قول بعض الصحابة. (فتح) الزوائد لقوله علي: "لا ترفع الأيدي إلا في سبع مواطن" وذكر منها تكبيرات العيد، يسكت بين كل تكبيرتين بقدر ثلاث تسبيحات؛ لأنها تقام بجمع عظيم، وبالموالاة تشتبه على من كان نائياً. (ع) ويخطب بعدها: لأنه عليها خطب بعد الصلاة خطبتين، بخلاف الجمعة حيث يخطب لها قبل الصلاة؛ لأن الخطبة فيها شرط، وشرط الشيء يسبقه، وفي العيد ليست بشرط، وبعد الصلاة بيان الأفضلية حتى لو قدمت على الصلاة جاز، ولا تعاد الخطبة بل التقديم خلاف الأولى. (فتح) خطبتين بجلسة بينهما، وهما سنة، فلو قدمتا على الصلاة جاز وكره. (ط) يعلم فيها إلخ: أي يعلم في الخطبة الأحكام الخمسة المتعلقة بصدقة الفطر : الأول: على من تحب، فتجب على الحر المسلم المالك للنصاب، والثاني: لمن تحب فللفقراء والمساكين والثالث متى تجب فبطلوع الفجر من يوم العيد، والرابع: كم تحب، فنصف صاع من بر أو صاع من تمر أو زبيب، والخامس: مم تحب، فمن أربعة = شعير.  كتاب الصلاة ١٥٨ باب صلاة العيدين صدقة الفطر، ولم تقض إن فاتت مع الإمام، وتؤخّر بعذر إلى الغد فقط، وهي أحكام الأضحى، لكن هنا يؤخر الأكل عنها، ويكبّر في الطريق جهرا. أن تظهر في حق من الجمعة أشياء مذكورة، أما ما سواها فبالقيمة. فإن قلت: إذا ندب أداؤها قبل الخروج فلا فائدة لهذا التعليم، قلنا: يمكن يأتي بها في العام القابل، أو في حق من لم يؤدها قبل الصلاة، وينبغي تعليمهم في التي قبلها ليخرجوها في محلها والخطبة في العيد ليست بشرط تؤدى بعد الصلاة لما روي عن ابن عمر ما أنه قال: صليت خلف رسول الله، وخلف أبي بكر، وعمر، وكانوا يبدؤون بالصلاة قبل الخطبة، ولا يؤذنون ولا يقيمون. إنما أحدث بنو أمية الخطبة قبل الصلاة؛ لأنهم كانوا يتكلمون في خطبتهم بما لا يحل، فكان الناس لا يجلسون بعد الصلاة لسماعها فأحدثوا قبل الصلاة. (فتح، مستخلص) صدقة الفطر: هل هي سنة أم واجبة وكيف يخرج ومم يخرج، ونحو ذلك. ولو خطب قبلها يجوز، ويكره لمخالفة السنة. (ع) ولم تقض معناه: لو لم يصل رجل مع الإمام لا يقضيها منفرداً؛ لأن صلاة العيد لم يشرع على سبيل الانفراد هذا عندنا، وقال الشافعي يصليها وحده كما يصلي مع الإمام، أما لو فاتت من الإمام أيضاً فإنها تؤدى في اليوم الثاني، ولو قدر بعد الفوت مع الإمام على إدراكها مع غيره، فعل للاتفاق على جواز تعددها (مستخلص فتح مع الإمام: بأن صلاها الإمام مع الجماعة ولم يصلها هو لا يقضيها في الوقت ولا بعده؛ لأنها شرعت بشرائط لا تتم بالمنفرد. (ع) بعذر بأن غم عليهم الهلال، وشهد بالهلال عند الإمام بعد الزوال أو قبله بحيث لا يمكن جمع الناس قبله، أو صلاها في غيم فظهر أنها وقعت بعد الزوال [ رمز الحقائق: ۱۰۲/۱]، أو حدث عذر آخر من الصلاة في اليوم الأول يصلونها في الغد ولم تقض بعده؛ لأن الأصل فيها أن لا تقضى كالجمعة إلا أنا تركناه بالحديث، وهو حديث شهادة رؤية الهلال بعد الزوال. (مستخلص عيني) فقط عندنا، وعند الشافعي: يؤخر إلى ما بعد الغد أيضاً. (ط) وهي أحكام إلخ [ أي الأحكام المذكورة في صلاة عيد الفطر من الشروط والمندوبات. (رمز الحقائق: ١٠٢/١)] أي إن ما ذكر من أول الباب إلى هنا من الشروط والمندوبات في الفطر كلها في الأضحى كذلك إلا أن المستحب أن يؤخر الأكل في الأضحى إلى ما بعد الصلاة؛ لما روي أنه عليه كان لا يطعم يوم النحر حتى يرجع من المصلى فيأكل أضحيته، ولأن الناس في ضيافة الله تعالى فالأكل من مائدة الضيافة أولى، وهذا في حق من يضحي ليأكل عن أضحيته أو لا، أما في حق غيره فلا بأس أن يأكل قبلها ولا يكره في حق من يضحي أيضاً. (عيني، مستخلص) ويكبر إلخ: هذا فرق آخر بين الفطر والأضحى، أي يكبر في طريق المصلى جهراً في الأضحى؛ لقوله تعالى: وَاذْكُرُوا اللهَ فِي أَيَّامٍ مَعْدُودَاتٍ (البقرة : ۲۰۳)، المراد به التكبير في هذه الأيام مطلقاً؛ ولما روي أن النبي عليه كان يكبر في طريق المصلى جهراً في يوم الأضحى، ثم يقطع التكبير كما انتهى إلى المصلى، وفي رواية: حتى يشرع الإمام فيها. (مستخلص، فتح)
Whoever misses the first takbir of the imam, he should say the takbir immediately. If a latecomer in bowing fears that the imam will raise his head if he says the takbir standing, he should perform it while bowing. If the imam bowed before he said the takbir, he should not return to standing to say it, nor should he say it in bowing according to the apparent narration. And the one who missed a rak'ah, when he stands to make it up, he recites first then says the takbir; because if he begins with the takbir, he would be connecting the takbirs consecutively, which no companion held. And if he begins with recitation, his action agrees with the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), because he held beginning with recitation in both. And continuity (muwalat) is recommended, so if one does not maintain it, he has abandoned the superior. (Fath) The two recitations: it is recommended that he says the opening takbir, then says the opening supplication, then says three takbirs before recitation, then when he stands for the second rak'ah he recites, and when he finishes recitation he says three takbirs, then says the takbir for bowing. (Ayni) And he raises his hands etc.: meaning in all the additional takbirs, whether the imam raises or not, and he does not place them down. From Abu Yusuf: he does not raise in any of them. And Abu Yusuf led the people in Eid prayer when he came to Baghdad, and he recited the takbirs according to Ibn Abbas, because Harun al-Rashid prayed behind him and ordered him to do so. And the matter is one of ijtihad, and obeying the imam in what is not disobedience is obligatory, and this is not disobedience because it is a saying of some companions. (Fath) The additional (takbirs): because of Ali's saying: "Do not raise the hands except in seven places" and he mentioned from them the takbirs of Eid. He is silent between every two takbirs for the duration of three tasbihs, because it is performed in a large congregation, and with continuity it becomes confusing for those far away. (Ayni) And he delivers the khutbah after it: because he delivers two khutbahs after the prayer, unlike Jumu'ah where he delivers before the prayer because the khutbah is a condition there and a condition precedes its object, whereas in Eid it is not a condition, and after the prayer indicates preferability, so if it is offered before the prayer it is permissible, and the khutbah is not repeated, but preceding is contrary to the better. (Fath) Two khutbahs with a sitting between them, and they are sunnah, so if they are presented before the prayer it is permissible but disliked. (Tahawi) He teaches therein: meaning he teaches in the khutbah the five rulings related to sadaqat al-fitr: first: upon whom it is obligatory: it is obligatory on the free Muslim who owns the nisab; second: for whom it is for the poor and needy; third: when it becomes obligatory: at the break of dawn on the day of Eid; fourth: how much: half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or raisins; fifth: from what: from four = barley. [PAGE_159] Book of Prayer 158 Chapter of Eid Prayer. Sadaqat al-fitr, and it is not made up if missed with the imam, and it is delayed due to an excuse only until the next day. And it (the Eid prayer of Fitr) has the rulings of Adha, but here one delays eating, and says the takbir loudly on the way. That it appears in the right of the congregation things mentioned. As for other than that, then by value. If you say: if it is recommended to perform it before going out, there is no benefit in this teaching, we say: perhaps he will perform it the next year, or for one who did not perform it before the prayer. And it is recommended to teach them in the one before it so they may give it in its proper time. And the khutbah in Eid is not a condition, it is performed after the prayer because of what is narrated from Ibn Umar that he said: 'I prayed behind the Messenger of Allah, and behind Abu Bakr, and Umar, and they would begin with the prayer before the khutbah, and they did not call adhan or iqamah.' The Umayyads innovated the khutbah before the prayer because they would speak in their khutbah about what was not permissible, so the people would not sit after the prayer to listen, so they innovated it before. (Fath, Mustakhlas) Sadaqat al-fitr: whether it is sunnah or obligatory, how to give, and from what, and so on. And if he delivers the khutbah before it, it is permissible but disliked for contradicting the sunnah. (Ayni) And it is not made up meaning: if a man does not pray with the imam, he does not make it up individually, because the Eid prayer is not legislated individually according to us. And al-Shafi'i says: he prays it alone as he prays with the imam. But if it is missed from the imam as well, then it is performed on the second day. And if after missing it one can catch it with another group, he does so due to consensus on the permissibility of multiple congregations. (Mustakhlas Fath) With the imam: i.e., the imam prayed with the congregation and he did not pray it, he does not make it up in its time or after, because it is legislated with conditions not fulfilled by an individual. (Ayni) Due to an excuse: such as the moon being obscured, and the sighting is witnessed before the imam after noon or before such that it is not possible to gather people before, or he prayed in cloudy weather and then it appears that it occurred after noon [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/102], or any other excuse from the prayer on the first day: they pray it on the next day and it is not made up after that, because the principle is that it is not made up like Jumu'ah, but we have left this principle due to the hadith of the witness of the sighting of the moon after noon. (Mustakhlas Ayni) Only according to us, while al-Shafi'i says: delay it until after the next day as well. (Tahawi) And it (the Eid prayer of Fitr) has the rulings etc.: meaning the rulings mentioned from the beginning of the chapter up to here regarding conditions and recommended acts in Fitr are all likewise in Adha, except that it is recommended to delay eating in Adha until after the prayer, because of what is narrated that he (peace be upon him) would not eat on the day of Nahr until he returned from the musalla and ate his sacrifice, and because the people are guests of Allah, so eating from the table of hospitality is better. And this is for the one who sacrifices to eat from his sacrifice or not, but for others there is no harm in eating before it, and it is not disliked for the one who sacrifices either. (Ayni, Mustakhlas) And he says takbir etc.: this is another difference between Fitr and Adha: i.e., he says the takbir loudly on the way to the musalla in Adha, due to His saying: 'And remember Allah during the appointed days' (Surah al-Baqarah: 203), which means the takbir in these days absolutely; and because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would say the takbir loudly on the way to the musalla on the day of Adha, then he would stop the takbir when he reached the musalla, and in one narration: until the imam begins. (Mustakhlas, Fath)
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings for the latecomer (masbuq) to the Eid prayer, the ruling on missed prayer, and the distinctions between the two Eids. It begins with the rule for someone who misses the first takbir of the imam: he must say the opening takbir immediately upon arrival. If the imam is bowing and the latecomer fears that raising hands and saying takbir while standing will cause him to miss the bowing, he may say the takbir while in bowing. If the imam bowed before the latecomer said the takbir, he does not return to standing to say it, nor does he say it in bowing according to the apparent transmission. The one who missed a full rak'ah, when he stands to complete his prayer, recites the Fatihah and a surah first, then says the additional takbirs. This is because beginning with takbirs would cause him to connect the takbirs consecutively, which no companion practiced, and beginning with recitation agrees with the view of Ali. The commentary explains that continuity between the two recitations is recommended, not obligatory. The text then discusses the recommendation to raise hands in all additional takbirs, with a note that Abu Yusuf did not do so. It also describes the ruling on the khutbah: two khutbahs delivered after the prayer, with a sitting between them. Unlike Jumu'ah, the khutbah is not a condition for Eid prayer; it is sunnah. Delivering it before the prayer is permissible but disliked as it contradicts the sunnah. The passage then explains the teaching of sadaqat al-fitr in the khutbah. It clarifies that the Eid prayer is not made up individually if missed with the imam, following the Hanafi view, while the Shafi'i school allows individual prayer. However, if the entire congregation misses it, it is performed on the second day. An excuse such as obscured moon allows delay to the next day. Finally, the text highlights differences between Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha: in Adha, it is recommended to delay eating until after the prayer, and to say the takbir loudly on the way to the musalla. These rulings are supported by hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbūq): A latecomer who misses part of the congregational prayer with the imam.
صدقة الفطر (ṣadaqat al-fiṭr): Obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan before Eid prayer.
التكبير في الطريق (al-takbīr fī al-ṭarīq): Announcing takbir loudly on the way to the Eid prayer, especially in Adha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person misses the Eid prayer with the imam, what is the ruling?
A) He should make it up individually as two rak'ahs.
B) He should not make it up individually; it is not legislated alone.
C) He should make it up with another congregation if possible, but if not, he prays alone.
D) He should perform four rak'ahs of regular prayer instead.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Eid prayer is a congregational sunnah; it is not made up individually, and the khutbah follows the prayer.

Postponing 'Eid al-Adha Prayer: Ruling and Conditions
Ruling on postponement of 'Eid al-Adha prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on postponing the 'Eid al-Adha prayer and distinguish between postponement with and without a valid excuse.

Core Idea
Postponing 'Eid prayer without excuse is valid but sinful; an excuse removes dislike but does not affect validity.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: if the 'Eid prayer cannot be held on its appointed day, what is the ruling? The commentator explains the time limit, the effect of an excuse, and the distinction between 'Eid al-Adha and 'Eid al-Fitr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time restriction
The 'Eid al-Adha prayer is timed with the sacrifice and may be postponed up to three days (11th, 12th, 13th Dhul Hijjah).
2
Understand the effect of an excuse
A valid excuse (e.g., heavy rain, security concerns) removes the dislike (karahah) of postponement, but without an excuse the postponement is disliked.
The excuse only removes karahah, it does not affect validity.
3
Distinguish postponement without excuse
If the prayer is postponed without a valid excuse, the prayer is valid (sahih) but the people are sinful (isa'ah).
4
Compare with 'Eid al-Fitr
For 'Eid al-Fitr, postponement without excuse invalidates the prayer; the excuse is a condition for validity, not just removing dislike.
5
Note the practical consequence
Communities should strive to pray on time. If delayed, ensure it is within the three days; if without excuse, seek forgiveness but the prayer is accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

باب صلاة العيدين
الأضحية وتكبيرات التشريق في الخطبة، وتؤخّر بعذر إلى ثلاثة أيام،
أي الناس أحكام الأضحية

والتعريف ليس بشيء، وسن
أي لا يتعلق به الثواب

في الخطبة: [هل هما واجبان أم سنتان وكيف يضحي ويكبر ونحو ذلك. (ط، م)] هكذا ذكروا مع أن تكبير التشريق يحتاج إلى تعليمه قبل يوم عرفة للإتيان فيه، فينبغي في خطبة الجمعة التي تكون قبل يوم عرفة، والتشريق في اللغة: إلقاء اللحم في الشمس للجفاف، ولما كان الناس يجفون لحوم الأضاحي سميت ثلاثة أيام بعد يوم النحر بأيام التشريق. (المحشي) وتؤخر بعذر إلخ التأخير هنا إلى ثلاثة أيام؛ لكونها موقتة بوقت الأضحية، فتجوز ما بقي وقتها، وإذا أخرت هل يجوز الذبح قبل الزوال أم لا؟ قال الزيلعي : ولو لم يصل الإمام العيد في اليوم الأول أخروا التضحية إلى الزوال ولا تجزئهم التضحية في اليوم الأول إلا بعد الزوال، وكذا في اليوم الثاني لا تجزئهم قبل الزوال إلا إذا كانوا لا يرجون أن يصلي الإمام فحينئذ تجزئهم، فلو أخرت بلا عذر أساؤوا وجازت، فالعذر هنا لنفي الكراهة فقط، وفي عيد الفطر شرط الجواز. (فتح)
إلى ثلاثة أيام لأنها أيام عيد وأضحية ولا تصلى بعد ذلك، فلو أخر بلا عذر أساء. (ط، ع) والتعريف إلخ: [وهو أن يجتمع الناس يوم عرفة في بعض المواضع تشبيهاً بالواقفين بعرفة. (عيني)] اعلم أن التعريف يأتي لمعان الإعلام والتطييب من العرف وإنشاد الضالة، والوقوف بعرفة، والتشبه بأهل عرفات، وهو المراد هنا، وقوله: "ليس بشيء" أي من حكم الوقوف كقول محمد: دم السمك ليس بشيء أي في حكم الدماء؛ لأنه شيء حقيقة إلا أنه لما لم يكن معتبراً نفى عنه الشيئية وهو نكرة في سياق النفي، فيشمل جميع أوصاف العبادة من الفرض والواجب والسنة، والمستحب ونحوه، وعن أبي يوسف ومحمد في غير رواية الأصول أنه لا يكره؟ لما روي عن ابن عباس لما أنه فعل ذلك بالبصرة، وما يفعله أهل بيت المقدس وأهل الجامع الأزهر بمصر يحمل على هذا، والظاهر أنه مكروه؛ لأن الوقوف عرف عبادة مختصة بالمكان المعين فلا يكون عبادة في غيره كسائر المناسك، وفعل ابن عباس يحتمل أن يكون خرج للاستسقاء ونحوه، لا للتشبه بأهل عرفات. (عيني، فتح)
Book of Prayer. Chapter of the Two 'Eid Prayers. Sacrifice and the takbirs of tashriq in the sermon, and it is postponed due to an excuse up to three days. Meaning: the people (need to know) the rulings of sacrifice. So. And at-ta'rif is not anything, and (it is) sunnah. Meaning: no reward is attached to it. Connected to his statement: he knows, meaning the prayer of al-Adha. In the sermon: [Are they both obligatory or two sunnahs, and how to sacrifice and say takbir and the like.] Thus they mentioned, even though the takbir of tashriq needs to be taught before the day of Arafah to perform it, so it should be in the Friday sermon that occurs before the day of Arafah. And tashriq linguistically: throwing meat in the sun to dry. Since people would dry the meat of sacrifices, the three days after the day of Nahr are called the days of Tashriq. (al-Mahashi) 'And it is postponed due to an excuse etc.' The postponement here is up to three days because it is timed with the time of sacrifice, so it is permissible as long as its time remains. If it is postponed, is slaughter permissible before zawal or not? al-Zayla'i said: If the Imam did not perform the 'Eid prayer on the first day, they delay the sacrifice to zawal and their sacrifice is not valid on the first day except after zawal. Similarly on the second day, it is not valid before zawal unless they do not hope that the Imam will pray, then it is valid for them. So if they postpone without an excuse, they are sinful but it is valid. So the excuse here is only to remove the dislike (karahah). In 'Eid al-Fitr, it is a condition for validity. (Fath) 'Up to three days' because they are days of 'Eid and sacrifice, and it is not prayed after that. So if one postpones without excuse, he sins. (T, A) 'And at-ta'rif etc.': [It is that people gather on the day of Arafah in some places imitating those standing at Arafah. (Ayni)] Know that ta'rif has meanings of informing, perfuming from 'arf, and calling the lost, and standing at Arafah, and imitating the people of Arafat, and that is what is meant here. His statement 'is not anything' means from the ruling of standing (wuquf), like Muhammad's statement: 'The blood of fish is not anything' i.e., in the ruling of bloods; because it is a thing in reality, but since it is not considered, he denies its thingness, and it is an indefinite noun in the context of negation, so it includes all descriptions of worship from obligatory, required, sunnah, recommended, etc. And from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in non-principle narrations that it is not disliked? Because of what is narrated from Ibn Abbas that he did that in Basra, and what the people of Bayt al-Maqdis and the people of al-Azhar Mosque in Egypt do is interpreted accordingly. The apparent view is that it is disliked (makruh) because standing at Arafah is a worship specific to the specific place, so it is not worship elsewhere like the other rites. The action of Ibn Abbas may be that he went out for prayer for rain or the like, not to imitate the people of Arafat. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on two rulings from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The first ruling concerns the postponement of the 'Eid prayer. The matn states that the 'Eid prayer may be postponed due to an excuse up to three days. The commentary clarifies that this postponement applies to the 'Eid al-Adha prayer specifically, as it is connected to the time of sacrifice. If the prayer is postponed without a valid excuse, it is still valid but sinful (isaa'ah). The excuse here only removes the dislike (karahah), meaning that without an excuse, the postponement is makruh. In 'Eid al-Fitr, however, postponement without excuse is not allowed at all. The second ruling is on 'at-ta'rif' (gathering on 'Arafah day in other places imitating those at 'Arafat). The matn says 'it is not anything,' meaning it has no religious merit. The commentary explains that the word 'thing' here is negated in a general context, covering all levels of religious recommendation; thus ta'rif is not a worship act. There is a reported practice from Ibn Abbas and others, but the commentator prefers the view that it is makruh because the standing at 'Arafah is a specific rite confined to that location, analogous to other rites that are also place-specific. The action of Ibn Abbas is interpreted as possibly for other purposes like prayer for rain.

Key Terms
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah): 11th, 12th, and 13th.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on postponing the 'Eid al-Adha prayer with a valid excuse?
A) It is invalid.
B) It is permissible and not disliked.
C) It is permissible but disliked.
D) It is obligatory to postpone.

Key Takeaway
Postponing 'Eid al-Adha prayer is valid within three days; an excuse removes sin and dislike, while omission of excuse incurs sin but the prayer remains valid.

The Ruling on Ta'rif: Gathering Outside 'Arafah on 'Arafah Day
Commentary on the legal status of ta'rif

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on ta'rif and evaluate the evidence that leads to its dislike.

Core Idea
Ta'rif is not an act of worship and is disliked because it imitates a rite confined to 'Arafat.

This passage addresses a practice common in some regions: gathering on the day of 'Arafah in places other than 'Arafat, imitating the Hajj pilgrims. The commentator rules that this is 'not anything' and clarifies its legal status using qiyas and response to conflicting reports.

Guided Path
1
Define ta'rif
Ta'rif is a gathering on the day of 'Arafah in a place outside 'Arafat, imitating the pilgrims at 'Arafat.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi position is that ta'rif is not an act of worship and is makruh (disliked). The matn says 'not anything', negating any religious merit.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in some narrations do not dislike it, based on the practice of Ibn Abbas and others. However, the apparent (zahir) view is makruh.
The difference exists within the school, but the mufta bihi is makruh.
4
Analyze the proof (qiyas)
Standing at 'Arafah is a worship specific to that place. By analogy, other rites (like sa'i between Safa and Marwah) are also place-specific. Imitating a rite outside its place is not worship and is disliked.
5
Address the counter-evidence
The action of Ibn Abbas (gathering in Basra) is interpreted as possibly for prayer for rain, not for ta'rif. The practice in Bayt al-Maqdis and al-Azhar is also reinterpreted accordingly.

Takbir al-Tashriq: Ruling, Timing, Wording, and Conditions
Commentary detailing the rulings of takbir al-tashriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on takbir al-tashriq, identify its timing, number, and wording, and explain the conditions for obligation including the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib once after each obligatory fard prayer from Fajr of 'Arafah; the mufta bihi holds it obligatory on all who pray fard.

Takbir al-Tashriq is a distinctive dhikr during the days of 'Eid al-Adha. The matn calls it 'sunnah', but the commentary clarifies that here it means wajib. This passage outlines the ruling, the differing Companion views on timing, the number of takbirs, the preferred wording from the story of Ibrahim, and the conditions that make it obligatory. We will also examine the internal Hanafi difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his students on who must recite it.

Guided Path
1
Determine the ruling level
Understand that the matn's 'sunnah' is interpreted as wajib because of the command in the Quran and the practice of the Companions.
The correct view is that it is wajib.
2
Identify the start and end times
Compare the views of Ibn Mas'ud (eight prayers), 'Ali (twenty-three), and Ibn Umar (fourteen). The Hanafi school adopts Abu Hanifa's beginning (Fajr of 'Arafah) and the Sahibayn's ending ('Asr of last Tashriq) as the mufta bihi.
The fatwa follows the longer period.
3
Learn the number and wording
The takbir is said once after the salam. The prescribed wording includes tahlil and tahmid, based on the story of Ibrahim and Isma'il.
Adding more is fadl, not obligatory.
4
Analyze the conditions for obligation
Conditions: after fard 'ayn prayer, in congregation, in a city (misr). Imam Abu Hanifa restricts obligation to city residents in congregation; the Sahibayn extend it to all who perform fard, including travelers and women.
The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
According to the relied-upon position, takbir al-tashriq is wajib on every person who performs an obligatory prayer, whether male/female, resident/traveler, in congregation or alone.
The masbuq recites after completing his missed rak'ahs.

Source Text

وسن إلخ: [ أي تكبير التشريق، وقيل: يجب، وهو الأصح. (ط، ع)] سن ههنا بمعنى وجب، واختلف الصحابة في مبدئه فقال شبان الصحابة كابن عباس رضي الله عنهما، وابن عمر رضي الله عنه يبدأ بعد صلاة الظهر من أول أيام النحر، وبه أخذ الشافعي، وقال كبارهم كعمر رضي الله عنه، وعلي رضي الله عنه، وابن مسعود رضي الله عنه: يبدأ بعد صلاة الفجر من يوم عرفة، وهو مذهبنا، واختلفوا في مختمه أيضاً، فقال ابن مسعود: يقطع بعد صلاة العصر من يوم النحر، وهي ثمان صلوات، وبه أخذ الإمام أبو حنيفة ابتداء وانتهاء، وقال علي: يقطع بعد صلاة العصر من آخر أيام التشريق وهي: ثلاثة وعشرون صلاة، وبه أخذ الإمامان ابتداء وانتهاء، وقال ابن عمر رضي الله عنه: يقطع بعد صلاة الفجر من آخر أيام التشريق، وهي أربع عشرة صلاة، وأخذ به الشافعي ابتداء وانتهاء. (فتح)

كتاب الصلاة
باب صلاة العيدين
بعد فجر عرفة إلى ثمان مرّةً "الله أكبر" إلى آخره بشرط إقامة ومصر ومكتوبة
أي التاسع من ذي الحجة
وجماعة مستحبّةٍ، وبالاقتداء يجب على المرأة والمسافر. أي بالمقيم أي التكبير
فلا تجب على المنفرد
متعلق بقوله سن فلا تجب على مسافر
بعد فجر عرفة: أي ابتداؤه بعد صلاة فجر عرفة، التاسع من ذي الحجة ويأتي بالتكبير بلا تراخ حتى لو خرج من المسجد، أو جاوز الصفوف في الصحراء، أو أتى بما يمنع البناء لا يأتي به، ولو سبقه حدث بعد السلام فإن شاء توضأ وكبر أو أتى على غير طهارة. وقوله : "مرة" وقال الشافعي: يقول: الله أكبر ثلاث مرات، أو خمس مرات، أو سبع مرات، ولا يزاد عليه؛ لأن المنصوص عليه هو التكبير ، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلِتُكَبِّرُوا اللَّهَ عَلَى مَا هَدَاكُمْ (البقرة: ١٨٥) والتهليل والتحميد ليستا بتكبير حقيقة. ولنا: أن المأثور عن الخليل عليه السلام هكذا، فإنه إذا أضجع إسماعيل للذبح أمر الله تعالى جبريل عليه السلام حتى يذهب إليه بالفداء، فلما رأى جبريل أنه أضجعه للذبح قال: الله أكبر الله أكبر كي لا يعجل بالذبح، فلما سمع إبراهيم عليه السلام صوت جبريل وقع عنده أنه يأتيه بالبشارة فقال: لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر، فلما سمع إسماعيل عليه السلام صوتهما وقع عنده أنه فدي فقال: الله أكبر ولله الحمد. (مستخلص، فتح)
ثمان ثمان صلوات عند الإمام أي يكون آخره صلاة العصر من يوم النحر، وهو قول ابن مسعود. [رمز الحقائق: ١٠٣/١] مرةً أي مرة واحدة، فإن زاد عليها يكون فضلاً. [رمز الحقائق: ١٠٣/١]
الله أكبر: أي من قول: الله أكبر الله أكبر لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر الله أكبر ولله الحمد. (ع)
ومصر: فلا تجب على أهل القرى. (ع) و مكتوبة [ أي صلاة فرض فلا تجب على المتنفل(ع)] أي مفروضة على الأعيان، فعم الجمعة، وخرج غير المفروضة ولو وتراً، وكذا صلاة الجنازة؛ لأنها ليست فرضاً على الأعيان وكذا صلاة العيد، لكن البلخيون يكبرون عقب صلاة العيد؛ لأنها تؤدى بجماعة فأشبهت الجمعة. (فتح) جماعة مستحبة [ احتراز عن جماعة النساء فإن المرأة لا يجب عليها التكبير وإن صلت مع الجماعة؛ لأن جماعتهن مكروهة. (ع)] فيجب على الرجال المقيمين في الأمصار عقب المكتوبات بالجماعة، فلا يجب على القروي والمنفرد والمسافر وإن صلى بجماعة، هذا عند الإمام، وقالا : هو على كل من صلى المكتوبة مصرياً، أو قرويا، أو مسافراً، أو منفرداً، أو امرأة؛ لأنه شرع تبعاً للمكتوبة، فيؤديه كل من يؤديها، والفتوى على قولهما. (فتح) على المرأة والمسافر المرأة تخافت بالتكبير ؛ لأن صوتها عورة، بخلاف المسافر، وكذا يجب على المسبوق؛ لأنه مقتدٍ بتحريمة، لكن لا يكبر مع الإمام بل بعد قضاء مافاته. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥٤٦/١] وكذا يجب على المؤتم أن يأتي بتكبير التشريق وإن تركه إمامه لأدائه بعد الصلاة واللاحق كالمسبوق. (فتح)
والمسافر: للتبعية غير أن المرأة لا ترفع صوتها بخلاف المسافر ؛ لأن الجهر فيه سنة. (ع)
And 'sunnah' etc.: [It means the takbir of tashriq, and it is said it is obligatory, and that is the correct view. (T, A)] 'Sunnah' here means obligatory. The Companions differed on its beginning: the younger Companions like Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar said it begins after the Zuhr prayer of the first day of Nahr, and al-Shafi'i adopted this. The senior Companions like 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud said it begins after the Fajr prayer of the day of Arafah, and that is our madhhab. They also differed on its end: Ibn Mas'ud said it ends after the Asr prayer of the day of Nahr, making eight prayers; Imam Abu Hanifa adopted this for both beginning and end. 'Ali said it ends after the Asr prayer of the last day of Tashriq, making twenty-three prayers; the two Imams (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) adopted this for both beginning and end. Ibn Umar said it ends after the Fajr prayer of the last day of Tashriq, making fourteen prayers; al-Shafi'i adopted this for both beginning and end. (Fath)

Book of Prayer. Chapter of the Two 'Eid Prayers. After Fajr of Arafah to eight (prayers) once: 'Allahu Akbar' etc. with the condition of residence, city, and obligatory prayer, and congregation is recommended, and by following (the imam) it is obligatory upon the woman and the traveler. I.e., upon the resident, i.e., the takbir. So it is not obligatory upon the one praying alone. Connected to his statement 'sunnah' so it is not obligatory upon a traveler. 'After Fajr of Arafah': i.e., its start is after the Fajr prayer of Arafah, the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. He performs the takbir without delay, such that if he leaves the mosque, or passes the rows in the desert, or does something that prevents connection, he does not perform it. If something (a hadath) precedes him after the salam, if he wishes he can perform wudu and say takbir, or he may do it without purification. His statement 'once': al-Shafi'i said: he says Allahu Akbar three times, or five times, or seven times, and no more; because what is prescribed is the takbir, Allah said: 'And that you magnify Allah for having guided you' (2:185) and the tahlil and tahmid are not really takbir. Our proof: the transmitted from al-Khalil (Abraham) peace be upon him is thus: when he laid Isma'il down for sacrifice, Allah commanded Jibril to go to him with the ransom. When Jibril saw that he had laid him down for sacrifice, he said: Allahu Akbar Allahu Akbar so that he would not hasten with the sacrifice. When Ibrahim heard Jibril's voice, he thought it came with good news and said: La ilaha illa Allah wallahu Akbar. When Isma'il heard their voices, he thought that he was ransomed and said: Allahu Akbar wa lillahi al-hamd. (Mustakhlas, Fath) 'Eight': eight prayers according to Imam Abu Hanifa, i.e., its end is the Asr prayer of the day of Nahr, and this is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/103] 'Once': i.e., once; if he adds to it, it is a virtue. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/103] 'Allahu Akbar': i.e., from the saying: Allahu Akbar Allahu Akbar la ilaha illa Allah wallahu Akbar Allahu Akbar wa lillahi al-hamd. (A) 'And a city (misr)': so it is not obligatory upon the villagers. (A) 'And an obligatory prayer (maktubah)': i.e., a fard prayer, so it is not obligatory upon one praying a supererogatory prayer. (A) I.e., it is fard 'ayn (individual obligation), so it includes Friday, and excludes non-obligatory prayers even if witr, and likewise the funeral prayer because it is not fard 'ayn, and likewise the 'Eid prayer. But the Balkh scholars say takbir after 'Eid prayer because it is performed with congregation so it resembles Friday. (Fath) 'Congregation is recommended': [a precaution against the congregation of women, for a woman is not obligated to say takbir even if she prays with the congregation because her congregation is disliked. (A)] So it is obligatory upon resident men in cities after the obligatory prayers with congregation. It is not obligatory upon the villager, the one praying alone, and the traveler even if he prays with congregation. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is upon everyone who performs the obligatory prayer, whether city dweller, villager, traveler, alone, or woman, because it is prescribed following the obligatory prayer, so everyone who performs it should perform the takbir. The fatwa is according to their view. (Fath) 'Upon the woman and the traveler': the woman says it quietly because her voice is 'awrah, unlike the traveler. Likewise it is obligatory upon the masbuq (latecomer) because he is a follower in his beginning, but he does not say takbir with the imam but rather after completing what he missed. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/546] Likewise it is obligatory upon the mu'tam (follower) to perform the takbir of tashriq even if his imam leaves it, because he performs it after the prayer, and the lahiq is like the masbuq. (Fath) 'And the traveler': for following (the obligation), except that the woman does not raise her voice unlike the traveler, because raising the voice is Sunnah. (A)
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on takbir al-tashriq. It begins by noting that the word 'sunnah' in the matn actually means wajib (obligatory), and this is the correct view. It then discusses the different opinions of the Companions regarding the start and end times of this takbir. The Hanafi position, based on Ibn Mas'ud, is that it starts from Fajr of the day of 'Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) and ends after 'Asr of the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), which covers eight obligatory prayers (Fajr, Zuhr, 'Asr of 'Arafah, then Maghrib, Isha, Fajr, Zuhr, 'Asr of Nahr). This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. His two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, adopt the view of 'Ali that it ends after 'Asr of the last day of Tashriq (13th Dhul Hijjah), totaling 23 prayers. The Shafi'i school follows a different calculation. The text then proceeds to explain the conditions and manner of the takbir. It is performed after obligatory prayers (fard 'ayn) with congregation, and the takbir is said once (one time) after the salam. The specific wording includes tahlil and tahmid as well, as narrated from the story of Prophet Ibrahim. There is a condition of being a resident in a city (misr); villagers are not obligated according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but his students extend it to all who perform the obligatory prayer, and the fatwa is on their view. Women are obligated but recite quietly. A latecomer (masbuq) performs it after completing his missed prayers, and a follower (mu'tam) must recite it even if the imam neglects it. The proof for the obligation is the verse 'And that you magnify Allah for having guided you' (al-Baqarah 2:185) and the story of Ibrahim's sacrifice as transmitted.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbir al-tashriq): The extra takbirs recited after obligatory prayers from Fajr of 'Arafah to 'Asr of the last day of Tashriq.
سن (sunna): In this context, it is interpreted as wajib (obligatory), not merely recommended.
مصر (misr): A city (town) with a population large enough to have congregational prayers established. The takbir is obligatory only in such places according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late (after the imam has started) and misses some rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi), who must perform takbir al-tashriq?
A) Only residents of cities praying in congregation
B) Everyone who performs an obligatory prayer, including travelers and women
C) Only men in cities
D) Only the imam of a mosque

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-tashriq is a wajib act recited once after each fard prayer from Fajr of 'Arafah to 'Asr of the last day of Tashriq, obligatory upon all who perform fard prayers according to the mufta bihi.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
7 min
The Ruling and Conditions of Takbir al-Tashriq
Ruling on Takbir al-Tashriq with conditions, proofs, and intra-madhhab differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Takbir al-Tashriq in the Hanafi school, identify its conditions and times, and explain the intra-madhhab difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is sunnah muakkadah but the fatwa makes it effectively wajib on all who pray the obligatory prayer.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary explains the ruling of Takbir al-Tashriq, its prescribed time from Fajr of Arafah, the conditions of residence and congregation, and the differing views within the school. By working through the text, you will understand how the Hanafi school balances textual evidence from the Qur'an and the practice of Ibrahim with practical conditions of obligation, and how the fatwa settles on the more inclusive view of the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is Takbir al-Tashriq? What is its hukm according to the matn? The base text says it is sunnah, but the commentary explains it is sunnah muakkadah and the Sahibayn consider it wajib. Note the difference between sunnah and wajib in Hanafi usul.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah, but the fatwa follows the Sahibayn's view, making it effectively necessary.
2
Locate the temporal scope
When does Takbir al-Tashriq begin and end? The text specifies after Fajr of Arafah (9th of Dhul Hijjah) to after Asr of the 13th (eight prayers according to Imam Abu Hanifa). Identify the eight prayers: Fajr, Zuhr, Asr of Arafah, and the five prayers of the first day of Eid plus Fajr, Zuhr, Asr of the 13th.
Some scholars count only five prayers (the five days) but Imam Abu Hanifa says eight.
3
Identify the conditions for obligation
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, conditions for obligation are: being a resident of a city (miṣr), praying an obligatory prayer (fard), and praying in congregation. Women and travelers are not required, and one praying alone is not required. The Sahibayn remove all these conditions and make it obligatory on everyone who prays the fard prayer.
The condition of 'city' is defined as a place where Jumu'ah is held.
4
Examine the proof (dalil)
What is the Hanafi proof? The Qur'anic verse (2:185) commands takbir, and the story of Ibrahim and Isma'il provides the specific wording and shows the inclusion of tahlil and tahmid. Contrast with the Shafi'i view that restricts to 'Allahu Akbar' only.
The story is transmitted (mursal?) but accepted by the Hanafis as a valid precedent.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which view is the operative ruling for fatwa? The text explicitly says 'wal-fatwa 'ala qawlihima' (the fatwa is on their saying), meaning the Sahibayn's view that it is required for all who pray the fard prayer, regardless of residence or travel.
This makes the practice virtually wajib, though the base text still classifies it as sunnah.

كتاب الصلاة باب صلاة العيدين بعد فجر عرفة إلى ثمان مرّةً "الله أكبر" إلى آخره بشرط إقامة ومصر ومكتوبة أي التاسع من ذي الحجة وجماعة مستحبّةٍ، وبالاقتداء يجب على المرأة والمسافر. أي بالمقيم أي التكبير فلا تجب على المنفرد متعلق بقوله سن فلا تجب على مسافر بعد فجر عرفة: أي ابتداؤه بعد صلاة فجر عرفة، التاسع من ذي الحجة ويأتي بالتكبير بلا تراخ حتى لو خرج من المسجد، أو جاوز الصفوف في الصحراء، أو أتى بما يمنع البناء لا يأتي به، ولو سبقه حدث بعد السلام فإن شاء توضأ وكبر أو أتى على غير طهارة. وقوله : "مرة" وقال الشافعي: يقول: الله أكبر ثلاث مرات، أو خمس مرات، أو سبع مرات، ولا يزاد عليه؛ لأن المنصوص عليه هو التكبير ، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلِتُكَبِّرُوا اللَّهَ عَلَى مَا هَدَاكُمْ (البقرة: ۱۸۵) والتهليل والتحميد ليستا بتكبير حقيقة. ولنا: أن المأثور عن الخليل عليه هكذا، فإنه إذا أضحع إسماعيل للذبح أمر الله تعالى جبريل عليه حتى يذهب إليه بالفداء، فلما رأى جبريل أنه أضحعه للذبح قال: الله أكبر الله أكبر كي لا يعجل بالذبح، فلما سمع إبراهيم علي صوت جبريل وقع عنده أنه يأتيه بالبشارة فقال: لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر، فلما سمع إسماعيل عليه صوتهما وقع عنده أنه فدي فقال: الله أكبر ولله الحمد. (مستخلص، فتح) ثمان ثمان صلوات عند الإمام أي يكون آخره صلاة العصر من يوم النحر، وهو قول ابن مسعود. [رمز الحقائق: ١٠٣/١] مرةً أي مرة واحدة، فإن زاد عليها يكون فضلاً. [رمز الحقائق: ١٠٣/١] الله أكبر: أي من قول: الله أكبر الله أكبر لا إله إلا الله والله أكبر الله أكبر ولله الحمد. (ع) ومصر: فلا تجب على أهل القرى. (ع) و مكتوبة [ أي صلاة فرض فلا تجب على المتنفل(ع)] أي مفروضة على الأعيان، فعم الجمعة، وخرج غير المفروضة ولو وتراً، وكذا صلاة الجنازة؛ لأنها ليست فرضاً على الأعيان وكذا صلاة العيد، لكن البلخيون يكبرون عقب صلاة العيد؛ لأنها تؤدى بجماعة فأشبهت الجمعة. (فتح) جماعة مستحبة [ احتراز عن جماعة النساء فإن المرأة لا يجب عليها التكبير وإن صلت مع الجماعة؛ لأن جماعتهن مكروهة. (ع)] فيجب على الرجال المقيمين في الأمصار عقب المكتوبات بالجماعة، فلا يجب على القروي والمنفرد والمسافر وإن صلى بجماعة، هذا عند الإمام، وقالا : هو على كل من صلى المكتوبة مصرياً، أو قرويا، أو مسافراً، أو منفرداً، أو امرأة؛ لأنه شرع تبعاً للمكتوبة، فيؤديه كل من يؤديها، والفتوى على قولهما. (فتح) على المرأة والمسافر المرأة تخافت بالتكبير ؛ لأن صوتها عورة، بخلاف المسافر، وكذا يجب على المسبوق؛ لأنه مقتد تحريمة، لكن لا يكبر مع الإمام بل بعد قضاء مافاته. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥٤٦/١] وكذا يجب على المؤتم أن يأتي بتكبير التشريق وإن تركه إمامه لأدائه بعد الصلاة واللاحق كالمسبوق. (فتح) : والمسافر: للتبعية غير أن المرأة لا ترفع صوتها بخلاف المسافر ; لأن الجهر فيه سنة. (ع)
The Book of Prayer, Chapter on the Prayer of the Two Eids: After Fajr of Arafah until eight times, one time 'Allahu Akbar' to its end, with the condition of residence, city, and obligatory prayer, and congregation is recommended, and by following (the imam) it becomes obligatory upon the woman and the traveler. That is, the takbir is upon the resident, so it is not obligatory upon the one praying alone, attached to his saying: sunnah, so it is not obligatory upon a traveler. After Fajr of Arafah: i.e., its beginning is after the Fajr prayer of Arafah, the ninth of Dhul Hijjah, and he performs the takbir without delay, such that if he leaves the mosque, or passes the rows in the desert, or does something that prevents building upon the prayer, he does not perform it. And if an event (breaking wudu) overtakes him after the salam, then if he wishes he may perform wudu and say takbir, or he may say it without purification. And his saying: 'one time': Al-Shafi'i said: he says Allahu Akbar three times, or five times, or seven times, and no more; because what is specified is the takbir, Allah said: 'And that you magnify Allah for that He has guided you (2:185).' And tahlil and tahmid are not takbir in reality. And for us: that which is transmitted from al-Khalil (Ibrahim) is like this: when he laid down Isma'il for sacrifice, Allah commanded Jibril to go to him with the ransom. When Jibril saw that he had laid him down for sacrifice, he said: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, so that he would not hasten the sacrifice. When Ibrahim heard Jibril's voice, he thought he had brought good news, so he said: La ilaha illa Allah, Allahu Akbar. When Isma'il heard both their voices, he thought he had been ransomed, so he said: Allahu Akbar wa lillahi al-hamd. (Mukhtasar, Fath) Eight prayers according to Imam (Abu Hanifa): i.e., its end is the Asr prayer of the Day of Nahr, which is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 103/1] One time: i.e., one single time, and if he adds to it, it is virtuous. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 103/1] Allahu Akbar: i.e., from the saying: Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illa Allah, wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar wa lillahi al-hamd. (Ayni) And city: so it is not obligatory upon the people of villages. (Ayni) And obligatory prayer [i.e., a fard prayer, so it is not obligatory upon one performing supererogatory prayer (Ayni)] i.e., obligatory upon individuals, so it includes Jumu'ah, and excludes non-obligatory prayers even if witr, and likewise the funeral prayer because it is not a personal obligation, and likewise the Eid prayer, but the Balkh scholars say takbir after Eid prayer because it is performed with congregation so it resembles Jumu'ah. (Fath) Recommended congregation [a precaution against women's congregation, for the woman is not required to say takbir even if she prays with the congregation, because their congregation is disliked (Ayni)] So it is obligatory upon resident men in cities after obligatory prayers with congregation, so it is not obligatory upon the villager, the individual, and the traveler even if he prays with congregation. This is according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is upon everyone who prays the obligatory prayer, whether city dweller, villager, traveler, individual, or woman, because it is prescribed as a follow-up to the obligatory prayer, so everyone who performs it should perform it. And the fatwa is upon their saying. (Fath) Upon the woman and the traveler: the woman lowers her voice in takbir because her voice is awrah, contrary to the traveler. And likewise it is obligatory upon the masbuq (latecomer) because he is a follower from the beginning, but he does not say takbir with the imam, rather after making up what he missed. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 546/1] And likewise it is obligatory upon the follower to perform the takbir of tashriq even if his imam leaves it, because it is performed after the prayer, and the lahiq (one who joins late) is like the masbuq. (Fath) And the traveler: due to follow-up, except that the woman does not raise her voice unlike the traveler, because raising the voice is sunnah therein. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Qur'an and the practice of the Prophet Ibrahim (AS) regarding the takbir of tashriq. The author, commenting on the matn, explains that the takbir begins after Fajr of the ninth of Dhul Hijjah (Arafah) and continues until after Asr of the thirteenth (the Day of Nahr according to Abu Hanifa, totaling eight prayers: Fajr, Zuhr, Asr of Arafah, and the five prayers of the first day of Eid plus Fajr, Zuhr, Asr of the 13th). The Hanafi school holds that it is said once, though adding more is virtuous. It is a sunnah (not wajib) for those who are resident in a city, praying an obligatory prayer in congregation. The text details that it is not required for individuals, travelers, villagers, or women (though women must say it quietly). There is an intra-madhhab difference: Imam Abu Hanifa restricts it to residents in cities praying in congregation, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) make it obligatory on all who pray the obligatory prayer, regardless of status. The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view. The text also refutes Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that the takbir should be said three, five, or seven times and restricts it to only the takbir (not tahlil or tahmid). The Hanafi proof includes the Qur'anic verse commanding takbir after guidance (2:185) and the transmitted story of Ibrahim and Isma'il, which includes the full wording: 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illa Allah, wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar wa lillahi al-hamd.' The text also addresses the case of a latecomer (masbuq) and a follower whose imam omits the takbir, clarifying that they must still perform it after completing their prayer.

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (takbīr al-tashrīq): The prescribed takbirs recited after the obligatory prayers from Fajr of Arafah to Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
فجر عرفة (fajr 'arafah): The dawn prayer on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, the start of the takbir al-tashriq period.
مصر (miṣr): A large town or city where Jumu'ah and congregational prayers are established, as opposed to a small village.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the time for takbir al-tashriq begin?
A) After Fajr of the first day of Dhul Hijjah
B) After Fajr of the day of Arafah (9th of Dhul Hijjah)
C) After the Eid prayer on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah
D) After Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
Takbir al-Tashriq is a significant practice from Fajr of Arafah to Asr of the 13th, said once with the full wording; the fatwa makes it effectively wajib on all who pray the fard prayer.

Ruling on the Eclipse Prayer (Ṣalāt al-Kusūf)
Explaining the legitimacy, manner, and rulings of the eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the eclipse prayer (sunnah muakkadah), explain the method (two rak'ahs with one ruku' each, quiet recitation, no adhan/iqamah, no khutbah), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding multiple ruku'.

Core Idea
The eclipse prayer is sunnah muakkadah with one ruku' per rak'ah, unlike the Shafi'i two ruku' view.

The eclipse prayer is a confirmed sunnah that the Prophet ﷺ established when the sun or moon eclipses. In this passage from Kanz al-Daqā’iq with its sharḥ, the author presents the legitimacy, manner, and key rulings, including a well-known inter-madhhab dispute over the number of bowings. This lesson will walk you through the Hanafi position, its proof, and the rebuttal to the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
From the text, note that the eclipse prayer is ruled as sunnah (emphasized sunnah), though some scholars consider it wajib. The act is a two-rak'ah prayer performed during an eclipse, like the nafil prayer.
The text begins with 'He prays two rak'ahs like the nafil' and later states 'This prayer is sunnah; it is said to be wajib.'
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The author cites both Qur'an (17:59) and Sunnah (Bukhari hadith) to establish legitimacy. The primary proof for the manner is the hadith of Qabisa and many Companions that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs with one ruku' each, lengthening the recitation.
The text says: 'And for us (Hanafis) is what Qabisa narrated... and a group of Companions narrated two rak'ahs.'
3
Understand the Shafi'i counter-dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on hadith from 'A'isha and Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet prayed with four ruku' (two per rak'ah) and four prostrations.
The text mentions: 'Al-Shafi'i went to that they pray with two bowings... based on what 'A'isha and Ibn 'Abbas narrated.'
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the multiple-ruku' narrations are contradictory (varying numbers from three to six) and al-Shafi'i himself did not accept all of them. The Hanafi view conforms to the general principle (asl) of one ruku' per rak'ah and is narrated by a larger group of Companions.
The text says: 'the narrations with multiple ruku' are contradictory... and our answer to Shafi'i is the same as his answer to those who report more than two ruku'.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis perform the eclipse prayer like a regular nafil with one ruku' per rak'ah; Shafi'is perform it with two ruku' per rak'ah. Additionally, Hanafis do not give a sermon, while Shafi'is do.
The text mentions the absence of khutbah by consensus of Hanafis, and that Shafi'i recommends it.

Source Text

باب صلاة الكسوف أي في بيان أحكامها س م ف يصلي ركعتين كالنفل إمام الجمعة بلا جهر وخطبة، بالرفع فاعل يصلي في القراءة باب صلاة الكسوف من إضافة الحكم إلى سببه. والمناسبة بين البابين أنهما يؤديان بالجماعة، وقدم العيد لوجوبه على الأصح. وصلاة الكسوف تثبت شرعيتها بالكتاب والسنة، أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا نُرْسِلُ بِالْآيَاتِ إِلَّا تَحْوِيفا) (الإسراء: ٥٩) والكسوف آية من آيات الله المخوفة، وأما السنة ففي البخاري: "أن الشمس والقمر لا ينكسفان لموت أحد من الناس ولكنهما آيتان من آيات الله، فإذا رأيتموهما فصلوا"، وفي رواية: "فادعوا". (فتح) الكسوف للشمس، والخسوف للقمر، وقد يستعمل الكسوف فيهما، وقيل: إذا ذهب بعضها فهو الكسوف، وإذا ذهب كلها فهو الخسوف. هي ركعتين بيان لأقل مقدارها وإن شاء صلى أربعا، أو أكثر، كل ركعتين بتسليمتين، أو كل أربع، وقوله: كالنفل: أي في عدم الأذان والإقامة، وعدم الجواز في الأوقات المكروهة، وفي إطالة القيام بالقراءة، والأدعية التي من خصائص النفل؛ لأن قيامه عليه في الأولى كان بقدر البقرة، وفي الثانية بقدر آل عمران، والمسنون استيعاب الوقت بالصلاة والدعاء، وقيل: يقرأ فيهما ما أحب كالصلاة المكتوبة، وذهب الشافعي إلى أنهما يصليان بركوعين؛ لما روت عائشة ما وابن عباس لما أنه عليه صلى صلاة كسوف الشمس ركعتين بأربع ركوعات وأربع سجدات ولنا ما روى قبيصة أنه عليه صلى ركعتين، فأطال فيهما القراءة، وقد روى الركعتين جماعة من الصحابة منهم ابن عمر، وسمرة بن جندب، وأبو بكر، ونعمان بن بشير، والأخذ بها أولى؛ لموافقة الأصول، ولا حجة له فيما رواه؛ لأنه ثبت أن مذهبهما بخلاف ذلك؛ ولأنه روي عنه عليه أنه صلى ثلاث ركوعات في كل ركعة، وأربع ركوعات، وخمس ركوعات وست ،رکوعات، ولم يأخذ الشافعي بما زاد على ركوعين، فكل جواب له عن الزيادة على ركوعين فهو جوابنا عما زاد على ركوع واحد. (فتح) كالنفل أي بلا أذان وإقامة وبركوع واحد في الركعة الواحدة كهيئة النفل (ط، ع) إمام الجمعة: بيان للمستحب، ويستحب في كسوف الشمس ثلاثة أشياء: الإمام ،والوقت والموضع الذي تصلى فيه صلاة العيد أو المسجد الجامع، ولو صلوا في موضع آخر أجزأهم والأول أفضل، ولو صلوا وحداناً في منازلهم جاز. (فتح) بلا جهر وخطبة وقال أبو يوسف: يجهر، وأما عدم الخطبة فبإجماع أصحابنا؛ لأنه لم ينقل فيه أثر، وخطبته عليها لما كسفت الشمس يوم موت سيدنا إبراهيم ليست إلا للرد على من توهم أنها كسفت لموته، وهذه الصلاة سنة، وقيل: واجبة لأمره عليها "إذا رأيتم شيئا من هذه الآيات فافزعوا إلى الصلاة، ويقرأ فيها ما أحب، والأفضل أن يطول القراءة فيها. (فتح) وخطبة أي بلا خطبة؛ لأنها لم تنقل وعن الشافعي: يخطب كالجمعة. (ط)
Chapter on the Eclipse Prayer: i.e., explaining its rulings. He prays two rak'ahs like the nafil, with the imam of Jumu'ah, without audible recitation and without a sermon, with the subject of 'prays' raised in reading. Chapter on the Eclipse Prayer: it is adding the ruling to its cause. The suitability between the two chapters (Eid and eclipse) is that both are performed with congregation, and Eid is given precedence due to its being obligatory according to the correct view. The legitimacy of the eclipse prayer is established by the Book and Sunnah. As for the Book, Allah's saying: 'And We do not send signs except as a warning' (17:59). The eclipse is one of the fearful signs of Allah. As for the Sunnah, in al-Bukhari: 'The sun and the moon are not eclipsed for the death of anyone, but they are two signs of Allah; when you see them, pray.' And in another narration: 'Supplicate.' (Fath) Kusuf is for the sun, and khusuf for the moon, though kusuf may be used for both. It is said: if only part disappears, it is kusuf; if all disappears, it is khusuf. It is two rak'ahs: a statement of its minimum amount; if he wishes, he may pray four or more, every two rak'ahs with one taslim, or every four. His saying: 'like the nafil' means in the absence of adhan and iqamah, and in not being permissible in disliked times, and in lengthening the standing in recitation, and the supplications that are specific to nafil, because the Prophet's (PBUH) standing in the first (rak'ah) was like (the recitation of) Surat al-Baqara, and in the second like Surat Al 'Imran. The sunnah is to fill the time with prayer and supplication. It is said that one recites whatever he likes as in the obligatory prayer. Al-Shafi'i went to that they pray with two bowings (in each rak'ah) based on what 'A'isha and Ibn 'Abbas narrated that the Prophet (PBUH) prayed the solar eclipse prayer two rak'ahs with four bowings and four prostrations. And for us (Hanafis) is what Qabisa narrated: that the Prophet (PBUH) prayed two rak'ahs and lengthened the recitation. And a group of Companions narrated two rak'ahs, including Ibn 'Umar, Samura ibn Jundub, Abu Bakr, and Nu'man ibn Bashir. Adopting this is better because it conforms to the principles. And he (al-Shafi'i) has no proof in what he narrated because it is established that the two narrations are contradictory; also because it is narrated that the Prophet (PBUH) prayed with three, four, five, and six bowings in each rak'ah, and al-Shafi'i did not adopt what exceeds two bowings, so every answer he has for the increase above two bowings is our answer for what exceeds one bowing. (Fath) Like nafil: i.e., without adhan and iqamah, and with one bowing in each rak'ah like the manner of nafil (Tahawi, Ayni). Imam of Jumu'ah: a statement of what is recommended. Three things are recommended for solar eclipse: the imam, the time, and the place where the Eid prayer is performed or the central mosque. If they pray in another place, it suffices, but the first is better. If they pray individually in their homes, it is permissible. (Fath) Without audible recitation and without sermon: Abu Yusuf said: he recites audibly. As for the absence of a sermon, it is by consensus of our companions because no tradition has been transmitted. And his (the Prophet's) sermon when the sun was eclipsed on the day of the death of our master Ibrahim was only to refute those who thought it eclipsed for his death. This prayer is sunnah; it is said to be wajib due to his command: 'When you see any of these signs, hasten to prayer.' And one recites whatever he likes, though it is best to lengthen the recitation. (Fath) And sermon: i.e., without a sermon because it has not been transmitted. And al-Shafi'i says: he delivers a sermon like Jumu'ah. (Tahawi)
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof detailing the eclipse prayer. The chapter begins by explaining that the legitimacy of the prayer comes from the Qur'an (17:59, where Allah sends signs as warnings) and from authentic hadith in Bukhari: the Prophet (PBUH) said that the sun and moon are not eclipsed for anyone's death but are signs of Allah, so when you see them, pray. The commentary distinguishes between kusuf (solar) and khusuf (lunar), though sometimes both are called kusuf. The minimum prayer is two rak'ahs, each with one ruku' (bowing), like a nafil prayer. It is prayed without adhan or iqamah, and it is not performed during disliked times. The recitation should be lengthy: the Prophet (PBUH) recited Surah al-Baqara in the first rak'ah and Surah Al 'Imran in the second. The text then presents a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that each rak'ah has two ruku's based on hadith from 'A'isha and Ibn 'Abbas. The Hanafi response is that the hadith with one ruku' is narrated by Qabisa and many Companions, and that the multiple ruku' narrations are contradictory; moreover, al-Shafi'i himself did not adopt all the narrations that mention more than two ruku's. The Hanafi position conforms to the general pattern of prayer (one ruku' per rak'ah) and is therefore preferred. The text also notes that it is recommended to pray in congregation with an imam, and that the imam should be the regular Jumu'ah imam. The prayer is recited quietly; Abu Yusuf held that it should be audible, but the prevailing view is quiet recitation. There is no khutbah (sermon) because no such practice is transmitted, although the Prophet (PBUH) gave a sermon once to correct a misconception. The prayer itself is sunnah, though some say it is wajib due to the command 'hasten to prayer'. The best is to fill the duration of the eclipse with prayer and supplication.

Key Terms
صلاة الكسوف (ṣalāt al-kusūf): The prayer performed during a solar eclipse, consisting of two rak'ahs like nafl, without adhan or iqamah.
كسوف (kusūf): Eclipse of the sun; sometimes used for the moon as well, but specifically for solar events.
خسوف (khusūf): Eclipse of the moon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many bowings (ruku') are performed in each rak'ah of the eclipse prayer?
A) Two bowings
B) One bowing
C) Four bowings
D) No bowings, only prostrations

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school performs the eclipse prayer as a sunnah muakkadah with one ruku' per rak'ah, quiet recitation, and no sermon, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and many Companions.

Lunar Eclipse Prayer and Prayer for Calamities in the Hanafi School
Rulings for lunar eclipse and other calamities with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for lunar eclipse prayer, explain why it is performed individually, and distinguish it from solar eclipse prayer.

Core Idea
Lunar eclipse prayer is performed individually because the Prophet never led it in congregation, and gathering at night is impractical and may cause fitna.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq continues the chapter on eclipse prayer, detailing the post-prayer supplication for solar eclipse and extending the rulings to lunar eclipse and other fearful natural events. The Hanafi school differentiates between the two types of eclipses, assigning a higher status to the solar eclipse prayer and treating lunar eclipse and other calamities as merely good deeds (hasanah) without congregation. Understanding the evidence and rationale behind this distinction is crucial for proper practice and for appreciating the Hanafi approach to textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling for solar eclipse
The text states that after the solar eclipse prayer, the imam leads supplication facing the qibla until the sun clears. This supplication is Sunnah. The prayer itself is also Sunnah (or wajib according to some).
The text mentions 'sunnah' for the du'a and explicitly says 'صلاة الكسوف سنة' (solar eclipse prayer is Sunnah).
2
Identify the ruling for lunar eclipse and other calamities
The passage says 'صلاة الخسوف حسنة' (lunar eclipse prayer is good) and similarly for other fearful events like darkness, strong wind, earthquakes, etc. The prayer is performed individually (فرادى), not in congregation.
The ruling level is 'hasanah' (good deed), lower than Sunnah.
3
Analyze the dalil for the solar eclipse ruling
The text cites the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: 'The sun and moon are two signs of Allah; when you see them, supplicate and pray until they clear.' This command (أمر) indicates Sunnah (in Hanafi usul, a command from the Prophet indicates obligation unless there is a qarina, but here it is interpreted as Sunnah).
The hadith supports spending the entire eclipse time in prayer and supplication.
4
Analyze the dalil for the lunar eclipse ruling
The Hanafi school relies on the absence of any report that the Prophet led congregational prayer for a lunar eclipse, despite lunar eclipses occurring during his time. This is combined with the practical difficulty and potential fitna of gathering at night.
The text says: 'لم ينقل أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم جمع الناس له' – it was not transmitted that he gathered people for it.
5
Examine the Shafi'i counter-argument and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i uses the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prayed in congregation for a lunar eclipse. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid) on a matter that should be widely known, so it is not accepted as binding.
This is a classic example of the Hanafi principle that khabar wahid cannot override general practice (مشهور).

Source Text

Book of Prayer. Chapter on Eclipse Prayer. Then he supplicates until the sun clears, otherwise they pray individually like for the lunar eclipse, and darkness, and wind, and fear. (i.e. the imam) (i.e. clears) (i.e. the people) (i.e. strong wind generally) (i.e. clears) (i.e. the people) (i.e. strong during the day). Then he supplicates: i.e. after the prayer, the imam supplicates facing the qibla, or standing facing the people, and the people say 'amen'. This is best. If he leans on a staff, it is good. He does not ascend the pulpit for supplication. Supplication after the prayer is Sunnah. His saying: 'until the sun clears' is due to the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah that the Prophet said: 'The sun and moon are two signs of Allah; they are not eclipsed for anyone's death or life; when you see them, supplicate to Allah and pray until they clear.' This indicates spending the entire time in both, and that is the Sunnah. The meaning of clearing is complete clearing, not its beginning. If it does not clear and sets, he also abandons supplication. (Fath) 'Otherwise' refers to if the Friday imam is not present. 'Individually' means they pray individually two rak'ahs or four. ('Ayn) 'Like the lunar eclipse' means just as one prays in the lunar eclipse individually, because it was eclipsed in his time many times and it was not reported that he led the people for it, and because a large gathering at night after they have slept is not possible and is a cause of fitna, so it is not prescribed; rather each person supplicates for himself. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/551) The summary is that solar eclipse prayer is Sunnah or wajib, lunar eclipse prayer is good (hasanah), and similarly prayer in darkness, wind, and other fearful events because all are fearful signs. Al-Shafi'i says: when the moon is eclipsed, the imam prays with the people in the mosque two rak'ahs and bows two bowings in each rak'ah, and recites audibly, based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas that he prayed with the people in the lunar eclipse. This hadith is not adopted because it is a solitary report in a well-known matter. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'Fear' refers to fear, earthquakes, lightning, shooting stars, terrifying light at night, snow, continuous rain, and general diseases. (T)
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the eclipse prayer, focusing on the actions after the prayer and the rulings for other celestial and natural phenomena. After the solar eclipse prayer, it is Sunnah for the imam to lead the congregation in supplication (du'a) facing the qibla, with the people saying 'amin', until the sun clears completely. If it does not clear before sunset, the du'a is discontinued. If the imam of Friday (the appointed leader) is not present, the people pray individually (munfarid) in two or four rak'ahs. The lunar eclipse (khusuf) is treated differently: it is prayed individually, not in congregation, because the Prophet never led congregational prayer for it, and gathering at night is impractical and could cause fitna. The summary from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq classifies solar eclipse prayer as Sunnah (or wajib), lunar eclipse prayer as merely good (hasanah), and similarly prayer during other fearful events like darkness, strong wind, earthquakes, etc., as good deeds. There is a dispute with al-Shafi'i, who holds that lunar eclipse should be prayed in congregation with audible recitation and two bowings per rak'ah, based on a hadith from Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid) in a matter of common knowledge, so it is not accepted as binding. The passage concludes by listing various fearful events that warrant individual prayer and supplication.

Key Terms
الفزع (al-faza'): Fear or calamity, such as earthquakes, lightning, etc.
الخسوف (al-khusuf): Lunar eclipse
الكسوف (al-kusuf): Solar eclipse
حسنة (hasanah): A good deed; recommended but not Sunnah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the lunar eclipse prayer not performed in congregation?
A) Because the Prophet never led congregational prayer for it, and gathering at night is difficult.
B) Because the hadith for lunar eclipse is weak.
C) Because lunar eclipses are rare and not important.
D) Because the prayer is not allowed at night.

Key Takeaway
Lunar eclipse prayer and prayers for other natural calamities are performed individually (not in congregation) in the Hanafi school, as good deeds (hasanah), unlike the solar eclipse prayer which is Sunnah and performed in congregation.
