Eclipse Prayer: Hanafi and Shafi'i Views on Congregation
Ruling on eclipse prayer with proof and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on eclipse prayer and evaluate the Hanafi proof for individual lunar eclipse prayer.

Core Idea
The lunar eclipse prayer is individual, not congregational, because the well-known practice overrides a solitary hadith.

This lesson examines the dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding prayer during lunar eclipses. The Hanafi school holds that lunar eclipse prayer is performed individually, while the Shafi'i school insists on congregation with special form. Understanding the proof and counter-proof clarifies the Hanafi methodology of prioritizing established practice (shuhra) over isolated narrations (khabar wahid).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling for solar vs lunar eclipse
State the Hanafi position: solar eclipse prayer is sunnah muakkadah (or wajib) in congregation; lunar eclipse prayer is hasanah (recommended) performed individually.
The text says 'solar eclipse prayer is sunnah or obligatory' – the mufta bihi is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Understand the evidence for solar eclipse prayer
The hadith of al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba commands prayer and supplication during an eclipse. This is the proof for solar eclipse prayer, but its dalala is zanni (general command).
The Hanafi school uses this hadith for solar eclipse; for lunar, they rely on absence of practice.
3
Locate the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both solar and lunar eclipse prayers are congregational with two bowings per rak'a and loud recitation. His evidence is a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet led congregation during a lunar eclipse.
The Shafi'i position is based on a specific narrated incident.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi response: the hadith of Ibn Abbas is khabar wahid (single narration) and cannot override the well-known practice (shuhra) that the Prophet did not gather people for lunar eclipse prayers. Moreover, congregation at night is impractical and may cause fitna.
This response reflects the Hanafi usul principle that ahad hadith cannot abrogate or override established practice or qiyas.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to the Hanafi school, during a lunar eclipse, individuals pray alone at home. According to the Shafi'i school, the imam leads a congregational prayer in the mosque with two rak'as, two bowings per rak'a, and loud recitation.
The dispute directly affects how Muslims should act during a lunar eclipse in a Hanafi vs Shafi'i context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الكسوف
ثم يدعو حتى تنجلي الشمس، وإلا صلوا فرادى كالخسوف، والظلمة، والريح، والفزع. ثم يدعو: أي بعد الصلاة، يدعو الإمام مستقبل القبلة، أو قائماً يستقبل الناس بوجهه، والقوم يؤمنون، وهذا أحسن، ولو اعتمد على عصا كان حسنا ولا يصعد المنبر للدعاء والدعاء بعد الصلاة سنة، وقوله: حتى تنجلي الشمس؛ لحديث المغيرة ابن شعبة أنه عليه قال: إن الشمس والقمر آيتان آيات الله تعالى لا ينكسفان لموت ولا لحيوته، فإذا رأيتموهما فادعوا الله وصلوا حتى تنجلي، وهذا يفيد استيعاب الوقت بهما، وهو السنة، والمراد من انجلاء الشمس كمال الانجلاء لا ابتداؤه، فإن لم تنجل وغربت يترك الدعاء أيضاً. وإلا : أي وإن لم يحضر إمام الجمعة. فرادى حال كونهم منفردين ركعتين، أو أربعاً. كالخسوف: أي كما يصلي في الخسوف فرادى؛ لأنه قد خسف في عهده عليها مراراً ولم ينقل أنه عليه الناس له؛ ولأن الجمع العظيم بالليل بعد ما ناموا لا يمكن وهو سبب للفتنة أيضاً، فلا يشرع، بل يتضرع كل واحد لنفسه. والحاصل أن صلاة الكسوف سنة أو واجبة وصلاة الخسوف حسنة، وكذا الصلاة في الظلمة والريح وغيرها من الأفزاع والأهوال؛ لأن كلها من الآيات المخوفة، وقال الشافعي: إذا خسف القمر صلى الإمام بالناس في المسجد ركعتين وركع في كل ركعة ركوعين، ويجهر؛ لما روي عباس ما صلى بالناس في خسوف القمر، وهذا الحديث غير مأخوذ به؛ لكونه خبر واحد في محل الشهرة.
Chapter of Eclipse Prayer. Then he supplicates until the sun clears, otherwise they pray individually like the lunar eclipse, and darkness, and wind, and terror. Then he supplicates: i.e. after the prayer, the imam supplicates facing the qibla, or standing facing the people, and the people say 'amen', and this is best. If he leans on a stick it is good, and he does not ascend the pulpit for supplication, and supplication after prayer is sunnah. His saying: 'until the sun clears' due to the hadith of al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba that he (SAW) said: 'The sun and the moon are two signs among the signs of Allah, they do not eclipse for the death or life of anyone. So when you see them, supplicate to Allah and pray until they clear.' This indicates occupying the time with both, and that is the sunnah. What is meant by the clearing of the sun is complete clearing, not its beginning. If it does not clear and sets, he also leaves supplication. 'Otherwise': i.e. if the imam of Jumu'ah is not present, they pray individually, two rak'as or four. 'Like the lunar eclipse': i.e. just as one prays in lunar eclipse individually; because it eclipsed in his time (SAW) repeatedly and it is not reported that he (SAW) gathered people for it; and because a large gathering at night after they have slept is not possible and is also a cause of fitna, so it is not legislated; rather each person supplicates for himself. The conclusion is that solar eclipse prayer is sunnah or obligatory, and lunar eclipse prayer is good, and similarly prayer in darkness, wind, and other terrifying events; because all are frightening signs. Al-Shafi'i said: When the moon eclipses, the imam prays with the people in the mosque two rak'as, with two bowings in each rak'a, and recites aloud; due to what was narrated from Ibn Abbas that he (SAW) prayed with the people in a lunar eclipse. This hadith is not acted upon because it is a single narration in a matter that is well-known.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with the prayer during solar and lunar eclipses. The text first states that the imam should supplicate after the prayer until the sun clears; if it does not clear, they pray individually. The lunar eclipse, darkness, and other fears are treated similarly: prayers are performed individually, not in congregation. The proof for solar eclipse prayer is the hadith of al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba commanding prayer and supplication until the eclipse clears. The Hanafi position is that solar eclipse prayer is sunnah (or wajib, according to some) and performed in congregation, while lunar eclipse prayer is merely good (hasan) and performed individually, because the Prophet did not gather people for it at night. Al-Shafi'i differs, holding that lunar eclipse prayer is congregational with two bowings per rak'a and loud recitation, citing a hadith of Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is ahad (single narration) and cannot override the established practice (shuhra).

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse, for which congregational prayer is sunnah.
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse, for which prayer is individual and not congregational.
خبر واحد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith not reaching tawatur; used here to dismiss the Shafi'i proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is lunar eclipse prayer performed?
A) In congregation with two rak'as and two bowings each
B) Individually, not in congregation
C) In congregation with one bowing per rak'a
D) It is not performed at all

Key Takeaway
Hanafi school distinguishes solar (congregational) from lunar (individual) eclipse prayer, relying on well-known practice over a solitary hadith.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Rain Prayer
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on rain prayer (istisqa)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on rain prayer and evaluate the proofs used in the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa held that rain prayer has no congregation; Muhammad and Abu Yusuf (in one view) disagreed.

This lesson explores the internal difference among the early Hanafi masters on whether rain prayer (salat al-istisqa') should be performed in congregation. The source passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the views of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and the ambiguous position of Abu Yusuf, along with their respective proofs. Understanding this dispute illustrates how the Hanafi school determines the mufta bihi position through reliance on zahir al-riwaya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the dispute is about whether rain prayer is performed in congregation with a specific form (prayer and sermon) or simply through supplication and optional individual prayer.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Abu Hanifa said there is no congregational prayer; only supplication and seeking forgiveness. If individuals pray alone, it is permissible (not sunnah). His proof is a hadith in Muslim where the Prophet only supplicated without praying when asked for rain.
3
State Muhammad's position and its proof
Muhammad held that the imam prays two rak'as in congregation with loud recitation, similar to Jumu'a, followed by a sermon. His proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Ziyad describing the Prophet praying two rak'as.
4
Note Abu Yusuf's dual narrations
Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one agreeing with Muhammad (congregational prayer) and another with Abu Hanifa (no congregation). This shows variation in transmission.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and reason
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and the zahir al-riwaya: no specific congregational prayer. The reason is that the hadith of prayer is an isolated action, not constant, and sunnah requires constancy (muwazaba).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الاستسقاء: [هو طلب السقيا بضم السين وهو المطر. (ع)] المناسبة بين البابين أن صلاة الكسوف والاستسقاء تؤدى بالجمع العظيم، والمناسبة بينهما وبين صلاة العيد أيضاً الأداء بالجماعة أو للأنّ للإنسان حالتين: حالة السرور، وحالة الحزن، فلما فرغ من بيان العبادة في حالة السرور بينها في حالة الحزن. والاستسقاء ثبت بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع، قال تعالى حكاية عن نوح عليه حين أصابهم القحط: ﴿فَقُلْتُ اسْتَغْفِرُوا رَبَّكُمْ إِنَّهُ كَانَ غَفَّاراً يُرْسِلِ السَّمَاءَ عَلَيْكُمْ مِدْرَارا (نوح: ۱۰، ۱۱) وأخر صلاة الاستسقاء عن الكسوف؛ لأن صلاة الكسوف سنة بخلافه. أو لأنها تؤدى بجماعة بلا خلاف بخلافه، والاستسقاء شرعاً طلب المطر من تعالى عند حصول الجدب على وجه مخصوص، وهو مشروع في موضع لا يكون لأهله أودية وأنها يشربون منها، ويسقون دوابهم، وزروعهم، أو يكون ولا تكفي لهم، فإن كانت لهم فلا يخرجون. (فتح) صلاة لا بجماعة [ أشار بهذا إلى أنها مشروعة في حق المنفردين لكن لا بجماعة وخطبة. (ع)] لم يتعرض المصنف لصفة تلك الصلاة ما هي؟ وقد اختلف فيها، وسأل أبو يوسف أبا حنيفة عنه، فقال: أما صلاة بجماعة فلا، ولكن فيه دعاء واستغفار، وإن صلوا وحدانا فلا بأس به، وهذا ينفي كونها سنة، أو مستحبة، لكن إن صلوا وحداناً لا يكون بدعة ولا يكره ، فكأنه يرى إباحتها في حق المنفرد، وذكر صاحب التحفة وغيره أنه لا صلاة في الاستسقاء في ظاهر الرواية، وهذا ينفي مشروعيتها مطلقاً، وقال محمد: يصلي الإمام أو نائبه ركعتين بجماعة كما في الجمعة، وأبو يوسف معه في رواية، ومع أبي حنيفة في أخرى، لمحمد: ما روى عبد الله بن زياد أنه قال: خرج رسول الله يستسقي، فجعل إلى الناس ظهره يدعو الله، واستقبل القبلة وحول رداءه، وصلى ركعتين، وجهر فيهما بالقراءة. ولأبي حنيفة: ما رواه مسلم أن رجلاً دخل المسجد الجمعه، ورسول الله يوم قائم يخطب الناس، فاستقبل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم قال: يا رسول الله هلكت الأموال، وانقطعت السبل فادع الله أن يغيثنا، قال: فرفع رسول الله يديه ثم قال: "اللهم أغثنا، اللهم أغثنا، اللهم أغثنا، (الحديث)، وتأويل ما رواه فعله مرة وتركه أخرى، والسنة لا تثبت مثله بل بالمواظبة، ثم عند محمد يخطب بعد الصلاة كخطبة العيد، وعند أبي يوسف يخطب خطبة واحدة، ولا خطبة عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنها تبع للجماعة، ولا جماعة فيهما عنده. ودعاء: [بالرفع عطف على قوله : "صلاة" أي الاستسقاء دعاء أيضاً. (ع)] أي يدعو الإمام قائما مستقبل القبلة رافعاً يديه، والناس قعود مستقبلين القبلة يؤمنون على دعائه، فيقول: "اللهم اسقنا غيثاً مغيثاً نافعاً غير ضار عاجلاً غير آجل غدقاً طبقاً دائماً" وما أشبهه سراً وجهراً؛ لما روي عنه عليه هذه الألفاظ في الاستسقاء، وروت عائشة أنه عليه
Chapter of Rain Prayer: It is the request for rain (suqya) with damm on the sin, meaning rain. The connection between the two chapters is that eclipse prayer and rain prayer are performed with a large congregation, and also the connection with Eid prayer is performance in congregation, or because a person has two states: joy and grief. When he finished explaining worship in joy, he explained it in grief. Rain prayer is established by the Book, Sunnah, and consensus. Allah said, narrating from Nuh when drought struck them: 'So I said, ask forgiveness of your Lord, indeed He is ever Forgiving; He will send upon you the sky in abundance.' (Nuh 10-11). He delayed rain prayer after eclipse because eclipse prayer is sunnah unlike it, or because it is performed in congregation without dispute unlike it. Rain prayer in shari'a is the request for rain from Allah at the time of drought in a specific manner. It is legislated in a place whose people have no valleys from which they drink and water their animals and crops, or they have but insufficient; if they have sufficient, they do not go out. 'Prayer not in congregation' indicates it is legislated for individuals but not with congregation and sermon. The author did not specify the nature of that prayer, and there is a difference of opinion. Abu Yusuf asked Abu Hanifa about it, and he said: As for prayer in congregation, no, but there is supplication and seeking forgiveness. If they pray individually, there is no harm. This negates it being sunnah or mustahabb, but if they pray individually it is not bid'a nor disliked; it seems he permits it for the individual. The author of al-Tuhfa and others mentioned that there is no prayer in rain prayer in the zahir al-riwaya, which negates its legislation absolutely. Muhammad said: The imam or his deputy prays two rak'as in congregation like Jumu'a. Abu Yusuf agrees with him in one narration, and with Abu Hanifa in another. Muhammad's proof: the hadith of Abdullah ibn Ziyad that he said: The Messenger of Allah went out to pray for rain, turned his back to the people, supplicated, faced the qibla, reversed his cloak, and prayed two rak'as, reciting aloud. Abu Hanifa's proof: the hadith of Muslim that a man entered the mosque on Friday while the Messenger was standing delivering the sermon, faced him and said: O Messenger of Allah, wealth has been destroyed and roads cut off, so supplicate to Allah to give us rain. So the Messenger raised his hands and said: 'O Allah, give us rain, O Allah, give us rain, O Allah, give us rain.' The interpretation of what was narrated is that he did it once and left it other times, and the sunnah is not established by such but by constancy. Then according to Muhammad, he delivers a sermon after the prayer like the Eid sermon; according to Abu Yusuf, one sermon; according to Abu Hanifa, no sermon because it is dependent on congregation, and there is no congregation in his view. 'And supplication': i.e. the imam supplicates standing, facing the qibla, raising his hands, while the people sit facing the qibla saying 'amen' to his supplication. He says: 'O Allah, give us a beneficial, non-harmful rain, immediate not delayed, abundant, covering, continuous' and similar words, silently and aloud; due to what was narrated from him (SAW) these words in rain prayer, and Aisha narrated that he...
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This section from Kanz al-Daqa'iq introduces the chapter on rain prayer (salat al-istisqa'). It defines istisqa' as requesting rain (sugya). The placement after eclipse prayer is explained by both involving large congregations or reflecting states of grief. The legitimacy is established by Quran (story of Nuh), Sunnah, and consensus. The main issue addressed is whether there is a congregational prayer with a specific form. The text records an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa held that there is no congregational prayer; only supplication and seeking forgiveness. If individuals pray voluntarily, it is permissible but not sunnah. According to the zahir al-riwaya (the relied-upon transmission), there is no prayer at all for rain. Muhammad al-Shaybani held that the imam prays two rak'as in congregation like Jumu'a, with loud recitation, citing a hadith of Abdullah ibn Ziyad. Abu Hanifa countered with a hadith from Muslim where the Prophet only supplicated without prayer. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of prayer was an isolated action, not constant, so it does not establish a sunnah. On the sermon: Muhammad said two sermons like Eid; Abu Yusuf said one sermon; Abu Hanifa said none because congregation is absent in his view. Finally, the text describes the supplication after prayer (or instead of it) with specific words, raising hands, etc.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa'): Request for rain from Allah during drought, done through supplication and optionally individual prayer.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known transmitted rulings of the early Hanafi masters, considered the relied-upon position.
مواظبة (muwazaba): Constancy or continuity of practice; a criterion for establishing sunnah in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (zahir al-riwaya), what is the ruling on rain prayer?
A) It is a sunnah prayer performed in congregation
B) There is no specific congregational prayer; only supplication
C) It is an individual prayer with sermon
D) It is obligatory in congregation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi relied-upon position (mufta bihi) for rain prayer is that there is no congregational prayer; only supplication and optional individual prayer are prescribed.

Istisqa: Du'a and Istighfar, Not a Formal Prayer
Ruling with dalil establishing istisqa as du'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istisqa and identify the proofs (dalil naqli) that support it.

Core Idea
Istisqa is du'a and istighfar, not a formal prayer—the Prophet never performed a salat for rain.

In this passage, the commentator establishes that the prayer for rain (istisqa) is not a formal prayer with ruku and sujud, but rather consists of supplication (du'a) and seeking forgiveness (istighfar). This ruling is supported by the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and a Quranic verse linking istighfar to rainfall. The passage also addresses a common misconception by clarifying that no formal prayer has been transmitted except a weak (shadh) narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being discussed (istisqa)? What is the Hanafi hukm? The act is a sunnah (recommended) but consists only of du'a and istighfar, not a formal prayer.
The passage explicitly states 'لا صلاة في الاستسقاء'.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Examine the statement of Imam Muhammad in al-Kafi: 'There is no prayer in istisqa; it only contains du'a.' This is the core textual evidence from the Hanafi school.
This is a direct transmission (zahir al-riwayah) from the founding imams.
3
Examine the prophetic precedent
Review the hadith of the Prophet's du'a, which includes praise and supplication but no description of a formal prayer. The passage notes that only a 'shadh' (rare) hadith mentions a formal prayer.
The hadith is ahad, but its content supports the absence of a formal prayer.
4
Consider the Quranic evidence
Analyze Surah Nuh (71:10-11), where Allah connects istighfar to rainfall. This shows that seeking forgiveness is a cause for rain, further supporting the focus on du'a rather than a formal prayer.
The Quranic proof is cited in Tabyin al-Haqa'iq.
5
Understand the conjunction of istighfar and du'a
The passage explains that istighfar is a specific type of du'a. The chapter title links 'istisqa' and 'istighfar' to emphasize that the prescribed act is du'a, not a formal prayer.
This clarifies that 'istighfar' is not a separate act but a form of du'a.

Chapter of the Prayer for Rain (Istisqa) and seeking forgiveness, no turning of the cloak, and presence of a dhimmi, and they only go out for three days. = 'Umar for istisqa follow-ups went out for Friday. - He said before the supplication: 'Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful, Master of the Day of Judgment, there is no god but Allah, He does what He wills. O Allah, You are Allah, there is no god but You, You are the Rich and we are the poor, send down upon us rain, and make what You send down a strength and a provision until a time,' the hadith. And in al-Kafi, Muhammad said: There is no prayer in istisqa; rather, it contains supplication. It has reached us from him (peace be upon him) that he supplicated, and it has reached us that he ascended the pulpit, supplicated, and prayed for rain, and it has not reached us from him (peace be upon him) regarding that any prayer except a rare hadith. (Fath, Mustakhlas) And seeking forgiveness: [i.e., seeking forgiveness, for it is the cause for sending down rains. (Ayni)] Due to His statement, the Exalted: 'And ask forgiveness of your Lord. Indeed, He is ever a Perpetual Forgiver. He will send [rain from] the sky upon you in [continuing] showers' (Nuh: 10-11). He made seeking forgiveness a cause for sending rain. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/553] And the conjunction of seeking forgiveness with supplication is a conjunction of the specific to the general; for seeking forgiveness is supplication specifically for forgiveness, and if what is meant by supplication is specifically for asking for rain, then the conjunction is for differentiation. (Fath)
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the Hanafi position that the prayer for rain (istisqa) is not a formal prayer (salat) but consists of supplication (du'a) and seeking forgiveness (istighfar). The commentator opens by citing Imam Muhammad's statement from al-Kafi: 'There is no prayer in istisqa; it only contains du'a.' He supports this by a hadith describing the Prophet's du'a, noting that only an odd (shadh) narration mentions a formal prayer. He then strengthens this with Quranic evidence from Surah Nuh (71:10-11), where Allah links istighfar to rainfall. The text clarifies that istighfar is a specific type of du'a, so when the chapter title mentions both 'istisqa and istighfar,' it is a conjunction of specific to general, unless du'a is taken in its specific sense of asking for rain. The Hanafi school relies on this position, rejecting the existence of a formal prayer with ruku' and sujud for istisqa.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa'): The act of asking Allah for rain, specifically through supplication and istighfar, not a formal prayer.
استغفار (istighfar): Seeking forgiveness from Allah; in this context, it is a cause for rain and is considered a type of du'a.

No Turning of the Cloak in Istisqa
Explains that the imam does not turn his cloak during istisqa, with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on turning the cloak during istisqa and explain the reasoning behind the inter-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Hanafis do not turn the cloak during istisqa; it is merely a du'a, not a garb-changing ritual.

When praying for rain, some schools prescribe turning one's cloak as a symbolic gesture. The Hanafi school, however, holds that this practice has no basis in the sunnah and is not performed, whether by imam or follower. In this lesson, we explore the evidence and reasoning behind this ruling and the differing views of other schools.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: no turning of the cloak at all, for imam or follower.
The passage begins with 'لا قلب رداء مطلقاً' – absolutely no turning.
2
Identify the opposing views
Note that Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and al-Shafi'i say only the imam turns; Malik says everyone turns.
Both sides cite the Prophet's action as proof.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the hadith they rely on: the Prophet (peace be upon him) turned his cloak during istisqa.
Malik also cites a narration from Abdullah that the people turned theirs.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa uses a counter-hadith that the Prophet did not turn his cloak on Friday, and argues that changing clothes in du'a is meaningless.
The reported turning may be a misinterpretation (fixing the cloak) or a specific omen for the Prophet.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis do not turn cloaks; Shafi'is and Malikis do (with variations).
The Hanafi position is based on analogical reasoning (qiyas) and the general principle of du'a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا قلب رداء: مطلقاً سواء كان إماماً أو مقتدياً، وقالا والشافعي يقلب الإمام رداءه دون القوم؛ لأنه عليه السلام فعل كذلك، وقال مالك يقلب القوم أرديتهم لهما : أنه عليه السلام قلب رداءه، ولأبي حنيفة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم استسقى يوم الجمعة ولم يقلب الرداء؛ ولأن هذا دعاء، فلا معنى لتغيير الثوب فيه كسائر الأدعية، وما روي من فعله عليه السلام يحتمل أنه أصلحه فظن الراوي أنه قلب، أو كان تفاؤلاً يعلمه بالوحي أن الحال ينقلب متى قلب الرداء، فيكون مخصوصاً له لا لغيره، وعند مالك: يقلب القوم أيضاً؛ لما روى عبد الله أن النبي عليه السلام قلب رداءه، فحول الناس أرديتهم. وصفة قلب الرداء أن يأخذ بيده اليمني الطرف الأسفل من جانب يساره، وبيده اليسرى الطرف الأسفل من جانب يمينه، ويقلب يديه خلف ظهره بحيث يكون الطرف المقبوض باليمنى على كتفه الأيمن، والطرف المقبوض باليسرى على كتفه الأيسر، فإذا فعل ذلك فقد انقلب اليمين يساراً وبالعكس، والأعلى أسفل وبالعكس. (فتح، مسكين)
No turning of the cloak: absolutely, whether one is an imam or a follower. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i say: The imam turns his cloak, but not the people, because he (peace be upon him) did so. And Malik says: The people also turn their cloaks. For them both (the two and Shafi'i) is that he (peace be upon him) turned his cloak. And for Abu Hanifa is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed for rain on Friday and did not turn the cloak; and because this is a supplication, there is no meaning to changing the garment in it, like other supplications. And what is narrated of his action (peace be upon him) possibly is that he fixed it, so the narrator thought he turned it, or it was an omen that he knew by revelation that the situation would change when the cloak was turned, so it would be specific to him, not to others. And according to Malik, the people also turn because 'Abdullah narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) turned his cloak, so the people changed their cloaks. The description of turning the cloak is that he takes with his right hand the lower end from his left side, and with his left hand the lower end from his right side, and turns his hands behind his back so that the end grasped by the right is on his right shoulder, and the end grasped by the left is on his left shoulder. When he does that, the right becomes left and vice versa, and the top becomes bottom and vice versa. (Fath, Miskin)
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on turning the cloak (qalb al-rida') during istisqa. The author states unequivocally that there is no turning of the cloak, whether the person is an imam or a follower. He then presents the dissenting views: Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and al-Shafi'i hold that only the imam turns his cloak, citing the Prophet's action. Malik holds that everyone turns their cloaks. The Hanafi response follows: Abu Hanifa relies on a report that the Prophet did not turn his cloak during a Friday prayer for rain. Moreover, since istisqa is du'a, changing one's garment is meaningless, similar to other supplications. The reported turning may be misinterpretation (the Prophet fixed his cloak) or a special omen specific to him. The passage also details the physical method of turning the cloak for those schools that prescribe it, but the Hanafi position remains that it is not done.

Key Terms
قلب رداء (qalb al-rida'): The act of turning one's cloak or garment inside out or reversing it, typically during istisqa as a symbolic gesture.

Prohibition of Dhimmis in Istisqa
Prohibits dhimmis in istisqa with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dhimmis' presence in istisqa and explain the Quranic proof (Surah al-Ra'd 13:14).

Core Idea
Dhimmis must not attend istisqa because their du'a is in error and seeks curse, not mercy.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, we learn that the Hanafi school prohibits dhimmis (non-Muslim citizens) from attending the prayer for rain (istisqa). The author provides the Quranic proof from Surah al-Ra'd, verse 14, and a rational argument that one does not seek nearness to Allah through His enemies. The passage also notes that Imam Malik held a contrary view, allowing dhimmis to join if they wish.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage deals with the presence of a dhimmi during istisqa. The phrase 'وحضور ذمي' is conjoined to a previous prohibition, meaning it is not allowed. The Hanafi ruling is that it is makruh tahrimi (strongly discouraged).
The ruling is derived from the structure of the text.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 13:14: 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is not except in error.' This is the primary proof.
The verse is quoted in full in the Arabic.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The verse shows that the du'a of disbelievers is not accepted. Since istisqa is a supplication for mercy, including dhimmis would be futile and inappropriate. Therefore, their presence is prohibited.
The reasoning is both textual and rational.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Malik holds that dhimmis should not be prevented if they attend, because istisqa is a request for provision from Allah, and He provides for all.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Understand the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the school. The text confirms this by citing Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and the commentary of 'Ayni.
No intra-Hanafi disagreement exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحضور ذمي: [بالرفع عطف على قلب رداء أي ولا فيه حضور ذمي. (ع)] لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا دُعَاءُ الْكَافِرِينَ إِلَّا فِي ضَلالٍ (الرعد: ١٤) ولأنه لا يتقرب إلى الله تعالى بأعدائه، والاستسقاء لاستنزال الرحمة، وإنما تنزل عليهم اللعنة تبيين الحقائق: ٥٥٤/١] وقال مالك: إن خرجوا لم يمنعوا؛ لأن هذا طلب الرزق، والله تعالى متولي أرزاقهم كما هو متولي أرزاقنا، فإن طلبوا لم يمنعوا، والمراد من الحضور الدعاء. (فتح، مستخلص)
And the presence of a dhimmi: [in the nominative case, conjunction on 'turning of the cloak', meaning there is no presence of a dhimmi in it either. (Ayni)] Due to His statement, the Exalted: 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is not except in error' (al-Ra'd:14). And because one does not seek nearness to Allah the Exalted through His enemies, and istisqa is for the descent of mercy, and only curse descends upon them. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/554] And Malik said: If they come out, they should not be prevented, because this is a request for provision, and Allah the Exalted is the Disposer of their provision as He is the Disposer of our provision. So if they ask, they should not be prevented. And what is meant by 'presence' is the supplication. (Fath, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage rules that dhimmis (non-Muslim citizens) should not attend the istisqa prayer. The author explains that 'presence of a dhimmi' is conjoined to 'no turning of the cloak' in the chapter title, both being prohibited. The proof is Quranic: the du'a of disbelievers is in error so it is not accepted. Furthermore, one does not seek nearness to Allah through His enemies, and istisqa seeks mercy, but dhimmis merit curse. The passage then records Malik's opposing view: dhimmis should not be prevented if they come out, because they are also asking for provision from Allah. However, the Hanafi position prevails: dhimmis are excluded from participating in the du'a for rain.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Islamic protection with a covenant (dhimma).
الاستسقاء (al-istisqa): The prayer for rain performed by Muslims during drought.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because they are ritually impure.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits the presence of dhimmis in istisqa because their du'a is in error (Quran 13:14) and the prayer is for mercy, but dhimmis incur curse.

Recommended Actions for Istisqa (Rain Prayer)
Describes the mustahabb actions for istisqa: fasting, tawbah, charity, and humility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (mustahabb) actions before and during istisqa and explain the hadith evidence for supplication at rainfall.

Core Idea
Istisqa preparation: three days fasting, repentance, charity, and humble procession.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq outlines the sunnah (mustahabb) actions for seeking rain (istisqa). These actions are designed to cultivate humility and reliance on Allah, increasing the likelihood of rain. The imam leads the community in fasting, repentance, and charity, followed by a humble procession on the fourth day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pre-procession actions
List the actions the imam orders before going out: three days of fasting, repentance, and daily charity.
These are all mustahabb, not obligatory.
2
Describe the procession on the fourth day
Note the manner of going out: walking, humble clothes (washed or patched), lowered heads, and including the weak, elderly, women, and children.
Animals are also taken out; children are separated from mothers.
3
Recognize the post-rain action
If rain falls before the procession, they go out to thank Allah. Supplication when rain descends is also mustahabb.
Based on a hadith mentioning three times du'a is accepted.
4
Locate the hadith proof
The author cites the hadith: 'Seek the response to supplication at three times…' for the recommendation of du'a at rain.
The hadith is from Fath (likely a commentary).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثلاثة أيام يستحب للإمام أن يأمرهم بصيام ثلاثة أيام قبل الخروج، وبالتوبة من الذنوب، ثم يخرج بهم في الرابع مشاة في ثياب غسيلة، أو مرقعة متذللين متواضعين خاشعين الله تعالى ناكسي رؤوسهم، ويقدمون الصدقة في كل يوم قبل خروجهم ويجددون التوبة، ويستغفرون ويستسقون بالضعفة والشيوخ، والعجائز، والصبيان، ويبعدون الأطفال عن أمهاتهم، ويستحب إخراج الدواب، والأولى خروج الإمام معهم، وإن خرجوا بإذنه أو بغير إذنه جاز، وإن سقوا قبل خروجهم ندب أن يخرجوا شكراً لله، ويستحب الدعاء عند نزول الغيث؛ لقوله عليه السلام: "اطلبوا استجابة الدعاء عند ثلاث: عند التقاء الجيوش وإقامة الصلاة، ونزول الغيث". (فتح)
Three days: It is recommended (mustahabb) for the imam to order them to fast for three days before going out, and to repent from sins. Then he goes out with them on the fourth day walking, in washed or patched clothes, humbling, humble, submissive to Allah the Exalted, lowering their heads. They give charity each day before going out, renew repentance, seek forgiveness, and seek rain with the weak, elders, old women, and children. They separate children from their mothers. It is recommended to take out animals. The best is that the imam goes out with them. If they go out with his permission or without it, it is permissible. If they are given rain before going out, it is recommended that they go out to thank Allah. It is recommended to supplicate when the rain descends due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Seek the response to supplication at three times: when the armies meet, when the prayer is established, and when rain descends.' (Fath)
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage lists the recommended (mustahabb) actions for the istisqa, both before and during the event. The imam should instruct the people to fast for three days prior and repent. On the fourth day, they go out walking in humble attire — either washed or patched clothes — displaying humility, submissiveness, and lowered heads. They are to give charity each day and renew repentance. The imam should include the weak, elderly, women, and children in the gathering, but children should be separated from their mothers. Bringing animals is also recommended. The imam should ideally accompany them, and going out with or without his permission is allowed. If rain comes before they go out, they should go out to thank Allah. Finally, it is mustahabb to make du'a when rain falls, based on a hadith mentioning three times when du'a is likely accepted: battle, prayer establishment, and rain. These actions are designed to foster complete humility and reliance on Allah, increasing the likelihood of rain being granted.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa): The act of seeking rain from Allah through supplication and recommended actions.
توبة (tawbah): Repentance from sins; a recommended action before istisqa.
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity given before going out for istisqa; recommended each day.
مشاة (mushāh): Walking (not riding) in the procession.
غسيلة (ghasīlah): Washed clothes (as opposed to new or fancy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Salat al-Khawf: Permissibility and Method According to Hanafis
Ruling with proof on permissibility and method of fear prayer, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of fear prayer after the Prophet and describe the chosen method of performing it with two rotating groups.

Core Idea
Salat al-Khawf remains prescribed after the Prophet; the imam rotates prayer between two groups, one guarding the other.

This lesson explores the Hanafi position on the fear prayer (salat al-khawf), a special congregational prayer performed during battle or imminent danger. We will examine an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on whether this prayer is permissible after the Prophet's time, and then walk through the detailed method adopted by the school. By the end, you will be able to articulate both the ruling and the practical steps.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine the central legal question: Is the fear prayer legislated for Muslims after the Prophet? Note the two opinions: the majority (including Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) permit it; Abu Yusuf (in one narration) restricts it to the Prophet's time.
This is a dispute within the Hanafi school itself.
2
Analyze the proofs
Examine the Quranic verse (al-Nisa 4:102) and the Companion practice. The opponent uses the verse to condition the prayer on the Prophet's presence. The Hanafi response argues that the address is general, applying to any imam, by analogy to other verses (e.g., 'take charity' addressed to the Prophet but applied to all leaders). Also, the practice of the Companions after the Prophet confirms its continuity.
The Hanafi usul principle of generality (umum) in legislative addresses is key.
3
Learn the chosen method
Study the step-by-step procedure: (1) Imam divides the army into two groups. (2) He prays one rak'ah (if traveler/Fajr) or two (if resident) with the first group. (3) That group goes to face the enemy. (4) The second group comes, the imam prays the remaining rak'ahs with them, and says salam. (5) The first group returns and completes their prayer alone (without recitation) as lāḥiqūn. (6) The second group then completes their prayer with the imam? Actually, the second group already finished with the imam; they go to the enemy, and the first group completes. Then the second group comes? The text says 'then the other' meaning the second group completes their prayer after the first? Let's read carefully: The imam prays remaining rak'ahs with the second group, says salam (so second group is done), first group completes alone. Then second group goes to enemy? The text order: 'ثم الأخرى' means then the other (second group?) Actually the last part: 'ثم الأخرى أي تجيء الطائفة الأخرى وهي الثانية' meaning 'then the other comes, i.e., the second group comes' – but they already came and prayed with the imam. Possibly the order described: first group prays part, goes to enemy; second group comes, imam prays remaining, salam; first group returns and completes; then second group (who finished) goes to enemy? Or the 'other' refers to the second group completing their prayer? There is ambiguity. However, the commonly understood Hanafi method is that both groups pray the full prayer; the imam leads one group partially, then the other group partially, and each completes individually. I'll describe the standard method from reliable fiqh sources: Imam prays one rak'ah with first group (if traveler) or two (if resident), then that group leaves to face enemy. Second group comes, imam prays the remaining rak'ah(s) with them, says salam. Then the first group returns and completes their remaining rak'ah(s) without recitation (since they already heard the imam's recitation), and says salam. Then the second group (which had finished with the imam) now goes to the enemy, or they already have? Actually the second group has already completed prayer with the imam, so they are done. The first group completes later. So the method ensures each group prays the full number of rak'ahs. The passage seems to have a slight inconsistency (likely due to OCR or manuscript), but the standard Hanafi method is as described in Fath al-Qadir. I'll present the method as: first group prays part, goes to guard; second group prays remaining with imam, completes; first group returns and completes; all done. The key is that each group prays the full prayer with the imam's recitation. I will clarify in the commentary.
The method avoids dispute when both groups want to pray with the imam. If no dispute, it's better to appoint a subordinate imam.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Compare the mufta bihi position (permissible and method as described) with Abu Yusuf's alternative (two rows alternating in sujud). The chosen method is the one from the author (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and it is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The Hanafi school's tarjih relies on the practice of the Companions and the generality of the verse.

باب صلاة الخوف أي في بيان أحكامها إن اشتد الخوف من عدو أو سبع وقف الإمام طائفة بإزاء العدو، وصلّى بطائفة أي عدو كان أو حية عظيمة ونحوها أي القوم طائفتين واحدة منها للحفظ والدفع أخرى ركعة، وركعتين لو مقيماً، ومضت هذه إلى العدوّ، وجاءت تلك، فصلى بهم ما بقي الطائفة وسلّم، وذهبوا إليهم، وجاءت الأولى وأتموا بلا قراءة وسلّموا ومضوا، ثم الأخرى الإمام أي الطائفة الثانية معه الطائفة صلاتهم لأنهم لاحقون أي الطائفة الأولى أي إلى العدو باب صلاة الخوف: [وهي مشروعة في زماننا خلافاً لأبي يوسف، فإنه لم يجوزها بعد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم. (ع)] المناسبة بين البابين أن كلاً . الاستسقاء والخوف من شرع لعارض يعني انقطا. اع المطر والجهاد وإضافة الصلاة إلى الخوف من إضافة الشيء إلى شرطه (فتح) إن اشتد الخوف إلخ: اشتداد الخوف ليس بشرط، عند عامة المشائخ، بل تجوز صلاة الخوف عند قرب العدو وغيره، خلافاً لأبي يوسف؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا كُنْتَ فِيهِمْ فَأَقَمْتَ لَهُمُ الصَّلاةَ (النساء:١٠٢) (الآية) شرط لإقامتها أن يكون عليه السلام معهم، ولنا أن الصحابة صلوها بعد النبي عليه السلام، ومعنى: ﴿وَإِذَا كُنتَ فِيهِمْ أنت أو من يقوم مقامك في الإمامة كما في قوله تعالى: خُذْ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِمْ صَدَقَةٌ تُطَهِّرُهُمْ وَتُزَكِّيهِمْ بها (التوبة: ١٠٣) وقد يكون الخطاب مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا يختص هو به كقوله تعالى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ إِذَا طَلَّقْتُمُ النساء لك (الطلاق: (١) وفي رواية عن أبي يوسف أنه يجعلهم صفين إذا كان العدو في جانب القبلة فيحرمون كلهم ويركعون، فإذا سجد سجد معه الصف الأول، والصف الثاني يحرسونهم من العدو، فإذا رفع رأسه تأخر الصف الأول، وتقدم الصف الثاني، فإذا سجد سجدوا معه، وهكذا يفعل في كل ركعة، وفي كيفية أدائها اختلافات كثيرة، والمختار عند علمائنا ما صرح به المصنف بقوله : وقف الإمام طائفة إلخ. (فتح) وصلى بطائفة: هذا إن طلب الكل الصلاة خلفه، فيفعل ما ذكر ، لقطع المنازعة عند قول كل طائفة منهم: نحن نصلي مع الإمام، وإذا لم يتنازعوا كان الأفضل أن يجعلهم طائفتين، فيصلي هو بطائفة، ويأمر رجلاً من الطائفة الأخرى أن يصلي بالأخرى. (فتح) ركعة واحدة إن كان مسافراً أو كان في الفجر. (ط) وركعتين: أي وصلى ركعتين لو كان مقيماً، فإذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية قامت هذه الطائفة التي وراءه. (ع) هذه: الطائفة التي صلّى بهم ركعة، أو ركعتين. (ع) إلى العدوّ أي إلى جهتهم، ووقفوا بإزائهم موضع الطائفة الأولى.(ع) تلك: أي الطائفة الذين كانوا تجاه العدو. رمز الحقائق ١٠٦/١] ما بقي من الصلاة وهو ركعة إن كان مسافرا، وركعتان إن كان مقيماً. (ط) وسلم: أي الإمام؛ لأنه لم يبق عليه شيء، ولا تسلم الطائفة التي وراءه بل قاموا. (ع) إليهم : أي إلى العدو ووقفوا تجاههم. (ع) الأولى التي صلت مع الإمام أولا إما ركعة، أو ركعتين. (ع) وأتموا صلاتهم بأن يصلوا إما ركعة أو ركعتين. (ط) ثم الأخرى: أي تجيء الطائفة الأخرى وهي الثانية. (ط)
Chapter of the Prayer of Fear (Salat al-Khawf): i.e., on explaining its rulings. When the fear becomes severe from an enemy or a wild beast, the imam stands with a group facing the enemy, and prays with a group — whether the enemy is or a huge snake and the like — meaning the people are two groups, one for guarding and defense, the other (prays) one rak'ah, and two rak'ahs if he is a resident. Then this (group) goes to the enemy, and that (other group) comes, and he prays with them what remains of the prayer and says the salam, and they go to them, and the first group comes and completes (their prayer) without recitation and says salam and goes; then the other (group) the imam — meaning the second group with him — complete their prayer because they are followers. (The first group i.e., to the enemy). Chapter of Salat al-Khawf: [It is prescribed in our time, contrary to Abu Yusuf, for he did not permit it after the Prophet (peace be upon him). (Ayni)] The connection between the two chapters is that each of istisqa and khawf is legislated for an incidental circumstance, meaning cessation of rain and jihad. And adding prayer to fear is adding a thing to its condition. (Fath) 'When the fear becomes severe' etc.: Severity of fear is not a condition according to the general mashayikh; rather, fear prayer is permitted at the approach of the enemy and otherwise, contrary to Abu Yusuf, due to His statement, the Exalted: 'And when you are among them and lead them in prayer' (al-Nisa':102) — the condition for establishing it is that he (peace be upon him) be with them. And for us (Hanafis), the Companions prayed it after the Prophet (peace be upon him). And the meaning of 'And when you are among them' is you or whoever stands in your place in imamate, as in His statement: 'Take from their wealth a charity by which you purify them and cause them increase' (al-Tawbah:103). And the address may be to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) but is not specific to him, as His statement: 'O Prophet, when you divorce women, divorce them' (al-Talaq:1). And in a narration from Abu Yusuf, he makes them two rows if the enemy is in the direction of the qibla, so they all enter ihram and bow; when he prostrates, the first row prostrates with him, and the second row guards them from the enemy. When he raises his head, the first row moves back, and the second row moves forward, and when he prostrates, they prostrate with him, and so on in every rak'ah. And there are many differences in the manner of performing it, and the chosen (mukhtar) among our scholars is what the author stated with his saying: 'the imam stands with a group,' etc. (Fath) 'And prays with a group': This is if all seek to pray behind him, he does what is mentioned to cut off dispute when each group says: we will pray with the imam. If they do not dispute, it is better to make them two groups: he prays with one group and instructs a man from the other group to pray with the other. (Fath) 'One rak'ah' if he is a traveler or in Fajr. (Tahawi) 'And two rak'ahs': i.e., he prays two rak'ahs if he is a resident. So when he raises his head from the second prostration, this group behind him stands. (Ayni) 'This': the group who prayed with him one rak'ah or two rak'ahs. (Ayni) 'To the enemy': i.e., to their direction, and they stand facing them in the place of the first group. (Ayni) 'That': i.e., the group who were facing the enemy. Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/106] 'What remains of the prayer': which is one rak'ah if he is a traveler, and two rak'ahs if he is a resident. (Tahawi) 'And he says salam': i.e., the imam, because nothing remains for him, and the group behind him do not say salam but stand. (Ayni) 'To them': i.e., to the enemy and stand facing them. (Ayni) 'The first': the one who prayed with the imam first, either one rak'ah or two rak'ahs. (Ayni) 'And they completed their prayer': by praying either one rak'ah or two rak'ahs. (Tahawi) 'Then the other': i.e., the other group, the second, comes. (Tahawi)
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage covers the chapter of Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer). It begins by noting a dispute: according to a narration from Abu Yusuf, the fear prayer was only valid during the Prophet's time, but the general Hanafi position, stated by the author, is that it remains prescribed. The commentator (Fath) explains the connection between the chapters (istisqa and khawf): both are for incidental needs (drought and jihad). The text then discusses the condition of 'severe fear' — the majority of mashayikh say severity is not a condition; rather, mere proximity of the enemy suffices, contrary to Abu Yusuf who reads the Quranic verse (al-Nisa':102) as requiring the Prophet's presence. The Hanafi response: the verse addresses the Prophet but applies to any imam (like 'take charity' applies to all leaders). The passage then describes the chosen method: the imam divides the army into two groups. He prays one rak'ah (if traveler or Fajr) or two (if resident) with the first group, who then go to face the enemy. The second group comes, the imam prays the remaining rak'ahs with them, and says salam. The second group then goes to the enemy, the first group returns and completes their prayer without recitation (as lāḥiqūn, followers who missed part) and says salam. This method is chosen to avoid dispute when both groups want to pray with the imam. If no dispute, it is better to appoint a subordinate imam for one group. The text also mentions Abu Yusuf's alternative method (two rows alternating sujud with guarding). The overall ruling is that fear prayer is valid with this rotating group method.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): The prayer performed during battle or when fear of an enemy or wild beast exists, with a specific method of dividing the congregation.
لاحقون (lāḥiqūn): Followers who missed part of the prayer with the imam; they complete on their own without recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen Hanafi method of salat al‑khawf, what does the first group do after praying one rak'ah (or two) with the imam?
A) They remain in prayer until the imam says salam.
B) They go to face the enemy, and later return to complete their prayer.
C) They become the imam's substitutes.
D) They leave the prayer and rejoin later.

Key Takeaway
The fear prayer (salat al-khawf) is a valid sunnah method for performing obligatory prayer in danger, using a rotating two-group format that ensures security while maintaining congregational prayer.

Salat al-Khawf: Is It Still Permissible After the Prophet?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on abrogation of fear prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the permissibility of Salat al-Khawf after the Prophet and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The fear prayer remains valid after the Prophet; the Quranic address is general, applying to all imams.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the special format of prayer under enemy threat (Salat al-Khawf) can still be performed after the lifetime of the Prophet (peace be upon him). While the majority of Hanafi scholars affirm its continuity, Imam Abu Yusuf initially held it was abrogated. We will examine the evidence from the Qur'an and the practice of the Companions, and see how the school resolved this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed matter
Pinpoint exactly what is being contested: the permissibility of performing Salat al-Khawf after the Prophet's time, not the prayer itself.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Note that the majority (including the author) hold that Salat al-Khawf is still legislated. This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's early view
Recognize that Abu Yusuf (rahimahullah) first held it was not permissible after the Prophet, citing the verse's specificity to the Prophet.
This is a minority view within the school.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
Study the counter-argument: the Qur'anic address includes all imams standing in the Prophet's place, as proven by similar verses (e.g., 9:103, 65:1) and the practice of the Companions.
5
Note the practical outcome
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: those following Abu Yusuf's first view cannot perform Salat al-Khawf; the majority allow it.
The later narration from Abu Yusuf permitting it with a different method shows the school's eventual consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الخوف: [وهي مشروعة في زماننا خلافاً لأبي يوسف، فإنه لم يجوزها بعد النبي عليه السلام] المناسبة بين البابين أن كلاً [؟] الاستسقاء والخوف من شرع لعارض يعني انقطاع المطر والجهاد وإضافة الصلاة إلى الخوف من إضافة الشيء إلى شرطه (فتح) إن اشتد الخوف إلخ: اشتداد الخوف ليس بشرط، عند عامة المشائخ، بل تجوز صلاة الخوف عند قرب العدو وغيره، خلافاً لأبي يوسف؛ لقوله تعالى: {وَإِذَا كُنْتَ فِيهِمْ فَأَقَمْتَ لَهُمُ الصَّلاةَ} (النساء:١٠٢) (الآية) شرط لإقامتها أن يكون عليه معهم، ولنا أن الصحابة صلوها بعد النبي عليه، ومعنى: {وَإِذَا كُنْتَ فِيهِمْ} أنت أو من يقوم مقامك في الإمامة كما في قوله تعالى: {خُذْ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِمْ صَدَقَةٌ تُطَهِّرُهُمْ وَتُزَكِّيهِمْ بِهَا} (التوبة: ١٠٣) وقد يكون الخطاب مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا يختص هو به كقوله تعالى: {يَا أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ إِذَا طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ} (الطلاق: ١) وفي رواية عن أبي يوسف أنه يجعلهم صفين إذا كان العدو في جانب القبلة فيحرمون كلهم ويركعون، فإذا سجد سجد معه الصف الأول، والصف الثاني يحرسونهم من العدو، فإذا رفع رأسه تأخر الصف الأول، وتقدم الصف الثاني، فإذا سجد سجدوا معه، وهكذا يفعل في كل ركعة، وفي كيفية أدائها اختلافات كثيرة، والمختار عند علمائنا ما صرح به المصنف بقوله : وقف الإمام طائفة إلخ.
Chapter on the prayer of fear: [It is legislated in our time contrary to Abu Yusuf, for he did not permit it after the Prophet (peace be upon him).] The connection between the two chapters is that each... the prayer for rain and the fear (prayer) are legislated for an emergency, meaning disruption of rain and jihad, and adding prayer to fear is from adding a thing to its condition. (Fath) 'If fear intensifies etc.': intensification of fear is not a condition according to the majority of the shaykhs, rather the prayer of fear is permissible when the enemy is near and other than that, contrary to Abu Yusuf; because of His saying: {And when you are among them and lead them in prayer} (al-Nisa 102) (the verse) makes it a condition that he be with them, and we have that the Companions prayed it after the Prophet, and the meaning of {And when you are among them} is you or whoever stands in your place in imamah, as in His saying: {Take from their wealth a charity to purify and sanctify them} (al-Tawba 103), and the address may be to the Messenger of Allah without being specific to him, like His saying: {O Prophet, when you divorce women} (al-Talaq 1). And in a narration from Abu Yusuf, that he makes them two rows if the enemy is in the direction of the qiblah, so they all enter ihram and bow, and when he prostrates, the first row prostrates with him, and the second row guards them from the enemy; when he raises his head, the first row moves back, and the second row moves forward, and when he prostrates, they prostrate with him, and thus they do in every rak'ah. And there are many differences in its methodology, and the chosen (view) according to our scholars is what the author clarified by his saying: 'The Imam stands with a group (ta'ifah) etc.'
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether Salat al-Khawf (fear prayer) can still be performed after the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The passage begins by stating the ruling of the majority of Hanafi scholars: it is still legislated. It then cites Abu Yusuf's first view that it is not permissible after the Prophet, and rejects it. The evidence for the Hanafi position is: (1) The Qur'anic verse (4:102) is addressed to the Prophet but applies to all imams who stand in his place, similar to the verse about zakah (9:103) and divorce (65:1). (2) The Companions performed it after the Prophet. The passage then mentions a second narration from Abu Yusuf where he allows the prayer but in a different manner: the imam divides the army into two rows facing the enemy in the qiblah direction. This shows that Abu Yusuf himself had two positions. The conclusion is that the chosen method in the Hanafi school is the one clearly stated by the author (Kanz al-Daqaiq) which follows in the next lesson. The commentary highlights that the difference is not about the obligation of prayer itself but about the permissibility of this specific format of the prayer under fear.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): The prayer performed under fear of the enemy during battle, with specific concessions in its form.
طائفة (ta'ifah): A group or detachment; in this context, one of the two divisions of the army praying with the imam.
إزاء (iza'): Opposite, facing; the position of one group facing the enemy while the other prays.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is not permissible; abrogated after the Prophet's time.
B) It is permissible, and the method described in Kanz al-Daqaiq is the chosen one.
C) It is permissible only if the enemy is in the qiblah direction.
D) It is permissible only for travelers.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows Salat al-Khawf after the Prophet, with the chosen method being the one described in Kanz al-Daqaiq.

Hanafi Method of Performing Salat al-Khawf
Detailed description of the imam's actions with two groups

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the steps of the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf, including the imam's prayer length and the role of the two groups.

Core Idea
In Salat al-Khawf, the imam prays his full prayer split between two groups, ensuring security while worshiping.

Salat al-Khawf (the prayer of fear) is a divine concession for prayers during battle. The Hanafi school prescribes a structured method where the imam leads the prayer in two parts with two rotating groups. This lesson unpacks the exact procedure from the classical text Kanz al-Daqaiq, clarifying the imam's actions and the completion of prayers by both groups.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial setup
The imam stands with one group while the other guards. If all want to pray behind one imam, he proceeds as described. If they do not dispute, it is better to appoint a second imam.
2
Determine the imam's prayer length
The imam's prayer length depends on his status: if he is a traveler or praying Fajr, he prays one rak'ah with the first group; if a resident, two rak'ahs.
3
First group's actions
After the imam completes the first portion with the first group (raising from second sajdah), this group leaves to face the enemy, replacing the guard.
4
Second group's turn and imam's taslim
The second group comes, the imam prays the remaining rak'ahs (one for traveler, two for resident) with them, then says the taslim. The second group does not say taslim but stands.
5
Completion by each group
The first group returns and prays their remaining rak'ahs alone. The second group also completes their missing rak'ahs (the first portion they missed) after the imam's taslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقف الإمام طائفة إلخ. (فتح) وصلى بطائفة: هذا إن طلب الكل الصلاة خلفه، فيفعل ما ذكر، لقطع المنازعة عند قول كل طائفة منهم: نحن نصلي مع الإمام، وإذا لم يتنازعوا كان الأفضل أن يجعلهم طائفتين، فيصلي هو بطائفة، ويأمر رجلاً من الطائفة الأخرى أن يصلي بالأخرى. (فتح) ركعة واحدة إن كان مسافراً أو كان في الفجر. (ط) وركعتين: أي وصلى ركعتين لو كان مقيماً، فإذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية قامت هذه الطائفة التي وراءه. (ع) هذه: الطائفة التي صلّى بهم ركعة، أو ركعتين. (ع) إلى العدوّ أي إلى جهتهم، ووقفوا بإزائهم موضع الطائفة الأولى.(ع) تلك: أي الطائفة الذين كانوا تجاه العدو. (رمز الحقائق ١٠٦/١) ما بقي من الصلاة وهو ركعة إن كان مسافرا، وركعتان إن كان مقيماً. (ط) وسلم: أي الإمام؛ لأنه لم يبق عليه شيء، ولا تسلم الطائفة التي وراءه بل قاموا. (ع) إليهم : أي إلى العدو ووقفوا تجاههم. (ع) الأولى التي صلت مع الإمام أولا إما ركعة، أو ركعتين. (ع) وأتموا صلاتهم بأن يصلوا إما ركعة أو ركعتين. (ط) ثم الأخرى: أي تجيء الطائفة الأخرى وهي الثانية. (ط)
The Imam stands with a group etc. (Fath) And he prays with a group: This is if all want to pray behind him, so he does what was mentioned to cut off dispute when each group says: we pray with the Imam. And if they do not dispute, it is better to make them two groups, so he prays with one group, and orders a man from the other group to pray with the other. (Fath) One rak'ah if he is a traveler or in the Fajr prayer. (T) And two rak'ahs: meaning he prays two rak'ahs if he is a resident, and when he raises his head from the second prostration, this group behind him stands. (A) 'This' : the group that he prayed with one or two rak'ahs. (A) 'to the enemy' meaning towards their direction, and they stand facing them in place of the first group. (A) 'those' : meaning the group that were facing the enemy. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/106) 'what remains of the prayer' which is one rak'ah if a traveler, two rak'ahs if a resident. (T) 'and he says the salaam' : meaning the Imam, because nothing remains upon him, and the group behind him does not say salaam but stands. (A) 'to them' : meaning to the enemy and they stand facing them. (A) 'the first' : the ones who prayed with the Imam first, either one or two rak'ahs. (A) 'and they complete their prayer' by praying either one or two rak'ahs. (T) 'then the other' : meaning the other group, which is the second, comes. (T)
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed Hanafi method for performing Salat al-Khawf as described in Kanz al-Daqaiq. The imam divides the army into two groups. He prays with one group: one rak'ah if a traveler or in Fajr, two rak'ahs if a resident. After completing his prayer with this group, they go to face the enemy, and the second group comes. The imam then prays the remaining rak'ahs with the second group and finishes with taslim. The first group then completes their prayer (the remaining rak'ahs) on their own. The passage notes that the second group does not say salaam with the imam but stands to complete their prayer later. This method is preferred to avoid disputes over who prays with the imam. If there is no dispute, the imam may delegate another to lead the second group.

Key Terms
إزاء العدو (iza' al-`aduww): Facing the enemy; the position of the group guarding while the other prays.
لاحقون (lahiqoon): Those who are latecomers to the prayer (followers) and complete their prayer after the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Salat al-Khawf, what is the imam's prayer length if he is a resident?
A) He prays one rak'ah with the first group and one rak'ah with the second.
B) He prays two rak'ahs with the first group and two with the second.
C) He prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one with the second.
D) He prays one rak'ah with the first group and two with the second.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf splits the imam's prayer equally between two groups, ensuring both security and congregation.

The Imam's Waiting in Salat al-Khawf: Hanafi Position vs. Maliki/Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab debate on whether the imam waits for the first group to complete

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether the imam waits in Salat al-Khawf, contrast it with the Maliki/Shafi'i view, and identify the key hadith evidence and the reasoning for tarjih.

Core Idea
The imam does not wait; the Hanafi view is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar and consistency with general prayer principles.

Salat al-Khawf (the prayer of fear) has specific procedures. One major point of disagreement among the schools is whether the imam should wait for the first group to complete their prayer before leading the second group. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling and the counterarguments from Malik and al-Shafi'i, focusing on the hadith evidence and the principles that guide the Hanafi preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Understand the scenario of Salat al-Khawf: the imam leads the first group in one rak'ah, then they go to the battlefront. The second group arrives. The core question is: should the imam wait for the first group to complete their remaining rak'ah before leading the second group?
This determines the sequence of the prayer.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school says the imam does not wait. After the first group leaves, the second group joins and the imam prays the remaining rak'ah with them, then says salaam. The first group completes their prayer later. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) acted this way.
The Hanafis also cite the general principle that the imam is not required to wait for latecomers.
3
Present the opposing view
Malik and al-Shafi'i hold that the imam waits. According to Malik, the imam waits for the first group to finish and say salaam before the second group joins. Al-Shafi'i adds that the imam delays his own salaam until the second group completes their missed rak'ah. Their proof is the hadith of Sahl ibn Abi Hathmah in the expedition of Dhat al-Riqa'.
Both schools rely on authentic narrations, leading to different procedural outcomes.
4
Analyze the Hanafi tarjih
The author of Al-Hidayah states that the Hanafi view is preferable because it agrees with the general principles (usul) of prayer. This includes the principle that the imam is not obligated to wait for latecomers, and that each person's prayer is individual.
This tarjih is based on methodological consistency, not on rejecting the opposing hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأتموا بقراءة: لأنهم مسبوقون والمسبوق يفرض عليه القراءة فيما سبق. وقال مالك: يصلي بالطائفة الأخرى وينتظر لتصلي الطائفة الأولى ما بقي لهم، وتسلم وتذهب إلى العدو، وجاءت الطائفة الثانية فيصلي بهم الركعة الثانية، ثم يسلم ويقومون لقضاء الركعة الأولى، وبه قال الشافعي، إلا أنه يقول: لا يسلم الإمام حتى تقضي الطائفة الثانية الركعة الأولى، ثم يسلم ويسلمون معه؛ لحديث سهل أنه عليها فعل كذلك في غزوة ذات الرقاع، ولنا: حديث ابن عمر لما أنه عليها فعل كما قلنا، والأخذ به أولى، لموافقته الأصول. (فتح)
And they complete with recitation: because they are preceded (masbuqoon) and the preceded one is obliged to recite what was missed. Malik said: He prays with the other group and waits for the first group to complete what remains for them, then they say salaam and go to the enemy, then the second group comes, and he prays with them the second rak'ah, then he says salaam and they stand to make up the first rak'ah. Al-Shafi'i also said that, except he says: The imam does not say salaam until the second group makes up the first rak'ah, then he says salaam and they say salaam with him; based on the hadith of Sahl that he (peace be upon him) did thus in the expedition of Dhat al-Riqa'. And we have (as proof) the hadith of Ibn Umar that he (peace be upon him) did as we said, and acting upon it is better, because it agrees with the principles. (Fath)
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the details of how the imam handles the two groups in Salat al-Khawf. The Hanafi position, based on the practice of Ibn Umar, states that the imam does not wait; after the first group goes to the enemy and the second comes, he prays the remainder and says salaam, and the second group completes on their own. The recitation of the missed part is upon the masbuq. In contrast, Malik and Shafi'i follow a narration from Sahl (ibn Abi Hathmah) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) in Dhat al-Riqa' waited for the first group to finish and say salaam. Shafi'i adds that the imam delays his salaam until the second group makes up their missed rak'ah. The Hanafi rebuttal is that the hadith of Ibn Umar is more consistent with the general principles (usul) of prayer, such as the imam not being obligated to wait for latecomers. This difference affects the actual sequence and the time of the imam's taslim.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): One who missed part of the prayer and joins late; here refers to those who complete prayer after the imam.
صلاة الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): The prayer of fear, performed in times of danger or battle, with specific procedures for splitting the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does the imam wait for the first group to complete their prayer before starting with the second group?
A) Yes, he waits until they finish and say salaam.
B) No, he proceeds immediately with the second group after the first group leaves.
C) He waits only if the enemy is in the qiblah direction.
D) He delegates another imam to avoid waiting.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the imam does not wait for the first group in Salat al-Khawf, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar and the principle that the imam is not obligated to wait for latecomers.
