Fighting During Prayer Invalidates It: Hanafi Proof and Dispute
Ruling on fighting in prayer with inter-madhhab proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that fighting invalidates prayer, explain the Hanafi proof from the Prophet's delay at Khandaq, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the command to carry weapons.

Core Idea
Fighting during prayer invalidates it because it is 'amal kathir; the Prophet's delay at Khandaq proves it is not permissible.

This passage addresses the critical question: does fighting during Salat al-Khawf invalidate the prayer? The Hanafi school firmly states that it does, because fighting constitutes many external actions that break the prayer. The passage provides the Prophet's practice at the Battle of the Trench as evidence and refutes the Shafi'i/Maliki reliance on the Qur'anic command to carry weapons. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi insistence on maintaining the sanctity of prayer even in battle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its basis
The text says 'وَمَنْ قَاتَلَ بَطَلَتْ صَلَاتُهُ' and explains the basis: fighting is 'عمل كثير' (many actions). Note that any large number of external actions invalidates prayer.
The principle of 'amal kathir is central to Hanafi fiqh of prayer.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Prophet (ﷺ) delayed four prayers on the day of Khandaq. If fighting were permissible during prayer, he would have prayed while fighting. His delay proves it is not allowed.
This is a strong dalil naqli from the Prophet's action.
3
Analyze the counter-argument
Shafi'i and Malik argue from Qur'an 4:102 that carrying weapons in prayer implies permission to fight. The Hanafi response: the command is for protection, not active combat, and carrying weapons is mustahabb, not wajib, because it is not part of prayer's actions.
The Hanafi usul principle: 'amr carries obligation, but context can shift it to nadb.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafi: fighting invalidates prayer, so one must repeat it. Shafi'i/Malik: if necessary, prayer remains valid. The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi).
The disagreement has real impact on the worshipper's duty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلّى في المغرب بالأولى ركعتين وبالثانية ركعة، ومن قاتل بطلت صلاته، وإن اشتد الخوف صلوا ركباناً فرادى بالإيماء إلى أي جهة قدروا، ولم تجز بلا حضور عدو. أي الإمام أي في صلاته أي بالطائفة الأولى فلو عكس فسدت صلاة الكل من المصلين بعمل كثير بطلت صلاته الأن المشي والقتال عمل كثير، وقال الشافعي: إن احتاج إليه لا تبطل. (رمز الحقائق: ١٠٦/١)] لأن النبي عليه شغل عن أربع صلوات يوم الخندق، ولو جاز الأداء مع القتال لما تركها. كشف الحقائق: ۸۸/۱] فإن قيل: إنما أخرها؛ لأن آية صلاة الخوف لم تكن نزلت لانعدام مشروعية الصلاة مع القتال، قلنا: آية صلاة الخوف نزلت بذات الرقاع وهي قبل الخندق (مستخلص) وقال في "فتح المعين": إن مشروعيتها في ذات الرقاع قبل الخندق وهم، بل هي إنما شرعت في الصحيح بعد الخندق، ولا تبطل الصلاة عند الشافعي ومالك بناء على أن الأمر بأخذ السلاح في قوله تعالى: {وَلْيَأْخُذُوا أَسْلِحَتَهُمْ} (النساء:١٠٢) يفيد جواز القتال في الصلاة، ولنا: ما روينا من تأخير الصلوات يوم الخندق وفائدة الأمر بأخذ الأسلحة إباحة قتال المفسد، فأفادت حله بعد أن كان حراماً، وحمل السلاح في الصلاة عند الخوف مستحب عندنا وليس بواجب، خلافاً للشافعي ومالك عملا بظاهر قوله تعالى المذكور، قلنا: هو محمول على الندب؛ لأن حملها ليس من أعمالها فلا يجب فيها. وإن اشتد الخوف جداً ابتداء، ولم يمكنهم الصلاة مع الجماعة. (ع) صلوا ركباناً: قيد به للاحتراز عما لو صلوا مشاة حال افتتاحها حيث لا يصح؛ لفسادها، وقيد بالفرادي؛ لأنها لا تجوز بجماعة؛ لعدم الاتحاد في المكان، إلا إذا كان راكباً مع الإمام على دابة واحدة، فإنه يجوز اقتداء المتأخر منهما بالمتقدم اتفاقاً وفرادى جمع فرد على غير قياس. (فتح) فرادى أي منفردين، وعن محمد لهم أن يصلوا ركباناً بجماعة. (ع) بالإيماء متعلق "بصلوا" أي مستقبلين القبلة، وإن عجزوا عن التوجه إلى القبلة صلوا إلى أي جهة إلخ. (ع) بلا حضور عدو أي مقابلتهم بطريق الحقيقة، وأما إذا كان ببعد منهم فلا تجوز، ولو شرعوا فيها والعدو حاضر ثم ذهب لا يجوز لهم الانحراف؛ لزوال سبب الرخصة، وبعكسه لو شرعوا فيها ثم حضر العدو جاز لهم الانحراف في أوانه لوجود الضرورة. (فتح، مسكين) عدو: لعدم الضرورة حقيقة، حتى لو رأوا سواداً فظنوه عدواً، فصلوها ثم بان بخلافه أعادوها. (ط،ع)
And he prayed in Maghrib with the first (group) two rak'ahs and with the second one rak'ah. And whoever fights, his prayer becomes invalid. And if fear intensifies, they pray on horseback, individually, with gestures in whatever direction they are able, and it is not permissible without the presence of an enemy. (Meaning the Imam, in his prayer, with the first group; if he reversed, the prayer of all the worshippers would become corrupt due to many actions). 'His prayer becomes invalid' because walking and fighting are many actions. Al-Shafi'i said: If he needs to fight, it does not invalidate. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/106) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was occupied with four prayers on the day of the Khandaq (Trench), and if performing prayer with fighting were permissible, he would not have left them. (Kashf al-Haqa'iq 1/88) If it is said: He only delayed them because the verse of Salat al-Khawf had not been revealed, due to the absence of legislation of prayer with fighting, we say: The verse of Salat al-Khawf was revealed in Dhat al-Riqa', which was before Khandaq. And it is said in 'Fath al-Mu'in': That it was legislated in Dhat al-Riqa' before Khandaq is a mistake; rather it was legislated after Khandaq according to the correct view. And prayer is not invalidated according to al-Shafi'i and Malik based on the command to take weapons in His saying: {And let them take their weapons} (al-Nisa' 102) which indicates the permissibility of fighting during prayer. And we have: what we narrated about the delay of prayers on the day of Khandaq, and the benefit of the command to take weapons is to permit fighting against a corruptor, so it indicates that it becomes permissible after being forbidden. And carrying weapons in prayer during fear is recommended (mustahabb) according to us, not obligatory, contrary to al-Shafi'i and Malik acting upon the apparent meaning of the aforementioned verse. We say: It is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) because carrying (weapons) is not from the actions of prayer, so it is not obligatory. And if fear becomes extremely intense initially, and they cannot pray with the congregation, they pray on horseback (rukbanan): a restriction to avoid what if they pray on foot at the start, for it would be invalid because of its corruption, and restricted to individually (furada) because it is not permissible in congregation due to lack of unity in place, except if one is on a mount with the imam on the same animal, for then following of the one behind the one ahead is permissible by agreement. (Fath) 'Individually' means alone, and from Muhammad: they may pray on horseback in congregation. (A) 'with gestures' is related to 'they pray' meaning facing the qiblah, and if they are unable to face the qiblah, they pray in whatever direction etc. (A) 'without the presence of an enemy' meaning actually facing them; but if they are far away, it is not permissible. And if they start the prayer while the enemy is present, then the enemy disappears, it is not permissible for them to deviate, because the reason for the concession has ceased; and conversely, if they start the prayer and then the enemy appears, it is permissible for them to deviate at that time due to the need. (Fath, Miskin) 'Enemy': because there is no real need; even if they see a black mass and think it is an enemy, and pray (the fear prayer), then it becomes clear otherwise, they must repeat it. (T, A)
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage covers two additional rulings related to Salat al-Khawf. First, it states that if a person fights (engages in combat) during prayer, the prayer becomes invalid because fighting involves many external actions (amal kathir) that break the prayer. The text refutes the Shafi'i view that fighting does not invalidate if necessary, using the evidence that the Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed prayers on the day of the Trench (Khandaq) rather than praying while fighting. A counter-argument that the verse of Salat al-Khawf was not yet revealed is rebutted by noting that the verse was in fact revealed before Khandaq (at Dhat al-Riqa'). The text also clarifies that carrying weapons in prayer is recommended (mustahabb) in Hanafi view, not obligatory as some others hold, because carrying weapons is not part of the prayer's actions. The second ruling covers extreme fear where even the basic form of Salat al-Khawf is not possible. In such a case, individuals pray on horseback (or other mounts) individually, making gestures (ima') for bowing and prostration, and they may face any direction. This is not permissible if there is no actual enemy present; if they mistakenly think there is an enemy but then find out otherwise, they must repeat the prayer. The passage also notes a condition: if they start prayer without fear and then fear arises, they may deviate; but if fear ends during prayer, they must return to the normal form.

Key Terms
عمل كثير (amal kathir): Many actions; a large number of movements external to prayer that invalidate it.
قتال (qital): Fighting or combat during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what evidence is used to prove that fighting invalidates prayer?
A) The Prophet's command to carry weapons.
B) The Prophet's delay of prayers at Khandaq.
C) The Qur'anic verse on Salat al-Khawf.
D) Consensus of all scholars.

Key Takeaway
Fighting during prayer invalidates it because it involves many external actions, as proven by the Prophet's delay at Khandaq.

Extreme Fear Prayer: Praying on Mounts with Gestures
Extreme fear prayer: conditions and form

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the form of prayer in extreme fear (praying on mounts individually with gestures), identify its conditions, and apply the ruling when fear intensifies or subsides.

Core Idea
In extreme fear, one prays individually on a mount with gestures, but only if an enemy is actually present.

This passage explains the extreme form of Salat al-Khawf when fear is so intense that even the usual congregational form is impossible. The Hanafi school permits praying on horseback (or any mount) individually, making gestures for bowing and prostration, and facing any direction if unable to face the qiblah. However, this concession is only valid when an enemy is truly present; if the fear is based on a misperception, the prayer must be repeated. The passage also addresses the conditions under which one may deviate from the qiblah and when praying in congregation is allowed on a single mount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
The ruling: pray on mounts individually with gestures (ima'). Conditions: extremely intense fear, inability to pray with congregation, and actual presence of an enemy.
The concession is rukhsah; it is only valid when the need is genuine.
2
Analyze the restriction: why individually and not on foot
The text says 'furdan' (individually) because congregation requires unity of place; on mounts, it's not possible unless two share the same animal. It also prohibits starting on foot because that would corrupt the prayer.
Imam Muhammad allowed congregation on a single mount, but the relied-upon position is individually.
3
Examine the scope of concession: direction and enemy presence
If able, face qiblah; if not, any direction. The enemy must be actually present (in close proximity); if mistaken, prayer must be repeated.
The presence must be actual; a misperception invalidates the concession.
4
Note the change of status during prayer
If fear disappears during prayer, one must return to normal form; if fear appears after starting, one may deviate.
The concession is temporary and ceases when the need ends.

And he prayed in Maghrib with the first (group) two rak'ahs and with the second one rak'ah. And whoever fights, his prayer becomes invalid. And if fear intensifies, they pray on horseback, individually, with gestures in whatever direction they are able, and it is not permissible without the presence of an enemy. (Meaning the Imam, in his prayer, with the first group; if he reversed, the prayer of all the worshippers would become corrupt due to many actions). 'His prayer becomes invalid' because walking and fighting are many actions. Al-Shafi'i said: If he needs to fight, it does not invalidate. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/106) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was occupied with four prayers on the day of the Khandaq (Trench), and if performing prayer with fighting were permissible, he would not have left them. (Kashf al-Haqa'iq 1/88) If it is said: He only delayed them because the verse of Salat al-Khawf had not been revealed, due to the absence of legislation of prayer with fighting, we say: The verse of Salat al-Khawf was revealed in Dhat al-Riqa', which was before Khandaq. And it is said in 'Fath al-Mu'in': That it was legislated in Dhat al-Riqa' before Khandaq is a mistake; rather it was legislated after Khandaq according to the correct view. And prayer is not invalidated according to al-Shafi'i and Malik based on the command to take weapons in His saying: {And let them take their weapons} (al-Nisa' 102) which indicates the permissibility of fighting during prayer. And we have: what we narrated about the delay of prayers on the day of Khandaq, and the benefit of the command to take weapons is to permit fighting against a corruptor, so it indicates that it becomes permissible after being forbidden. And carrying weapons in prayer during fear is recommended (mustahabb) according to us, not obligatory, contrary to al-Shafi'i and Malik acting upon the apparent meaning of the aforementioned verse. We say: It is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) because carrying (weapons) is not from the actions of prayer, so it is not obligatory. And if fear becomes extremely intense initially, and they cannot pray with the congregation, they pray on horseback (rukbanan): a restriction to avoid what if they pray on foot at the start, for it would be invalid because of its corruption, and restricted to individually (furada) because it is not permissible in congregation due to lack of unity in place, except if one is on a mount with the imam on the same animal, for then following of the one behind the one ahead is permissible by agreement. (Fath) 'Individually' means alone, and from Muhammad: they may pray on horseback in congregation. (A) 'with gestures' is related to 'they pray' meaning facing the qiblah, and if they are unable to face the qiblah, they pray in whatever direction etc. (A) 'without the presence of an enemy' meaning actually facing them; but if they are far away, it is not permissible. And if they start the prayer while the enemy is present, then the enemy disappears, it is not permissible for them to deviate, because the reason for the concession has ceased; and conversely, if they start the prayer and then the enemy appears, it is permissible for them to deviate at that time due to the need. (Fath, Miskin) 'Enemy': because there is no real need; even if they see a black mass and think it is an enemy, and pray (the fear prayer), then it becomes clear otherwise, they must repeat it. (T, A)
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage covers two additional rulings related to Salat al-Khawf. First, it states that if a person fights (engages in combat) during prayer, the prayer becomes invalid because fighting involves many external actions (amal kathir) that break the prayer. The text refutes the Shafi'i view that fighting does not invalidate if necessary, using the evidence that the Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed prayers on the day of the Trench (Khandaq) rather than praying while fighting. A counter-argument that the verse of Salat al-Khawf was not yet revealed is rebutted by noting that the verse was in fact revealed before Khandaq (at Dhat al-Riqa'). The text also clarifies that carrying weapons in prayer is recommended (mustahabb) in Hanafi view, not obligatory as some others hold, because carrying weapons is not part of the prayer's actions. The second ruling covers extreme fear where even the basic form of Salat al-Khawf is not possible. In such a case, individuals pray on horseback (or other mounts) individually, making gestures (ima') for bowing and prostration, and they may face any direction. This is not permissible if there is no actual enemy present; if they mistakenly think there is an enemy but then find out otherwise, they must repeat the prayer. The passage also notes a condition: if they start prayer without fear and then fear arises, they may deviate; but if fear ends during prayer, they must return to the normal form.

Key Terms
ركبان (rukban): Riders on mounts; praying on riding animals when dismounting is not possible due to fear.
إيماء (ima'): Gestures; replacing bowing and prostration with head movements when unable to perform full movements.
فرادى (furada): Individually; each person prays alone, not in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for the extreme fear prayer according to Hanafi?
A) Praying in congregation.
B) Facing the enemy.
C) Actual presence of the enemy.
D) Praying on the ground.

Key Takeaway
Extreme fear prayer is a concession requiring actual enemy presence; it is performed individually on a mount with gestures, and the form adjusts if fear ceases or appears.

Fighting During Fear Prayer: Hanafi Position and Proof
Detailed rulings and inter-madhhab dispute on fear prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of leading Salat al-Khawf and explain why fighting invalidates the prayer based on the dalil of Khandaq.

Core Idea
Fighting during fear prayer invalidates it because the Prophet delayed prayers rather than combine them.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the rulings of Salat al-Khawf and a key inter-madhhab dispute: Does fighting during the prayer invalidate it? The Hanafi school insists it does, based on the Prophet's practice during the Battle of Khandaq, while Shafi'i and Malik permit it under necessity. Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi usul in prioritizing an established Sunnah over a general textual command.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school holds regarding the method of leading Salat al-Khawf and the effect of fighting during the prayer.
The imam leads the first group in two rak'ahs and the second in one for Maghrib; fighting invalidates the remainder of the prayer.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Determine which school(s) disagree and what they hold concerning fighting and the method.
Al-Shafi'i and Malik hold that fighting does not invalidate if necessary, and they have a different method based on the hadith of Sahl.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the evidence cited by the opposing school: the hadith of Sahl from Dhat al-Riqa' and the verse commanding to take weapons (al-Nisa' 102).
They interpret the verse as permitting fighting during prayer.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school rebuts the opponent's dalil using the hadith of Ibn Umar and the delay of prayers at Khandaq.
The verse is about carrying weapons, not fighting; the Khandaq hadith is definitive proof that fighting and prayer cannot be combined.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference between the positions in real-world application.
Hanafi: if a soldier fights, his prayer is batil. Shafi'i/Malik: it remains valid if necessary.

Source Text

للضرورة أي صلاة الخوف
وأتموا بقراءة: لأنهم مسبوقون والمسبوق يفرض عليه القراءة فيما سبق. وقال مالك: يصلي بالطائفة الأخرى وينتظر لتصلي الطائفة الأولى ما بقي لهم، وتسلم وتذهب إلى العدو، وجاءت الطائفة الثانية فيصلي بهم الركعة الثانية، ثم يسلم ويقومون لقضاء الركعة الأولى، وبه قال الشافعي، إلا أنه يقول: لا يسلم الإمام حتى تقضي الطائفة الثانية الركعة الأولى، ثم يسلم ويسلمون معه؛ لحديث سهل أنه عليها فعل كذلك في غزوة ذات الرقاع، ولنا: حديث ابن عمر لما أنه عليها فعل كما قلنا، والأخذ به أولى، لموافقته الأصول. (فتح) بالأولى ركعتين: لأن تنصيف الركعة الواحدة غير ممكن فجعلناها في الأول، وهو أولى بحكم السبق، وقال الثوري بالعكس؛ لأن فرض القراءة في الركعتين الأوليين فينبغي أن يكون لكل طائفة في ذلك حظ. (مستخلص) بطلت صلاته الأن المشي والقتال عمل كثير، وقال الشافعي: إن احتاج إليه لا تبطل. (رمز الحقائق: ١٠٦/١)] لأن النبي عليه شغل عن أربع صلوات يوم الخندق، ولو جاز الأداء مع القتال لما تركها. كشف الحقائق: ۸۸/۱] فإن قيل: إنما أخرها؛ لأن آية صلاة الخوف لم تكن نزلت لانعدام مشروعية الصلاة مع القتال، قلنا: آية صلاة الخوف نزلت بذات الرقاع وهي قبل الخندق (مستخلص) وقال في "فتح المعين": إن مشروعيتها في ذات الرقاع قبل الخندق وهم، بل هي إنما شرعت في الصحيح بعد الخندق، ولا تبطل الصلاة عند الشافعي ومالك بناء على أن الأمر بأخذ السلاح في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلْيَأْخُذُوا أَسْلِحَتَهُمْ ﴾ (النساء:١٠٢) يفيد جواز القتال في الصلاة، ولنا: ما روينا من تأخير الصلوات يوم الخندق وفائدة الأمر بأخذ الأسلحة إباحة قتال المفسد، فأفادت حله بعد أن كان حراماً، وحمل السلاح في الصلاة عند الخوف مستحب عندنا وليس بواجب، خلافاً للشافعي ومالك عملا بظاهر قوله تعالى المذكور، قلنا: هو محمول على الندب؛ لأن حملها ليس من أعمالها فلا يجب فيها.
وإن اشتد الخوف جداً ابتداء، ولم يمكنهم الصلاة . مع الجماعة. (ع) صلوا ركباناً: قيد به للاحتراز عما لو صلوا مشاة حال افتتاحها حيث لا يصح؛ لفسادها، وقيد بالفرادي؛ لأنها لا تجوز بجماعة؛ لعدم الاتحاد في المكان، إلا إذا كان راكباً مع الإمام على دابة واحدة، فإنه يجوز اقتداء المتأخر منهما بالمتقدم اتفاقاً وفرادى جمع فرد على غير قياس. (ع) بلا حضور عدو أي مقابلتهم بطريق الحقيقة، وأما إذا كان ببعد منهم فلا تجوز، ولو شرعوا فيها والعدو حاضر ثم ذهب لا يجوز لهم الانحراف؛ لزوال سبب الرخصة، وبعكسه لو شرعوا فيها ثم حضر العدو جاز لهم الانحراف في أوانه لوجود الضرورة. (فتح، مسكين)

Chapter of Fear Prayer. He [the imam] completed with recitation, and he prayed in Maghrib with the first [group] two rak'ahs and with the second one rak'ah. Whoever fights, the remainder of their prayer is invalidated. Meaning: the imam, in his prayer, with the first group. If he reversed, the prayer of all the worshippers would be invalidated due to excessive action. His prayer [is invalidated], and if fear intensifies, they pray as riders individually by gesture towards any direction they are able, and it is not permissible without the presence of an enemy. [Commentary: "collected" meaning rider, a state; "by necessity" meaning the fear prayer. "They complete with recitation" because they are those who are preceded, and the one preceded is required to recite what preceded. Malik said: He prays with the other group and waits for the first group to pray what remains for them, then they say salam and go to the enemy; the second group comes and he prays with them the second rak'ah, then he says salam and they stand to make up the first rak'ah. This is also held by al-Shafi'i, except that he says: The imam does not say salam until the second group completes the first rak'ah, then he says salam and they say salam with him, based on the hadith of Sahl that he (peace be upon him) did so in the Ghazwah of Dhat al-Riqa'. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar that he (peace be upon him) did as we say, and adopting it is more appropriate because it agrees with principles. (Fath) "Two rak'ahs with the first" because dividing a single rak'ah is not possible, so we placed it with the first, and it takes precedence by the rule of precedence. Al-Thawri said the opposite, because recitation is obligatory in the first two rak'ahs, so each group should have a share in that. (Mustakhlas) "His prayer is invalidated" because walking and fighting are excessive actions. Al-Shafi'i said: If he needs it, it is not invalidated. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 1/106) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was occupied with four prayers on the day of Khandaq, and if performing with fighting were permissible, he would not have left them. (Kashf al-Haqaiq 88/1) If it is said: He only delayed them because the verse of fear prayer had not been revealed due to the lack of legislation of prayer with fighting, we say: The verse of fear prayer was revealed at Dhat al-Riqa', and that was before Khandaq. (Mustakhlas) And he said in Fath al-Mu'in: The claim that it was legislated at Dhat al-Riqa' before Khandaq is a mistake; rather it was only legislated in the correct view after Khandaq. The prayer is not invalidated according to al-Shafi'i and Malik based on the command to take weapons in His statement: "And let them take their weapons" (al-Nisa' 102), which indicates the permissibility of fighting during prayer. Our proof is what we narrated of the delay of prayers on the day of Khandaq. The benefit of the command to take weapons is to permit fighting against the corrupt person, so it indicates its permissibility after it was prohibited. Carrying weapons in prayer during fear is recommended for us, not obligatory, contrary to al-Shafi'i and Malik acting on the apparent meaning of the aforementioned verse. We say: It is interpreted as recommendation, because carrying weapons is not part of its actions, so it is not obligatory therein. And if fear becomes very intense from the beginning, and they are unable to pray with the congregation, they pray as riders: constrained to that to avoid the case where they pray as pedestrians at the start, which would not be valid due to its invalidity. Constrained to individually because it is not permissible with congregation due to the lack of unity of place, except if the rider is with the imam on one animal, then the later one following the earlier is permissible by agreement. "Individually" is a plural of 'fard' irregularly. (Fath) "Individually" meaning separate. From Muhammad: They may pray as riders in congregation. (Ayn) "By gesture" connected to "they pray", meaning facing the qibla, and if unable to face the qibla, they pray towards any direction etc. (Ayn) "Without the presence of an enemy" meaning facing them in reality. But if they are distant from them, it is not permissible. And if they started it with the enemy present and then the enemy left, it is not permissible for them to deviate because the reason for the concession has ceased. Conversely, if they started it and then the enemy appeared, it is permissible for them to deviate at its time due to the existence of necessity. (Fath, Miskin) "Enemy": because there is no necessity in reality, so if they saw a dark mass and thought it was an enemy, and prayed it, then it turned out to be otherwise, they repeat it. (T, Ayn)
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq covers the rulings of Salat al-Khawf (Prayer of Fear) during battle. The matn states that the imam completes the prayer with recitation for the first group (they are preceded), and for Maghrib he leads the first group in two rak'ahs and the second group in one rak'ah. If the order is reversed, the prayer of all is invalidated because it constitutes excessive action (amal kathir). If a person fights during the prayer, the remainder of his prayer is invalidated. If fear becomes intense, they may pray as riders, individually, by gesture (ima') towards any direction they are able, but this is only valid if the enemy is actually present. The commentary then elaborates on these rulings and presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that fighting invalidates the prayer, based on the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed four prayers on the day of Khandaq; if fighting and prayer could be combined, he would not have delayed. The opponents (al-Shafi'i and Malik) argue that the verse 'and let them take their weapons' permits fighting during prayer, and they cite the hadith of Sahl from Dhat al-Riqa' concerning the method of leading. The Hanafi response distinguishes that the verse is about carrying weapons, not fighting, and that carrying weapons is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. The hadith of Ibn Umar is preferred over that of Sahl because it agrees with fundamental principles. The passage further clarifies that if the enemy is far away, the prayer of fear is not valid, and if the enemy disappears after the prayer begins, deviation from the original method is not permitted as the concession is lifted.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): A specific form of prayer performed during battle or intense fear, with a modified method as described in the text.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesture with the head or body to replace the normal bowing and prostration during prayer when unable to perform them fully, as in extreme fear.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A person who joins the prayer late and catches less than a full rak'ah with the imam; in fear prayer, the second group is considered masbuq.
عمل كثير (amal kathir): Excessive action that invalidates the prayer, such as walking or fighting; the threshold is actions that contradict the nature of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the evidence that fighting invalidates Salat al-Khawf?
A) The verse 'Let them take their weapons' (al-Nisa' 102).
B) The hadith that the Prophet delayed four prayers on the day of Khandaq.
C) The hadith of Sahl from Ghazwah Dhat al-Riqa'.
D) The consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that fighting invalidates Salat al-Khawf based on the definitive proof of the Prophet's delay of prayers on the day of Khandaq, prioritized over the general command to carry weapons.

Immediate Rulings on Preparing the Deceased
Rulings on preparing the deceased body before burial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on closing the eyes, fumigation, covering private parts, stripping, and talqeen, and identify the proofs and inter-madhhab disagreements.

Core Idea
Preparing the deceased: sunnah of odd-numbered fumigation, wajib of covering awrah, and no talqeen after burial.

This passage from the chapter of funerals outlines the immediate actions after death according to the Hanafi school. You will learn the rulings for closing the eyes, fumigating the bed, covering the private parts, stripping the body, and the disputed practice of talqeen (prompting the shahada). The text also clarifies the Hanafi position against the Shafi'i school on these matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
List each action mentioned: closing eyes, fumigation, placement on a bed, covering private parts, stripping, and talqeen. Determine the hukm level (sunnah, wajib, etc.) for each.
Note that covering private parts is wajib; others are sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the specific hadith cited for fumigation ('Allah is odd and loves odd') and for covering private parts ('Do not look at the thigh of a living person nor a dead person').
Also note the hadith for talqeen cited by Shafi'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each hadith proves the ruling: odd numbers are loved, so fumigation in odd numbers is sunnah; prohibition of looking implies obligation to cover.
For talqeen, the Hanafi interpretation reinterprets 'موتاكم' as those near death.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify that Imam al-Shafi'i differs on talqeen (prompts after burial) and on stripping (washes in a shirt). State their proofs.
Also note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on extent of awrah (major parts vs navel-to-knee).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi position is preferred: the text states that covering from navel to knee is correct, and talqeen after burial is not done based on the apparent narration.
The mufta bihi is covering from navel to knee and no talqeen after burial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجنائز
كيفية تجهيز الميت
الحياة، وغمض عيناه، ووضعَ على سرير مجمّر وترا، وستر عورته، وجرد، ووضئ
تلقين الميت في القبر مشروع عند أهل السنة؛ لأن الله تعالى يحييه في القبر، وقال الشافعي يلقن بعد الموت؛ لظاهر قوله عليه: "لقنوا موتاكم شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله" وعندنا في ظاهر الرواية: لا يلقن والمراد بموتاكم في الحديث من قرب من الموت كما في "اقرؤوها على موتاكم". تتمة: إذا مات المسلم تمد أعضاؤه ويوضع السيف أو المرآة على بطنه، وتوضع يده اليمنى في الجانب الأيمن واليسرى في الأيسر، ولا يجوز وضع اليدين على صدر الميت كما تفعله الكفرة؛ لأنه عليه أمر بالوضع في الجانب ولا بأس بإعلام الناس بموته؛ لأن فيه تكثير الجماعة من المصلين عليه والمستغفرين له بشرط أن لا يكون مع تنويه بذكره وتفخيم. وغمض عيناه: تحسيناً له، ويوضع على بطنه حديدة؛ لئلا ينتفخ، كذا روي عن الشعبي. على سرير: وهو الذي يغسله عليه، فإن لم يوجد فعلى لوح أو حجر مرتفع ليمكن غسله وتقليبه. مجمر: أي مبخر بعود ونحوه ؛ لإزالة الرائحة الكريهة. وترا صفة مصدر محذوف أي تجميراً وتراً، والتجمير والإجمار: التطيب بأن يطاف بالمجمر حوالي السرير مرة أو ثلاثاً أو خمساً؛ لقوله عليه: "إن الله وتر يحب الوتر". وستر عورته لأن سترها واجب والنظر إليها حرام كعورة الحي، ويستر ما بين سرته إلى ركبته بشد الإزار عليه، هو الصحيح " كما في حالة الحياة؛ ولقوله عليها لعلي: "لا تنظر إلى فخذ حي ولا ميت" ولا فرق بين الرجل والمرأة؛ لأن عورة المرأة للمرأة كالرجل للرجل. عورته الغليظة في ظاهر الرواية، وفي النوادر يستر من السرّة إلى الركبة وهو الصحيح، ثم إذا سترها لف الغاسل على يديه خرقة وغسلها. وجرد أي من الثياب ليمكنهم التنظيف، وقال الشافعي: يغسل في قميصه؛ لأنه عليها غسل في قميصه، ونحن اعتبرناه بحالة الحياة، وما رواه كان مخصوصاً به عليه، وقالوا: يجرد كما مات؛ لئلا يسرع إليه التغير بحرارة الثياب.
Chapter of Funerals. How to prepare the deceased: (He is alive) and (the one present) closes his eyes, and he is placed on a fumigated bed in odd numbers, and his private parts are covered, and he is stripped, and he is given wudu. The talqeen (prompting) of the deceased in the grave is legislated according to Ahl al-Sunnah, because Allah gives him life in the grave. Al-Shafi'i said: He is prompted after death, due to the apparent meaning of his ﷺ words: 'Prompt your dying ones with the testimony that there is no god but Allah.' According to us in the apparent narration: He is not prompted, and the meaning of 'your dying ones' in the hadith is those who are near death, as in 'Recite (Surah Ya-Sin) upon your dying ones.' Supplement: When a Muslim dies, his limbs are extended, a sword or mirror is placed on his stomach, his right hand is placed on the right side and left on the left side, and it is not permissible to place the hands on the chest of the deceased as the disbelievers do, because he ﷺ commanded placement on the side. There is no harm in informing people of his death, because it increases the congregation of those praying for him and seeking forgiveness for him, provided that it is not accompanied by personal praise and glorification. 'And closes his eyes': for beautification, and a piece of iron is placed on his stomach so that it does not swell; thus it is narrated from al-Sha'bi. 'On a bed': that is, the bed on which he is washed; if not found, then on a board or elevated stone to enable washing and turning. 'Fumigated': that is, perfumed with incense or similar to remove bad odor. 'In odd numbers': adjective of an omitted verbal noun, i.e., fumigation in odd numbers. Fumigation is perfuming by passing the incense burner around the bed once, thrice, or five times, due to his ﷺ words: 'Allah is odd and loves odd.' 'And cover his private parts': because covering them is obligatory and looking at them is forbidden like the private parts of the living. He covers from his navel to his knee by tying the waist-wrap over him; that is the correct view, as in life, and due to his ﷺ words to 'Ali: 'Do not look at the thigh of a living person nor a dead person.' There is no difference between male and female, because the private parts of a woman relative to a woman are like that of a man relative to a man. His major private parts (are covered) in the apparent narration, and in the rare narrations, he covers from navel to knee, and that is correct. Then, when he has covered them, the washer wraps a cloth on his hands and washes them. 'And stripped': that is, of clothes to enable cleaning. Al-Shafi'i said: He is washed in his shirt, because he ﷺ was washed in his shirt. We analogize him to the living state, and what he narrated was specific to him ﷺ. They said: He is stripped as he died, so that deterioration due to heat of clothes does not hasten.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage from the chapter of funerals (Kitab al-Jana'iz) is an expansion of the rulings for preparing the deceased (tajhiz al-mayyit). It begins with the immediate actions after death: closing the eyes (a Sunnah for beautification), placing the body on a bed that has been fumigated with incense in odd numbers (one, three, or five) to remove odor, covering the private parts (obligatory to prevent looking), and stripping the body of clothes to allow washing. The text then discusses a key dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding talqeen (prompting the deceased with the shahada after burial). The Hanafi position, based on the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), is that talqeen is not done after burial; rather, the hadith 'Prompt your dying ones' refers to those nearing death, not the deceased. A supplementary note describes extending the limbs, placing a sword or iron on the stomach to prevent swelling, and avoiding placing hands on the chest (a practice of disbelievers). Informing people of the death is permissible to increase the funeral prayer congregation, as long as it is not for boasting. The text also includes the dispute about stripping the deceased: Shafi'i holds that the deceased should be washed in his shirt, analogizing to the Prophet ﷺ being washed in his shirt; the Hanafis argue that this was specific to the Prophet, and the general rule is stripping, like in life, to allow thorough cleaning and prevent rapid decay.

Key Terms
تلقين الميت (talqeen al-mayyit): The act of prompting the deceased with the shahada after burial.
تجمير (tajmir): Fumigating the bed with incense in odd numbers to remove bad odor.
عورة (awrah): The part of the body that must be covered; for a deceased, the same as for the living.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when should the shahada be prompted to a dying person?
A) After burial
B) While alive and near death
C) During the funeral prayer
D) It is not prescribed at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes closing eyes, odd-numbered fumigation, covering from navel to knee, and stripping for washing, but does not practice talqeen after burial.

Salah — Prayer

Leadership and Communal Obligation in Funeral Prayer
Defines who leads the funeral prayer and its status as fard kifayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who leads the funeral prayer and explain why it is fard kifayah, citing the evidence and the inter-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
The sultan leads the funeral prayer; honoring authority is wajib, and the prayer is a communal obligation.

This lesson from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses two fundamental rulings for funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). First, who is most entitled to lead – a matter of priority that touches on the respect due to authority. Second, the obligation level of the prayer itself – a communal duty that, once performed by some, lifts from the rest. Understanding these rulings helps you navigate both the fiqh of leadership in worship and the structure of collective obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main rulings
Read the passage and extract: (a) who leads the funeral prayer (the sultan) and (b) the level of obligation (fard kifayah). These are the core legal determinations.
The phrase 'السلطان أحق بصلاته' gives both the leader and the implied obligation to give precedence.
2
Examine the evidence for each ruling
For leadership: note the practice of Husayn ibn 'Ali giving precedence to the governor Sa'id ibn al-'As. For fard kifayah: the hadith commands (e.g., 'Pray over every righteous and sinful person') and ijma (consensus) establish the obligation, but the phrase 'فرض كفاية' explains that the right of the deceased can be fulfilled by some.
The command 'صلوا' indicates obligation, but communal fulfillment removes hardship.
3
Map the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute
Identify Abu Yusuf's position (wali more entitled) and al-Shafi'i's position (wali precedes ruler). Understand the Hanafi response: the ruler's precedence is wajib based on the Companions' practice.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is clear: if the ruler is present, he leads even if the family objects.
4
Assess the authority weight and mufta bihi
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's: sultan first, then judge, then imam of the neighborhood. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and supported by the practice of Husayn.
Abu Yusuf's view is a valid intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf but is not the operative fatwa.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a deceased Muslim in a city where the governor is present. Under Hanafi fiqh, the governor leads. The prayer is fard kifayah; if at least one group prays, the obligation is fulfilled for all.
The scenario tests understanding of both leadership priority and collective obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الصلاة على الميت السلطان أحق بصلاته، وهي فرض كفاية. فصل: أي هذا فصل في الصلاة على الميت، والأصل فيه قوله صلوا على كل بر وفاجر"، وقوله علية: للمسلم على المسلم ستة حقوق"، وذكر من جملتها أن يصلي على جنازته وكذا الإجماع منعقد على فرضية صلاة الجنازة إلا أنها فرض كفاية لأن قضاء حق الميت يحصل بالبعض، وقيل: هذه الصلاة بهذه الكيفية، والتكبير من خصائص هذه الأمة كالوصية للثلث. (مستخلص، فتح) أحق بصلاته لأن في التقديم عليه إهانته وتعظيمه واجب، وأراد بالسلطان من له حكم وولاية على الناس، سواء كان الخليفة أو غيره. وفي رمز الحقائق :[۱۰۹/۱] نص عليه أبو حنيفة بقوله: الخليفة أولى إن حضر، فإن لم يحضر فإمام المصر أي حاكمها، وبعده القاضي، وبعده إمام الحي، ومعنى الأحقية في قوله: "السلطان أحق" وجوب تقديمه بخلاف تقديم إمام الحي على الولي فإنه مندوب، وقوله: "إن حضر لما روي أن الحسين بن علي ما لما مات الحسن الله قدم سعيد بن العاص وقال: لو لا السنة لما قدمتك، وكان سعيد والياً في المدينة يومئذ، وذكر في الأصل أن إمام الحي أولى بها يعني إذا لم يحضر السلطان ولا من يقوم مقامه، وقال أبو يوسف: ولي الميت أولى بها، وقال الشافعي: الولي مقدم على الوالي. (عيني، فتح) وهي فرض كفاية فتسقط بإقامة البعض عن الباقين. Section on the prayer over the deceased. The sultan is most entitled to lead his prayer, and it is a communal obligation. Section: This is a section on the prayer over the deceased. The basis for it is his saying: 'Pray over every righteous and sinful person,' and his saying: 'A Muslim has six rights over another Muslim,' and among them he mentioned that he should pray over his funeral. Likewise, consensus is established on the obligation of funeral prayer, but it is a communal obligation because fulfilling the right of the deceased is achieved by some... He is most entitled to lead his prayer because giving precedence to someone else would be an insult to him, and honoring him is obligatory. By 'sultan' is meant anyone who has authority and governance over the people, whether the caliph or others... Abu Hanifa stated: The caliph is most entitled if present; if not present, then the governor of the city, then the judge, then the imam of the neighborhood. The meaning of 'most entitled' in his statement 'the sultan is most entitled' is the obligation of giving him precedence, unlike giving precedence of the imam of the neighborhood over the wali, which is recommended... It is related that when al-Hasan died, al-Husayn gave precedence to Sa'id ibn al-'As, saying: 'Were it not for the sunnah, I would not have given you precedence.' Abu Yusuf said: The wali of the deceased is more entitled. Al-Shafi'i said: The wali takes precedence over the ruler. It [the prayer] is a communal obligation, so it drops from the rest when some perform it. By consensus, so whoever denies it becomes a disbeliever because he denies consensus. Its cause is a deceased Muslim; its pillar is the takbirs and standing; its sunnah is praising, eulogizing, and supplication; its etiquettes are many, and the best of its rows are the last ones.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This section from Kanz al-Daqa'iq covers two main rulings for funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). First, who is most entitled to lead: the sultan (ruler), because giving precedence to someone else would dishonor him, and honoring him is obligatory. By 'sultan' is meant anyone with authority, such as the caliph, governor, judge, or imam of the neighborhood, in that order of priority. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i differ: Abu Yusuf says the wali (family guardian) is more entitled; al-Shafi'i says the wali precedes the ruler. The Hanafi position, based on the practice of Husayn ibn 'Ali at the funeral of al-Hasan, is that the ruler's precedence is wajib (obligatory), while the imam of the neighborhood's precedence over the wali is only recommended (mandub). Second, the ruling of the prayer itself: it is fard kifayah (communal obligation) by consensus (ijma). If some people perform it, the obligation drops from the rest. Denying its obligation is kufr because it rejects ijma. Its cause is a deceased Muslim; its rukn (pillar) is the takbirs and standing; its sunnah includes praising Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, and supplicating for the deceased. The best rows are the last ones (to avoid distractions).

Key Terms
سلطان (sultan): Any person with authority over people, such as the caliph, governor, or judge.
أحق (ahaqq): Most entitled, having priority, implying obligation of precedence.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation that falls from all if some perform it.
إمام الحي (imam al-hayy): The imam of the neighbourhood or local mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who leads the funeral prayer if the sultan (ruler) is present?
A) The sultan leads
B) The wali leads
C) The imam of the neighborhood leads
D) The family chooses

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the sultan leads the funeral prayer as a wajib precedence, and the prayer itself is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) by consensus.

The Order of Entitlement to Lead the Funeral Prayer
States the order of entitlement to lead the funeral prayer with proofs and disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of entitlement for leading the funeral prayer and explain the proof from hadith and the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
The ruler leads the funeral prayer; honouring him is obligatory.

This lesson examines who has the right to lead the funeral prayer. The Hanafi school gives highest priority to the ruler (sultan) to avoid dishonouring authority, based on a hadith of al-Husayn. However, there is a known disagreement within the school and with al-Shafi'i. Understanding this order is important for proper funeral arrangements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The funeral prayer is fard kifayah by ijma. The passage begins by establishing this and then moves to who leads.
2
State the Hanafi order of entitlement
The order is: sultan (ruler) > qadi > imam of the quarter > wali (guardian). The right of the sultan is wajib; the right of the imam over the wali is mandub.
3
Trace the proof from hadith
The hadith reports that al-Husayn gave precedence to Governor Sa'id b. al-As, saying 'Were it not for the sunna, I would not have given you precedence.' This shows the ruler is more entitled.
The sunna refers to the practice of giving rulers priority.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that the wali is more entitled than the ruler, while Abu Hanifa holds the opposite.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Al-Shafi'i also holds that the wali is ahead of the ruler.
The Hanafi response emphasises honouring the ruler.

تتمة: لو صلي على ميت قبل أن يغسل تعاد الصلاة بعد الغسل إذا أمكن غسله فإن لم يمكن بأن دفن بلا غسل ولم يمكن إخراجه إلا بالنبش سقط الغسل، وصلي على قبره بلا غسل ضرورة، فإن لم يهل عليه التراب أخرج وغسل، ولو صلي عليه بلا غسل ودفن أعيدت على القبر، وقيل: تنقلب صحيحة. (ط) ثم الولي: على ترتيب العصبات إلا الأب فيقدم على الابن اتفاقاً في الأصح لغيره: بالصلاة عليه؛ لأن التقديم حقه، فله إبطاله بتقديم غيره رمز الحقائق: ۱۱۰/۱] غير الولي والسلطان: أي وغير السلطان، يعني من هو مؤخر عن الولي، فإن صلى القاضي أو الإمام أي لا يعيد؛ لأنهما مقدمان عليه.
Chapter: This is a chapter on the funeral prayer. Its basis is his saying: 'Pray over every righteous and sinful person,' and his saying: 'A Muslim has six rights over a Muslim,' and among them is that he prays over his funeral. Likewise consensus is established on the obligation of the funeral prayer, but it is a collective obligation (fard kifaya) because the right of the deceased can be fulfilled by some. It is said: This prayer is in this manner, and the takbir is from the special characteristics of this nation, like the will for one-third. He is most entitled to lead his prayer because giving priority to him is dishonouring him, and honouring him is obligatory. By 'sultan' is meant one who has authority and governance over people, whether he is the caliph or other. In Rami al-Haqaiq: Abu Hanifa explicitly said: The caliph is more entitled if present; if not present, then the imam of the city, i.e., its ruler, then the qadi, then the imam of the quarter. The meaning of entitlement in his saying 'the sultan is most entitled' is the obligation of giving him precedence, unlike giving precedence to the imam of the quarter over the wali, which is recommended. His saying 'if present' because it is narrated that al-Husayn bin Ali, when al-Hasan died, presented Sa'id bin al-As and said: 'Were it not for the sunna, I would not have given you precedence.' And Sa'id was a governor in Medina at that time. It is mentioned in al-Asl that the imam of the quarter is more entitled to it when the sultan or his representative is not present. Abu Yusuf said: The wali of the deceased is more entitled to it. Al-Shafi'i said: The wali is given precedence over the ruler. And it is a collective obligation, so it falls due to its performance by some over others. By consensus, so whoever denies it becomes a disbeliever due to his denial of consensus. It was made collective because obliging everyone would be impossible or harmful. The cause of its obligation: the deceased Muslim. Its pillars: the takbirs and standing. Its sunnas: praising, lauding, and supplicating. Its etiquettes are many, and its best rows are the last.

[PAGE_175]
Chapter of Funerals
174
Most entitled to lead the funeral prayer
And its condition is the Islam of the deceased and his purity, then the qadi if present, then the imam of the quarter, then the wali, and he has the right to permit others. If one other than the wali and sultan prays over the deceased, meaning the one who is later in order than the wali, that is, he does not repeat because they are given precedence over him. Islam of the deceased: because of Allah's saying: 'And never pray over any of them who has died, ever' (9:84), meaning that the hypocrites are disbelievers, so one does not pray over the disbeliever. That is, a condition for the validity of the funeral prayer is the Islam of the deceased, either by himself, or by the Islam of one of his parents, or by following the abode of Islam. And if an adult is asked about Islam and does not describe it and dies, one does not pray over him, and Islam is its specific condition. And his purity: i.e., of the deceased, because he has the ruling of the imam, so it is not valid before washing. And his presence is a condition, so one does not pray over an absent person. And placing him in front of the people, so if they place him behind them, the prayer is not valid. And his purity: i.e., purity of the deceased, so it is not valid over one who has not been washed, nor over one who has impurity on him. As for purity of the place, if he is on a bier, it is permissible; if on the ground, it is permissible according to one opinion because the shroud is a barrier between the deceased and impurity, and it is said: not permissible because the shroud is subsidiary so it is not considered a barrier. The author did not mention some conditions, so we say: purity from impurity in garment, body, and place, and covering the private parts are conditions for the imam and the deceased, and the deceased being in front of the worshipper. If behind him, it is not valid because he is like an imam in one respect not in all, as evidence by its validity over a child, the deceased being ahead of the imam, the puberty of the imam, and the presence of the deceased or the majority of his body like half with the head, so one does not pray over an absent person. As for his prayer over the Negus, it is either because his bier was raised so he saw it in his presence, so the prayer of those behind him was over a deceased that the imam saw and was in his presence but not the followers, and this does not prevent following, or it was a special privilege for the Negus. His placement is a condition, so one does not pray over him carried on necks or on an animal except for a latecomer. Similarly, it is a condition that he be facing the qibla. If they mistake the qibla, the prayer is valid if they ijtihad, otherwise no. And if they place the head in the position of feet, the prayer is valid but they are blameworthy if intentional. Then what is meant by the place whose purity is required is either the bier or the ground. If there is no bier, then purity of the ground is required when the deceased is placed without a bier. As for with a bier, the non-requirement of purity of the ground is agreed upon. Appendix: If prayer is offered over a deceased before he is washed, the prayer is repeated after washing if washing is possible. If it is not possible, such as he was buried without washing and cannot be exhumed except by digging up, then washing is dropped, and prayer is offered over his grave without washing out of necessity. If he has not been covered with soil, he is exhumed and washed. And if prayer was offered over him without washing and he was buried, the prayer is repeated over the grave, and it is said: it becomes valid. (Fath) 'If present' and in some copies 'if both present' i.e., the sultan and the qadi, meaning the sultan is most entitled, then the qadi if the sultan does not lead. Then the imam of the quarter: he is the one with whom the deceased used to pray behind him in his life. Then the wali: according to the order of asabah, except the father is given precedence over the son in the soundest view. Others: by praying over him because taking precedence is his right, so he can nullify it by giving precedence to others. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 110/1) 'Other than the wali and sultan': meaning other than the sultan, i.e., one who is later than the wali. If the qadi or imam prays, they do not repeat because they are given precedence over him.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling on the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). It begins by establishing the prayer as fard kifayah based on the Prophet's commands and consensus. The prayer is a collective obligation; if some perform it, the rest are absolved. Denial of its obligation amounts to disbelief because it denies consensus. The cause of obligation is the deceased Muslim. Its essential pillars (arkan) are the four takbirs and standing. Its sunan include praising Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, and supplicating for the deceased. The passage then addresses who is most entitled to lead the prayer: the sultan (ruler) has the highest right, followed by the qadi, then the imam of the quarter, then the wali (guardian/executor). This order is based on the hadith where al-Husayn gave precedence to the governor over the wali. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold that the wali should have precedence, but the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that the ruler is given priority to avoid dishonouring him. The wali may delegate another to lead. If someone other than the wali and sultan leads (e.g., qadi or imam), the prayer is valid and need not be repeated because they are higher in rank. The conditions for validity are detailed next: the deceased must be Muslim (either personally or through parent or dar al-Islam). The deceased must be pure (after ghusl and free from najasah). The deceased must be present (most of the body) and placed in front of the worshippers. The worshippers must face the qibla. If the deceased is on a bier, the ground need not be pure; the shroud acts as a barrier. The appendix (tamama) discusses the case of praying before ghusl: if possible, the prayer is repeated after washing; if impossible (e.g., buried), the prayer is offered over the grave without ghusl.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultān): The ruler or person in authority over the people, e.g., caliph, governor.
الإمام (al-imām): The imam of the quarter (local mosque) who leads daily prayers.
الولي (al-walī): The guardian or executor of the deceased, usually a relative from the asabah.
فرض كفاية (fard kifāya): A collective obligation: if some Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved of sin.
التكبير (al-takbīr): The utterance of 'Allahu Akbar' four times in the funeral prayer, a pillar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer if the sultan is present?
A) The wali
B) The qadi
C) The sultan
D) The imam of the quarter

Key Takeaway
The ruler leads the funeral prayer; honouring him is obligatory, and the wali may only lead if higher authorities are absent.

Salah — Prayer

Conditions for the Validity of the Funeral Prayer
Lists and explains the conditions for funeral prayer validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the conditions for the validity of the funeral prayer and explain the ruling when prayer is offered before ghusl.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer requires the deceased to be Muslim, pure, present, and placed correctly.

This lesson details the conditions (shurut) required for the funeral prayer to be valid. These include Islam and purity of the deceased, their presence and correct placement, and the condition of facing qibla. Special cases like praying before ghusl or on a bier are also addressed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
The funeral prayer is fard kifayah. The conditions are for its validity (sihha).
2
List the conditions mentioned
The matn states: Islam of the deceased, purity (after ghusl), presence of the deceased, placement in front, and facing qibla. The commentary adds purity of place and covering 'awrah.
3
Explain each condition with evidence
Islam: Quran 9:84 forbids prayer over disbelievers. Purity: the deceased must be washed (ghusl). Presence: the body must be present; prayer over an absent person is invalid. Placement: the deceased must be in front of the worshippers. Qibla: must face the qibla.
4
Note exceptions and details
If the deceased is on a bier, purity of the ground is not required because the bier acts as a barrier. If the head is placed at the feet, the prayer is valid but blameworthy.
5
Understand the appendix (tamama)
If prayer is performed before ghusl, it must be repeated after washing if possible. If already buried without ghusl, prayer over the grave is offered without repeating ghusl.

Chapter: This is a chapter on the funeral prayer. Its basis is his saying: 'Pray over every righteous and sinful person,' and his saying: 'A Muslim has six rights over a Muslim,' and among them is that he prays over his funeral. Likewise consensus is established on the obligation of the funeral prayer, but it is a collective obligation (fard kifaya) because the right of the deceased can be fulfilled by some. It is said: This prayer is in this manner, and the takbir is from the special characteristics of this nation, like the will for one-third. He is most entitled to lead his prayer because giving priority to him is dishonouring him, and honouring him is obligatory. By 'sultan' is meant one who has authority and governance over people, whether he is the caliph or other. In Rami al-Haqaiq: Abu Hanifa explicitly said: The caliph is more entitled if present; if not present, then the imam of the city, i.e., its ruler, then the qadi, then the imam of the quarter. The meaning of entitlement in his saying 'the sultan is most entitled' is the obligation of giving him precedence, unlike giving precedence to the imam of the quarter over the wali, which is recommended. His saying 'if present' because it is narrated that al-Husayn bin Ali, when al-Hasan died, presented Sa'id bin al-As and said: 'Were it not for the sunna, I would not have given you precedence.' And Sa'id was a governor in Medina at that time. It is mentioned in al-Asl that the imam of the quarter is more entitled to it when the sultan or his representative is not present. Abu Yusuf said: The wali of the deceased is more entitled to it. Al-Shafi'i said: The wali is given precedence over the ruler. And it is a collective obligation, so it falls due to its performance by some over others. By consensus, so whoever denies it becomes a disbeliever due to his denial of consensus. It was made collective because obliging everyone would be impossible or harmful. The cause of its obligation: the deceased Muslim. Its pillars: the takbirs and standing. Its sunnas: praising, lauding, and supplicating. Its etiquettes are many, and its best rows are the last.

Chapter of Funerals
174
Most entitled to lead the funeral prayer
And its condition is the Islam of the deceased and his purity, then the qadi if present, then the imam of the quarter, then the wali, and he has the right to permit others. If one other than the wali and sultan prays over the deceased, meaning the one who is later in order than the wali, that is, he does not repeat because they are given precedence over him. Islam of the deceased: because of Allah's saying: 'And never pray over any of them who has died, ever' (9:84), meaning that the hypocrites are disbelievers, so one does not pray over the disbeliever. That is, a condition for the validity of the funeral prayer is the Islam of the deceased, either by himself, or by the Islam of one of his parents, or by following the abode of Islam. And if an adult is asked about Islam and does not describe it and dies, one does not pray over him, and Islam is its specific condition. And his purity: i.e., of the deceased, because he has the ruling of the imam, so it is not valid before washing. And his presence is a condition, so one does not pray over an absent person. And placing him in front of the people, so if they place him behind them, the prayer is not valid. And his purity: i.e., purity of the deceased, so it is not valid over one who has not been washed, nor over one who has impurity on him. As for purity of the place, if he is on a bier, it is permissible; if on the ground, it is permissible according to one opinion because the shroud is a barrier between the deceased and impurity, and it is said: not permissible because the shroud is subsidiary so it is not considered a barrier. His placement is a condition, so one does not pray over him carried on necks or on an animal except for a latecomer. Similarly, it is a condition that he be facing the qibla. If they mistake the qibla, the prayer is valid if they ijtihad, otherwise no. And if they place the head in the position of feet, the prayer is valid but they are blameworthy if intentional. Then what is meant by the place whose purity is required is either the bier or the ground. If there is no bier, then purity of the ground is required when the deceased is placed without a bier. As for with a bier, the non-requirement of purity of the ground is agreed upon. Appendix: If prayer is offered over a deceased before he is washed, the prayer is repeated after washing if washing is possible. If it is not possible, such as he was buried without washing and cannot be exhumed except by digging up, then washing is dropped, and prayer is offered over his grave without washing out of necessity. If he has not been covered with soil, he is exhumed and washed. And if prayer was offered over him without washing and he was buried, the prayer is repeated over the grave, and it is said: it becomes valid. Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling on the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). It begins by establishing the prayer as fard kifayah based on the Prophet's commands and consensus. The prayer is a collective obligation; if some perform it, the rest are absolved. Denial of its obligation amounts to disbelief because it denies consensus. The cause of obligation is the deceased Muslim. Its essential pillars (arkan) are the four takbirs and standing. Its sunan include praising Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, and supplicating for the deceased. The passage then addresses who is most entitled to lead the prayer: the sultan (ruler) has the highest right, followed by the qadi, then the imam of the quarter, then the wali (guardian/executor). This order is based on the hadith where al-Husayn gave precedence to the governor over the wali. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold that the wali should have precedence, but the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that the ruler is given priority to avoid dishonouring him. The wali may delegate another to lead. If someone other than the wali and sultan leads (e.g., qadi or imam), the prayer is valid and need not be repeated because they are higher in rank. The conditions for validity are detailed next: the deceased must be Muslim (either personally or through parent or dar al-Islam). The deceased must be pure (after ghusl and free from najasah). The deceased must be present (most of the body) and placed in front of the worshippers. The worshippers must face the qibla. If the deceased is on a bier, the ground need not be pure; the shroud acts as a barrier. The appendix (tamama) discusses the case of praying before ghusl: if possible, the prayer is repeated after washing; if impossible (e.g., buried), the prayer is offered over the grave without ghusl.

السلطان (al-sultān): The ruler or person in authority over the people, e.g., caliph, governor.
الإمام (al-imām): The imam of the quarter (local mosque) who leads daily prayers.
الولي (al-walī): The guardian or executor of the deceased, usually a relative from the asabah.
فرض كفاية (fard kifāya): A collective obligation: if some Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved of sin.
التكبير (al-takbīr): The utterance of 'Allahu Akbar' four times in the funeral prayer, a pillar.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Priority Order and Conditions for the Funeral Prayer (Salat al-Janazah)
States the priority order of imams and conditions for funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the priority order of imams for leading the funeral prayer and identify the conditions for its validity, applying the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
The sultan leads the funeral prayer; if absent, the judge, then the local imam, then the guardian – only the guardian may delegate.

The funeral prayer (Salat al-Janazah) is a communal obligation with specific rulings on who should lead it. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq establishes a clear hierarchy of entitlement and sets forth the conditions that must be met for the prayer to be valid. Understanding this priority ensures that the prayer is performed correctly and that the rights of the deceased and the community are respected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Priority Order
List the four categories of persons entitled to lead the funeral prayer in order: the sultan (ruler), the judge (qadi), the local imam (imam al-hayy), and the guardian (wali). Note that the sultan has the highest right.
The sultan here means the head of state or his representative.
2
Understand the Guardian's Role
The guardian may delegate his right to lead the prayer to someone else. However, if someone lower in rank (e.g., a stranger) leads the prayer without the guardian's permission, the guardian must repeat the prayer.
The guardian is the inheritor (asabah) in order; father takes precedence over son.
3
Analyze the Conditions for Validity
The passage lists conditions: the deceased must be Muslim, physically pure (washed, free from najasah), present, placed in front of the imam, and oriented towards the qibla. The prayer is not valid if the deceased is absent or not purified.
Cite the Quranic verse (9:84) as the proof for the condition of Islam.
4
Examine the Quranic Evidence
The author cites Quran 9:84, which prohibits praying over hypocrites. This implies that faith is a condition; thus the funeral prayer is only for Muslims.
The dalal is zanni because the verse addresses a specific group, but general prohibition is derived.
5
Consider Post-Prayer Scenarios
If the prayer was performed before washing or without proper conditions, it must be repeated. If burial has occurred without washing, prayer may be offered at the grave.
This shows the importance of fulfilling the conditions as soon as possible.

(ط) ثم الولي: على ترتيب العصبات إلا الأب فيقدم على الابن اتفاقاً في الأصح لغيره: بالصلاة عليه؛ لأن التقديم حقه، فله إبطاله بتقديم غيره رمز الحقائق: ۱۱۰/۱] غير الولي والسلطان: أي وغير السلطان، يعني من هو مؤخر عن الولي، فإن صلى القاضي أو الإمام أي لا يعيد؛ لأنهما مقدمان عليه. أعاد الولي، ولم يُصلّ غيره بعده، وإن دفن بلا صلاة صلي على قبره ما لم يتفسخ،
Chapter of Funerals. Most entitled to lead the funeral prayer: its conditions are the deceased being Muslim and pure, then the judge if present, then the imam of the locality, then the guardian. He (the guardian) may allow another to pray. If other than the guardian and the sultan pray, the guardian repeats. Explanation of conditions: Islam of the deceased: because Allah says 'And never pray for any of them who dies' (9:84) meaning the hypocrites are disbelievers, so prayer is not performed for a disbeliever. Purity of the deceased: it is not valid for one who has not been washed, or who has impurity. The text then discusses conditions of purity, presence, direction, and rulings on repeating the prayer if buried without washing.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq states the rulings on who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer and the conditions for its validity. The author begins with the order of priority: the ruler (sultan or judge) is most entitled, then the local imam who led the deceased in congregational prayers during his life, then the deceased's guardian (wali). The guardian may delegate others. If someone lower in rank prays without permission, the guardian must repeat the prayer. The passage then explains conditions: the deceased must be Muslim (citing Quran 9:84), physically pure (washed and free from najasah), present, and placed in front of the imam. The prayer is not valid for a missing person or if the deceased is carried on shoulders. The direction of qibla is also required. A supplementary discussion covers cases where the prayer was performed before washing: if possible, it must be repeated after washing; if burial has occurred, prayer is performed at the grave. The passage also notes that the sultan takes precedence over the judge, and the father over the son as guardian. If someone lower than the guardian prays, the guardian must repeat, but if the giver of permission is the guardian, no repetition is needed by the one who prayed.

Key Terms
الولي (al-wali): The legal guardian of the deceased, entitled to lead the funeral prayer by default.
إمام الحي (imam al-hayy): The imam who regularly led the deceased in congregational prayers during his life.
السلطان (al-sultan): The ruler or head of state, who has the highest right to lead funeral prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer if the sultan is present?
A) The local imam
B) The guardian (wali)
C) The sultan/ruler
D) The judge

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer leadership follows a strict hierarchy: sultan, judge, local imam, then guardian; the guardian may delegate, but others must seek permission or risk repetition.

The Four Takbirs and Recitation in Funeral Prayer
Method of the funeral prayer and the dispute on recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recitation in the funeral prayer and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
In the funeral prayer, the required recitation is thana' (praise), not Fatiha.

The funeral prayer is a unique act of worship with a distinctive structure. One of the key differences between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools concerns what is recited after the first takbir. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position that only thana' (praise) is required and that reciting Fatiha is not part of the sunna.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The funeral prayer consists of four takbirs. After the first takbir, recitation (qira'ah) is required. According to the Hanafi school, this recitation is thana' (the opening supplication Subhanaka Allahumma...), not Fatiha.
This is a wajib element – omission requires repetition of the prayer if done intentionally, or sajdah al-sahw if forgotten (but funeral prayer has no prostration, so compensation is made by repeating the prayer within the time).
2
Locate the dalil for the Hanafi position
The text cites the statement of Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet did not prescribe a specific recitation for the funeral prayer. Also, the general principle that the funeral prayer is not a standard prayer (salat) in which Fatiha is obligatory.
The key textual evidence is the absence of a command to recite Fatiha, and the practice of the Companions.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the funeral prayer is a prayer (salat) and every prayer requires Fatiha, based on the hadith 'No prayer is valid without Fatiha' and the report that Ali recited Fatiha at a funeral saying it was from the sunna.
The Shafi'i school considers Fatiha obligatory in every rak'ah of every prayer, including funeral.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The funeral prayer is not a regular prayer; it is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) with its own rules. (2) The report of Ali is interpreted as reciting Fatiha with the intention of praise (thana'), not as required recitation. The Hanafi position is that reciting Fatiha with the intention of praise is permissible, but if intended as obligatory recitation, it is disliked (makruh).
Thus, the Hanafi view allows Fatiha as thana' but not as fard.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In the Hanafi school, if a person recites Fatiha as the Quranic recitation (not as thana'), the prayer is still valid but makruh. In the Shafi'i school, omitting Fatiha invalidates the prayer.
This difference affects validity and recommended practice.

باب الجنائز ١٧٥ كيفية الصلاة على الميت وهي أربع تكبيرات بثناء أي الصلاة الولي أعاد الولي ولو على قبره إن شاء؛ لأجل حقه لا لإسقاط الفرض، ولهذا قلنا ليس لمن صلى عليها أن يصلي مع الولي؛ لأن تكرارها غير مشروع، وعلم من قوله: "أعاد الولي" أن لإمام الحي أن يعيد أيضاً؛ لأن الإعادة حيث ثبتت لمن هو أدنى وهو الولي كان ثبوتها للأعلى أولى. ولم يصل غيره بعده: وكذا بعد إمام الحي وبعد كل من يتقدم على الولي خلافاً للشافعي؛ لأنه عليه صلى على قبر بعد ما صلى عليه أهله، وورد أن الناس صلوا على قوما بعد قوم ولنا ما سبق من عدم مشروعية التنفل بها، ولذا ترك الناس الصلاة على قبره عليها النبي وهو اليوم كما وضع؛ لأن أجساد الأنبياء لا يأكلها التراب، وعن عبد الله بن سلام لما فاتته الصلاة على عمر الله قال: إن سبقت بالصلاة فلم أسبق بالدعاء، وإنما صلى عليه على القبر بعد ما صلى عليه أهله؛ لأنه هو الولي؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ النَّبِيُّ أَوْلَى بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْ أَنْفُسِهِمْ ﴾ (الأحزاب:1) وتكرار الصلاة على النبي - عالية كان مخصوصا به. فائدة: لما أن غسل عليه وكفن ووضع على السرير دخل أبو بكر وعمر ما، ومعهما نفر من المهاجرين والأنصار، فقالا: السلام عليك أيها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته وسلم المهاجرون والأنصار كما سلم أبو بكر وعمر ما ، ثم صفوا صفوفا لا يؤمهم أحد ، ثم قال أبو بكر وعمر الله لهما وهما في الصف الأول: حياك رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اللهم إنا نشهد أنه بلغ ما أنزل إليه، ونصح لأمته، وجاهد في سبيل الله حتى أعز الله دينه وتمت كلمته، وأومن به وحده لا شريك له، فاجعلنا إلهنا ممن يتبع قول الذي معه، وأجمع بيننا وبينه حتى تعرفه بنا وتعرفنا به، فإنه كان بالمؤمنين رؤوفا رحيما، لا يبتغي بالإيمان بدلا، ولا يشتري به ثمناً أبداً، والناس يقولون: آمين ويخرجون فيدخل آخرون حتى صلى الرجال ثم النساء ثم الصبيان وهذا الصنيع وهو صلاتهم عليه فرادى لم يؤمهم أحد، أمر مجمع عليه لا خلاف فيه. (فتح) غيره: أي بعد الولي وكذا بعد كل من يتقدم على الولي، وقال الشافعي: يجوز لمن لم يصل أن يصلي بعده. (ع) وإن دفن أي الميت بعد الغسل أو قبله وأهيل التراب. (ط) ما لم يتفسخ عن أبي يوسف ومحمد: يصلى عليه إلى ثلاثة أيام، والصحيح أن التقدير ليس بلازم؛ لأنه يختلف باختلاف الزمان برداً وحراً، والمكان رخاوة وصلابة، وحال الميت سمنا وهزالاً، فيعتبر فيه أكبر الرأي لإقامة الواجب بقدر الإمكان. (فتح) ۱۹
Chapter of Funerals. Method of the funeral prayer: it is four takbirs with praise. The guardian repeats the prayer even at the grave if he wishes, for his right, not to fulfill the obligation. Thus we say that one who has already prayed may not pray with the guardian, because repetition is not prescribed... (The text continues with the story of the Prophet's funeral and discussions on the time limit for grave prayer and the recitation in takbirs.)
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage details the performance of the funeral prayer and expands on the ruling that the guardian (wali) may repeat the prayer if someone lower in rank performed it initially. The repetition is allowed only for the guardian and those above him (local imam, judge, sultan); others may not repeat because the funeral prayer cannot be performed superfluously. This is opposed to Imam al-Shafi'i who allows anyone to pray later. The Hanafi position is supported by the practice of the Companions who prayed over the Prophet individually without an imam, and by the hadith that the Prophet himself prayed at the grave after burial. The passage then discusses the time limit: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, prayer over the grave is allowed up to three days, but the correct view is not limited to a fixed time because it varies with conditions. Finally, the issue of recitation: the prayer consists of four takbirs; in the first takbir, one recites thana' (praise). The preferred thana' is 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika' as in regular prayers, not the full 'wa jalla thana'uka'. Reciting Fatiha is not required; if recited with the intention of praise (thana') it is permissible, but with the intention of Quranic recitation it is disliked.

Key Terms
تكبيرات (takbirat): The phrases 'Allahu Akbar' said in the funeral prayer, four in number.
ثناء (thana'): Praise of Allah, specifically the opening supplication (Subhanaka Allahumma).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is obligatory (fard)
B) It is sunnah and recommended
C) It is permissible only with the intention of praise, but disliked if intended as Quranic recitation
D) It is forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi funeral prayer, the required recitation after the first takbir is thana' (praise), not Fatiha.
