Repetition of the Funeral Prayer by the Guardian and Others
Ruling on repetition of funeral prayer by guardian and others

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain who may repeat the funeral prayer and why, and contrast the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Only the guardian (wali) and those above him may repeat the funeral prayer; others may not.

The funeral prayer is a unique obligation that is not repeated arbitrarily. This lesson examines the ruling on repeating the funeral prayer, especially at the grave, and the specific right of the guardian. We will also explore the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who allows anyone to pray later.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is repeating the funeral prayer after it has already been performed. The Hanafi ruling: only the guardian (wali) may repeat, and also those above him (imam of the locality, sultan). Others who have already prayed may not repeat.
The repetition is for the guardian's 'right' (haqq), not to fulfill the obligation (which is already discharged).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the practice of the Companions at the Prophet's funeral, where they prayed individually without an imam, indicating that repetition is not a congregational act. Also, the verse 'The Prophet is more worthy of the believers than themselves' (33:6) used to show the guardian's special right.
The dalil also includes the absence of any report that the Companions prayed multiple times for the same person in congregation.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i allows any person who missed the prayer to pray later, based on the Prophet's own action of praying at a grave after the family had prayed, and general analogy that the funeral prayer is a prayer like any other, and prayers can be made up.
The Shafi'i school does not restrict repetition to the guardian.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response emphasizes that the funeral prayer is not a supererogatory prayer; it is a single fard kifayah that cannot be repeated as a nafl. The Prophet's action is specific to him as the highest guardian. The practice of the Companions at his funeral, praying individually without an imam, shows that there is no prescribed repetition.
Thus, repetition is only for those with a specific right (guardianship).
5
Determine the practical consequence
In the Hanafi school, if the imam or guardian prays, no one else may pray later. In the Shafi'i school, anyone may pray later even if the first prayer was performed.
This affects how funerals are handled when multiple groups want to pray.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجنائز ١٧٥ كيفية الصلاة على الميت وهي أربع تكبيرات بثناء أي الصلاة الولي أعاد الولي ولو على قبره إن شاء؛ لأجل حقه لا لإسقاط الفرض، ولهذا قلنا ليس لمن صلى عليها أن يصلي مع الولي؛ لأن تكرارها غير مشروع، وعلم من قوله: "أعاد الولي" أن لإمام الحي أن يعيد أيضاً؛ لأن الإعادة حيث ثبتت لمن هو أدنى وهو الولي كان ثبوتها للأعلى أولى. ولم يصل غيره بعده: وكذا بعد إمام الحي وبعد كل من يتقدم على الولي خلافاً للشافعي؛ لأنه عليه صلى على قبر بعد ما صلى عليه أهله، وورد أن الناس صلوا على قوما بعد قوم ولنا ما سبق من عدم مشروعية التنفل بها، ولذا ترك الناس الصلاة على قبره عليها النبي وهو اليوم كما وضع؛ لأن أجساد الأنبياء لا يأكلها التراب، وعن عبد الله بن سلام لما فاتته الصلاة على عمر الله قال: إن سبقت بالصلاة فلم أسبق بالدعاء، وإنما صلى عليه على القبر بعد ما صلى عليه أهله؛ لأنه هو الولي؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ النَّبِيُّ أَوْلَى بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْ أَنْفُسِهِمْ ﴾ (الأحزاب:1) وتكرار الصلاة على النبي - عالية كان مخصوصا به. فائدة: لما أن غسل عليه وكفن ووضع على السرير دخل أبو بكر وعمر ما، ومعهما نفر من المهاجرين والأنصار، فقالا: السلام عليك أيها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته وسلم المهاجرون والأنصار كما سلم أبو بكر وعمر ما ، ثم صفوا صفوفا لا يؤمهم أحد ، ثم قال أبو بكر وعمر الله لهما وهما في الصف الأول: حياك رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اللهم إنا نشهد أنه بلغ ما أنزل إليه، ونصح لأمته، وجاهد في سبيل الله حتى أعز الله دينه وتمت كلمته، وأومن به وحده لا شريك له، فاجعلنا إلهنا ممن يتبع قول الذي معه، وأجمع بيننا وبينه حتى تعرفه بنا وتعرفنا به، فإنه كان بالمؤمنين رؤوفا رحيما، لا يبتغي بالإيمان بدلا، ولا يشتري به ثمناً أبداً، والناس يقولون: آمين ويخرجون فيدخل آخرون حتى صلى الرجال ثم النساء ثم الصبيان وهذا الصنيع وهو صلاتهم عليه فرادى لم يؤمهم أحد، أمر مجمع عليه لا خلاف فيه. (فتح) غيره: أي بعد الولي وكذا بعد كل من يتقدم على الولي، وقال الشافعي: يجوز لمن لم يصل أن يصلي بعده. (ع) وإن دفن أي الميت بعد الغسل أو قبله وأهيل التراب. (ط) ما لم يتفسخ عن أبي يوسف ومحمد: يصلى عليه إلى ثلاثة أيام، والصحيح أن التقدير ليس بلازم؛ لأنه يختلف باختلاف الزمان برداً وحراً، والمكان رخاوة وصلابة، وحال الميت سمنا وهزالاً، فيعتبر فيه أكبر الرأي لإقامة الواجب بقدر الإمكان. (مسكين) بثناء: أي مع ثناء، وقد اختلف فيه، فقال بعضهم: بحمد الله في ظاهر الرواية، وقال بعضهم: يقول: "سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك" كما في سائر الصلوات وهو رواية الحسن عن الإمام، فظاهره أنه لا يزيد وجل ثناؤك"، وهو خلاف المحفوظ، وقال الشافعي: يقرأ الفاتحة؛ لأنها صلاة من وجه، ولا صلاة إلا بالفاتحة، ولما روي عن ابن عباس ما أنه عليا صلى على جنازة، فقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب، وقال: "لتعلموا أنه من السنة"، ولنا قول ابن مسعود له أنه عليها لم يوقت لنا في صلاة الجنازة قراءة، وفي "الخزانة": لا بأس بقراءة الفاتحة بنية الثناء، وإن قرأها بنية القراءة كره. (فتح) ۱۹
Chapter of Funerals. Method of the funeral prayer: it is four takbirs with praise. The guardian repeats the prayer even at the grave if he wishes, for his right, not to fulfill the obligation. Thus we say that one who has already prayed may not pray with the guardian, because repetition is not prescribed... (The text continues with the story of the Prophet's funeral and discussions on the time limit for grave prayer and the recitation in takbirs.)
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage details the performance of the funeral prayer and expands on the ruling that the guardian (wali) may repeat the prayer if someone lower in rank performed it initially. The repetition is allowed only for the guardian and those above him (local imam, judge, sultan); others may not repeat because the funeral prayer cannot be performed superfluously. This is opposed to Imam al-Shafi'i who allows anyone to pray later. The Hanafi position is supported by the practice of the Companions who prayed over the Prophet individually without an imam, and by the hadith that the Prophet himself prayed at the grave after burial. The passage then discusses the time limit: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, prayer over the grave is allowed up to three days, but the correct view is not limited to a fixed time because it varies with conditions. Finally, the issue of recitation: the prayer consists of four takbirs; in the first takbir, one recites thana' (praise). The preferred thana' is 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika' as in regular prayers, not the full 'wa jalla thana'uka'. Reciting Fatiha is not required; if recited with the intention of praise (thana') it is permissible, but with the intention of Quranic recitation it is disliked.

Key Terms
ولي (wali): The guardian of the deceased, typically the father, grandfather, or son who is responsible for the funeral arrangements.
صلاة على القبر (salat 'ala al-qabr): The funeral prayer performed at the grave after burial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is permitted to repeat the funeral prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Any Muslim who missed the first prayer
B) Only the guardian (wali)
C) Only the imam of the locality
D) Both B and C, and anyone above them

Key Takeaway
Only the guardian and those above him have the right to repeat the funeral prayer; others may not because the prayer is not a nafl.

Ruling on Repeating the Funeral Prayer: The Guardian’s Right
Ruling with proof on repetition of funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who may repeat the funeral prayer and explain the proof from the Prophet’s action.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer is not supererogatory; only the guardian may repeat it.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa’iq addresses a key point of disagreement: may a person who missed the funeral prayer pray later? The Hanafi school holds that only the guardian (wali) may repeat the prayer, and no one else may do so after him. This is based on the nature of the janazah prayer as a right of the guardian, not a general sunnah that can be repeated. Let’s examine the ruling, its evidence, and the Shafi’i counterargument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling regarding repetition
The passage begins with 'أعاد الولي' – the guardian repeats the funeral prayer. It also states that no one else may pray after him.
The guardian is the legally responsible relative.
2
Understand the basis: right of the guardian vs. obligation
The text says 'لأجل حقه لا لإسقاط الفرض' – the repetition is due to his right, not to fulfill the obligation.
This is key: repetition is not a supererogatory prayer.
3
Examine the proof from the Prophet’s action
The text mentions that the Prophet prayed at a grave after the family had prayed (hadith). This shows the guardian’s right. Also, the Prophet’s own funeral: people prayed individually without an imam, indicating that repetition is not legislated.
The Prophet is the wali of the believers per Quran 33:6.
4
Contrast with the Shafi’i position
Imam al-Shafi’i allows anyone who missed to pray later. The Hanafi response: the funeral prayer is not a supererogatory prayer (nafl) that can be repeated; it is a specific right of the guardian.
Practical consequence: if you miss the janazah with the imam, you cannot make it up later.
5
Apply the ruling: who else may repeat?
The imam of the locality may also repeat because the guardian is the lesser; the greater (imam) may also do so analogically.
This extends the right by qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجنائز كيفية الصلاة على الميت أعاد الولي، ولم يُصلّ غيره بعده، وإن دفن بلا صلاة صلي على قبره ما لم يتفسخ، إن شاء وهي أربع تكبيرات بثناء أي الصلاة الولي أعاد الولي ولو على قبره إن شاء؛ لأجل حقه لا لإسقاط الفرض، ولهذا قلنا ليس لمن صلى عليها أن يصلي مع الولي؛ لأن تكرارها غير مشروع، وعلم من قوله: "أعاد الولي" أن لإمام الحي أن يعيد أيضاً؛ لأن الإعادة حيث ثبتت لمن هو أدنى وهو الولي كان ثبوتها للأعلى أولى. ولم يصل غيره بعده: وكذا بعد إمام الحي وبعد كل من يتقدم على الولي خلافاً للشافعي؛ لأنه عليه صلى على قبر بعد ما صلى عليه أهله، وورد أن الناس صلوا على قوما بعد قوم ولنا ما سبق من عدم مشروعية التنفل بها، ولذا ترك الناس الصلاة على قبره عليها النبي وهو اليوم كما وضع؛ لأن أجساد الأنبياء لا يأكلها التراب، وعن عبد الله بن سلام لما فاتته الصلاة على عمر رضي الله عنه قال: إن سبقت بالصلاة فلم أسبق بالدعاء، وإنما صلى عليه على القبر بعد ما صلى عليه أهله؛ لأنه هو الولي؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ النَّبِيُّ أَوْلَى بِالْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنْ أَنْفُسِهِمْ ﴾ (الأحزاب:1) وتكرار الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان مخصوصا به. فائدة: لما أن غسل عليه وكفن ووضع على السرير دخل أبو بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما، ومعهما نفر من المهاجرين والأنصار، فقالا: السلام عليك أيها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته وسلم المهاجرون والأنصار كما سلم أبو بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما، ثم صفوا صفوفا لا يؤمهم أحد، ثم قال أبو بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما وهما في الصف الأول: حياك رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اللهم إنا نشهد أنه بلغ ما أنزل إليه، ونصح لأمته، وجاهد في سبيل الله حتى أعز الله دينه وتمت كلمته، وأومن به وحده لا شريك له، فاجعلنا إلهنا ممن يتبع قول الذي معه، وأجمع بيننا وبينه حتى تعرفه بنا وتعرفنا به، فإنه كان بالمؤمنين رؤوفا رحيما، لا يبتغي بالإيمان بدلا، ولا يشتري به ثمناً أبداً، والناس يقولون: آمين ويخرجون فيدخل آخرون حتى صلى الرجال ثم النساء ثم الصبيان وهذا الصنيع وهو صلاتهم عليه فرادى لم يؤمهم أحد، أمر مجمع عليه لا خلاف فيه. (فتح) غيره: أي بعد الولي وكذا بعد كل من يتقدم على الولي، وقال الشافعي: يجوز لمن لم يصل أن يصلي بعده. (ع)
Chapter of Funerals: How to pray the funeral prayer. The guardian repeats (the prayer), and no one else prays after him. If the deceased is buried without prayer, one may pray at his grave as long as the body has not decomposed, if he wishes. It consists of four takbirs with praise (thana). The guardian repeats the prayer, even at his grave if he wishes, due to his right, not to fulfill the obligation. Hence we say: whoever has already prayed may not pray with the guardian, because repetition is not legislated. It is understood from his statement 'the guardian repeats' that the imam of the locality may also repeat, because if repetition is established for the lesser (the guardian), then for the greater it is more appropriate. 'And no one else prays after him': similarly after the imam of the locality and after everyone who takes precedence over the guardian, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed at a grave after his family had prayed over him, and it is reported that people prayed over some people after others. Our evidence is what preceded: that supererogatory prayer is not legislated in it. Hence people left praying at his grave, and his body remains as it was placed because the bodies of prophets are not consumed by the earth. It is narrated from Abdullah ibn Salam that when he missed the prayer over Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), he said: 'If I was preceded in prayer, I was not preceded in supplication.' He prayed at the grave after his family had prayed because he was the guardian, due to the verse: 'The Prophet is more worthy of the believers than themselves' (al-Ahzab 33:6). Repetition of the prayer over the Prophet (peace be upon him) was specific to him. Benefit: When he was washed, shrouded, and placed on the bier, Abu Bakr and Umar entered with a group of Muhajirun and Ansar. They said: 'Peace be upon you, O Prophet, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings.' They lined up in rows without an imam. Then Abu Bakr and Umar said: '...' This practice—that they prayed individually without an imam—is a matter of consensus, no dispute. (Fath) 'Other than him' means after the guardian, and similarly after every one who takes precedence over the guardian. Al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible for one who has not prayed to pray after him.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the repetition of the funeral prayer. The main ruling: the guardian (wali) may repeat the funeral prayer, even at the grave, but no one else may pray after him. The commentary explains that this is due to the guardian's personal right, not to fulfill the obligation. Hence, if someone has already prayed, they cannot pray with the guardian. The imam of the locality may also repeat by analogy. The Shafi'i position allows anyone who missed the prayer to pray later, even after the guardian. The Hanafi proof includes the Prophet's action of praying at the grave of a deceased after his family had prayed, and the story of Abdullah ibn Salam praying at Umar's grave because he was the guardian. The Prophet's own funeral is presented as evidence: people prayed individually without an imam, showing that the funeral prayer is not a communal prayer where repetition is common. The passage clarifies that the funeral prayer is not a supererogatory prayer that can be repeated multiple times; it is a specific right of the guardian.

Key Terms
الولي (al-wali): The legal guardian of the deceased, typically the closest relative responsible for burial arrangements.
الإعادة (al-i'adah): Repetition of the funeral prayer by the same person or another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, who may repeat the funeral prayer?
A) Anyone who missed the prayer
B) The imam of the locality
C) The wali (guardian) only
D) The family of the deceased

Key Takeaway
Only the guardian (wali) may repeat the funeral prayer; others may not because it is a specific right, not a general supererogatory act.

Time Limit for Grave Prayer and the Wording of Thana
Ruling on time limit thana wording with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time limit for praying at the grave and explain the correct thana wording, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i position on Fatiha recitation.

Core Idea
No fixed time limit for grave prayer; thana suffices; Fatiha with praise intention is allowed.

Funeral prayers have unique rulings. One is the prayer at the grave after burial. This lesson clarifies when it remains valid and what to recite in the opening praise (thana). The Hanafi school balances flexibility for the time limit with specific guidance for thana, upholding the Companion tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage covers (1) the time during which prayer at the grave is valid, and (2) the wording of the opening praise (thana) in the funeral prayer.
Both rulings are derived from the same text but are distinct legal issues.
2
Examine the time limit for grave prayer
Note that the condition is 'as long as the body has not decomposed'. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad suggested a three-day limit, but the relied-upon view is that no fixed time is necessary; it depends on external factors (climate, soil, body condition).
The judge's ijtihad determines the time based on preservation.
3
Analyze the thana dispute
The thana (praise) wording is debated: some say 'al-hamdu lillah', the preferred narration is 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika'. The Shafi'i school argues for reciting the Fatiha, citing a hadith from Ali. The Hanafi school relies on Ibn Mas'ud's statement that no recitation was prescribed.
The Hanafi view is that thana replaces Fatiha; Fatiha with Quran intention is makruh.
4
Compare proofs
Hanafi proof: Ibn Mas'ud said 'We were not prescribed any recitation.' Shafi'i proof: Ali recited Fatiha and called it sunnah. Hanafi response: Ali's action is interpreted as praise, not Quranic recitation.
The dispute is over the nature of the funeral prayer: standard prayer vs. special supplication.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, for grave prayer, wait as long as the body is intact. In funeral prayer, recite 'Subhanaka...' and avoid reciting Fatiha as Quran; if recited with praise intention, it is permissible.
The madhhab's position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن دفن أي الميت بعد الغسل أو قبله وأهيل التراب. (ط) ما لم يتفسخ عن أبي يوسف ومحمد: يصلى عليه إلى ثلاثة أيام، والصحيح أن التقدير ليس بلازم؛ لأنه يختلف باختلاف الزمان برداً وحراً، والمكان رخاوة وصلابة، وحال الميت سمنا وهزالاً، فيعتبر فيه أكبر الرأي لإقامة الواجب بقدر الإمكان. (مسكين) بثناء: أي مع ثناء، وقد اختلف فيه، فقال بعضهم: بحمد الله في ظاهر الرواية، وقال بعضهم: يقول: "سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك" كما في سائر الصلوات وهو رواية الحسن عن الإمام، فظاهره أنه لا يزيد وجل ثناؤك"، وهو خلاف المحفوظ، وقال الشافعي: يقرأ الفاتحة؛ لأنها صلاة من وجه، ولا صلاة إلا بالفاتحة، ولما روي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أن عليا رضي الله عنه صلى على جنازة، فقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب، وقال: "لتعلموا أنه من السنة"، ولنا قول ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه أنه قال: لم يوقت لنا في صلاة الجنازة قراءة، وفي "الخزانة": لا بأس بقراءة الفاتحة بنية الثناء، وإن قرأها بنية القراءة كره. (فتح)
And if the deceased is buried—after washing or before, and earth is piled—(T) as long as it has not decomposed. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: one may pray over it up to three days. The correct view is that a fixed time limit is not necessary, because it varies with time (cold/hot), place (soft/hard ground), and the condition of the deceased (fat/lean). So the judge's best opinion is considered to perform the obligation as much as possible. (Miskin) 'With thana': i.e., with praise. There is a difference of opinion: some say it is 'al-hamdu lillah' in the apparent narration; some say one says 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika' as in other prayers—this is the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam. It appears that he does not add 'wa jala thana'uka', contrary to what is memorized. Al-Shafi'i said: one recites the Fatiha because it is a form of prayer, and there is no prayer without the Fatiha, and because it is narrated from Ibn Abbas that Ali prayed over a funeral and recited the Fatiha, saying: 'So that you may know it is from the Sunnah.' Our evidence is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'We were not prescribed any recitation in the funeral prayer.' In al-Khazanah: there is no harm in reciting the Fatiha with the intention of praise, but if one recites it with the intention of Quran recitation, it is disliked. (Fath)
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues: the time limit for praying at the grave and the wording of the opening praise (thana) in the funeral prayer. On the first issue, the matn says prayer is permissible as long as the body has not decomposed. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad suggested a maximum of three days, but the relied-upon view (and the text's 'sahih') is that no fixed time is mandatory. Instead, it depends on conditions like weather and soil; the judge's ijtihad determines the time. On the second issue, the thana should be 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika' (as in other prayers) according to one narration from Imam Abu Hanifa via Imam Muhammad. The addition 'wa jala thana'uka' is not included. The Shafi'i school argues that the Fatiha is recited because the funeral prayer is a prayer and the Fatiha is obligatory in every prayer, citing a hadith from Ali. The Hanafi response is that the funeral prayer is not a standard prayer; recitation (qira'ah) was not prescribed for it. However, reciting the Fatiha with the intention of praise (thana) is permissible, but with the intention of Quranic recitation is makruh.

Key Terms
الثناء (al-thana): The opening praise in the funeral prayer, typically 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika'.
التفسخ (al-tafakkhu): Decomposition of the body; the condition after which prayer at the grave is no longer valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on reciting the Fatiha in the funeral prayer?
A) It is obligatory
B) It is recommended
C) It is prohibited
D) It is permissible if intended as praise, but makruh if intended as Quran recitation

Key Takeaway
Prayer at the grave is valid as long as the body has not decomposed; in the funeral prayer, thana (Subhanaka) is recited instead of Fatiha, and reciting Fatiha with Quran intention is makruh.

Salah — Prayer

Structure of Funeral Prayer: Takbirs, Duas, and Taslim
Expounds the four takbirs and their recitations, plus disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four takbirs of the funeral prayer, identify what is recited after each, and distinguish the Hanafi rulings from the Shafi'i position on hand raising and taslim.

Core Idea
Four takbirs define the funeral prayer; hands rise only in the first, and taslim ends it without extra dua.

The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is a communal obligation with a unique structure. Unlike regular prayers, it consists of four takbirs with specific supplications, no ruku or sujud. This passage from al-Hidayah details the sequence, the proofs for each element, and key differences with the Shafi'i school. Understanding these rulings ensures correctness in this important worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four takbirs and their recitations
After the first takbir, recite thana (praise). After the second, send salawat on the Prophet. After the third, make dua for the deceased and all Muslims. After the fourth, make taslim. No dua after the fourth and no tashahhud.
The reliable dua is given: 'Allahumma ighfir li-hayyina...'
2
Analyze hand raising and taslim rulings
Hands are raised only in the first takbir (Hanafi). Taslim is two salutations (right and left). These are sunnah. If the imam makes a fifth takbir, the follower should not follow it but wait for the imam's taslim.
Shafi'i raises hands in every takbir and makes one taslim.
3
Examine the proof for four takbirs
The Prophet prayed four takbirs over al-Najashi and continued this practice until his death, abrogating any earlier practice. This is the primary dalil.
If the imam makes six takbirs, it is not followed by consensus, contrary to Zufr's qiyas with Eid prayers.
4
Apply the preferred view on extra takbirs
The preferred view is that the follower waits for the imam's taslim and makes taslim with him. This is the mufta bihi opinion.
From Abu Hanifa, there is also the view that the follower makes taslim immediately when the imam's error becomes clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعد الأولى: أي التكبيرة الأولى، ويرفع يديه في هذه فقط، وقال الشافعي يقرأ الفاتحة عقب الثناء. (مسكين) ودعاء بأمور الآخرة، والمأثور حسن وهو: "اللهم اغفر لحينا وميتنا وشاهدنا وغائبنا وصغيرنا وكبيرنا وذكرنا وأنثانا، اللهم من أحييته منا فأحيه على الإسلام ومن توفيته منا فتوفه على الإيمان". (مسكين) وتسليمتين وليس بعدها دعاء سوى السلام وقيل يقول: "اللهم ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة، وفي الآخرة حسنة، وقنا برحمتك عذاب القبر وعذاب النار، وعند الشافعي يسلم تسليمة واحدة وقوله : فلو كبر خمسا لم يتبع؛ لأنه عليه حين صلى على النجاشي كبر أربع تكبيرات، وثبت عليها إلى أن توفي، فنسخت ما قبلها، وقيد بالخمس؛ لأنه لو كبر ستاً لا يتبع، اتفاقاً، خلافاً لزفر قياساً على تكبيرات الزوائد في العيد، وعن أبي حنيفة يسلم حين اشتغل إمامه بالخطأ، وعنه أنه ينتظر سلام الإمام يسلم معه وهو المختار، ولا يرفع يديه إلا في التكبيرة الأولى خلافاً للشافعي، فإنه يرفع في كل تكبيرة؛ لأن ابن عمر لما كان يفعل ذلك، ولنا: ما رواه الدار قطني عن ابن عباس وأبي هريرة رضي الله عنهما أنه عليه السلام كان إذا صلى على جنازة رفع يديه في أول تكبيرة ثم لا يعود. (فتح) بعد الرابعة: وينوي الميت بها مع القوم، ليس بعد الرابعة دعاء في الظاهر، ولا تشهد فيها. (ط)
After the first: i.e., the first takbir; he raises his hands only in this one. Al-Shafi'i said he recites the Fatiha after the thana. (Miskin) And supplication for matters of the Hereafter. The reliable (dua) is good: 'O Allah, forgive our living and our dead, those present and absent, young and old, male and female. O Allah, whoever You keep alive among us, let him live upon Islam, and whoever You cause to die among us, let him die upon faith.' (Miskin) And two taslims, and there is no supplication after it except salutation. It is said: 'Our Lord, give us good in this world and good in the Hereafter, and protect us from the punishment of the grave and the Fire.' According to al-Shafi'i, he makes one taslim. His statement: 'If he makes five takbirs, do not follow him' because the Prophet, when he prayed over al-Najashi, made four takbirs and adhered to them until he died, thus abrogating what came before. It is specified with five because if he makes six, it is not followed by consensus, contrary to Zufr by analogy with the extra takbirs in Eid. From Abu Hanifa: he makes taslim when his imam becomes occupied with error; and from him: he waits for the imam's taslim and makes taslim with him—this is the preferred view. He does not raise his hands except in the first takbir, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because Ibn Umar used to do that. Our evidence: al-Daraqutni narrated from Ibn Abbas and Abu Hurayra that the Prophet, when he prayed over a funeral, raised his hands in the first takbir and then did not repeat. (Fath) After the fourth: he intends the deceased with the people; there is no supplication after the fourth in appearance, and there is no tashahhud in it. (T)
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage expounds the structure of the funeral prayer according to the Hanafi school. There are four takbirs. After the first takbir, one recites the thana (praise); hands are raised only in this first takbir. After the second, one sends salawat upon the Prophet. After the third, one makes dua for the deceased and Muslims. After the fourth, one makes taslim (two salutations). The Shafi'i school differs on several points: they recite the Fatiha after thana, they raise hands for every takbir, and they make one taslim. The Hanafi reliance on the Prophet's practice is clear: he made four takbirs for al-Najashi, and this abrogated earlier practices. If the imam makes a fifth takbir, the followers should not follow him but wait. The preferred view is that the follower waits for the imam's taslim and then makes taslim with him. There is no dua or tashahhud after the fourth takbir.

Key Terms
التكبيرة (al-takbirah): The 'Allahu Akbar' said at each stage of the funeral prayer; there are four obligatory takbirs.
التسليم (al-taslim): The salutation (al-salamu alaykum) at the end of the funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when does the follower make taslim if the imam makes a fifth takbir?
A) Immediately after the fifth takbir
B) He does not follow the fifth takbir and waits for the imam's taslim, then makes taslim with him
C) He makes taslim after the fourth takbir independently
D) He follows the imam in the fifth takbir

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer consists of exactly four takbirs, with no extra dua or tashahhud after the fourth, and the follower must not follow an imam who makes a fifth takbir.

Funeral Prayer for a Child: Special Supplication and Rationale
Specifies the dua for a deceased child and explains rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the special supplication for a deceased child in Hanafi funeral prayer and explain why istighfar is omitted.

Core Idea
A child's funeral prayer omits istighfar because the child is sinless; instead, the dua asks the child to be a stored treasure and intercessor for parents.

In the Hanafi school, the funeral prayer for a child who died before puberty is not the same as for an adult. The standard supplication for forgiveness is replaced with a specific dua that acknowledges the child's sinlessness and seeks blessings for the parents. This lesson unpacks the rationale and the exact wording of this unique supplication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the ruling concerns the supplication (dua) in the funeral prayer for a child, specifically what to recite after the takbirs.
The default dua for adults includes 'Allahumma ighfir li-hayyina...' (seeking forgiveness).
2
Understand the rationale
The text states: 'because seeking forgiveness implies prior commission of sin, and the child is sinless (ma'sum)'. Therefore, istighfar is inappropriate for a child.
The same applies to the insane and mentally deficient – they are also considered sinless.
3
Learn the alternative supplication
Instead of the usual dua, recite: 'Allahumma ij'alhu lana faratan wa ajran wa dhukhra wa shafi'an mujjaban' or similar. The key terms are farat (predecessor), ajr (reward), dhukhra (stored treasure), and shafi' (intercessor).
'Dhukhra' is with a dhamma on the dhal, meaning lasting good reserved for the Hereafter.
4
Apply the same rule to others
The ruling extends to the insane (majnun) and mentally deficient (ma'tuh) because they are also sinless.
This shows the general principle: no istighfar for those who are ma'sum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لصبي: لأن الاستغفار يقتضي سبق ارتكاب الذنب وهو معصوم، وكذا المجنون والمعتوه. (مستخلص، عيني) ويقول: أي في صلاة جنازة الصبي مكان الدعاء المعروف يقرأ دعاء الذيل. (مسكين) وذخراً: بضم الذال المعجمة أي خيراً باقياً.
For a child: because seeking forgiveness implies prior commission of sin, and the child is sinless. Likewise the insane and the mentally deficient. (Mustakhlas, 'Ayni) And he says: i.e., in the funeral prayer of a child, instead of the well-known supplication, he recites the supplication of the tail. (Miskin) 'And a stored treasure' (dhukhra): with a dhamma on the dhal, meaning lasting good.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage deals with the special supplication for a deceased child in the funeral prayer. Since a child is sinless (ma'sum), one does not seek forgiveness (istighfar) but instead asks that the child be a 'precedent' (farat), a 'reward' (ajr), a 'stored treasure' (dhukhra), and an 'intercessor' (shafi') for his parents. The same applies to the insane and mentally deficient. The commentary clarifies that the word 'dhukhara' (with dhamma) means lasting good reward reserved for the Hereafter.

Key Terms
الفرط (al-farat): A predecessor who goes ahead to prepare a place for others; used for a child who dies before parents.
المعصوم (al-ma'sum): One protected from sin; here, a child who has not attained puberty is considered sinless.
الذخر (al-dhukhra): A stored treasure of good deeds; lasting good reserved for the Hereafter.
الأجر (al-ajr): Reward; here, the child becomes a source of reward for the parents.
الشفيع (al-shafi'): Intercessor; the child intercedes for the parents on the Day of Judgement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the child's parents are to be forgiven instead
B) Because the child is sinless (ma'sum) and istighfar implies prior sin
C) Because the child is not yet obligated to pray and thus needs no forgiveness
D) Because the child's burial is quicker and there is no time for the full dua

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi funeral rites, the supplication for a child omits istighfar and instead asks that the child be a forerunner, reward, stored treasure, and intercessor, reflecting the child's sinless state.

Rules for the Latecomer (Masbuq) in Funeral Prayer
Detailed rulings on how a latecomer joins and completes funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a latecomer in funeral prayer, apply the mufta bihi view, and correctly complete missed takbirs without supplication.

Core Idea
The latecomer to funeral prayer should start immediately; missed takbirs are made up without supplication.

This passage tackles the scenario of joining funeral prayer late. It addresses whether to wait or start, how to make up missed takbirs, and the intra-school difference. The key is to ensure the prayer is completed before the bier is lifted, following the mufta bihi view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The funeral prayer is fard kifayah. The latecomer (masbuq) must attempt to join; his obligation depends on the ruling applicable to his situation.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites a qiyas (analogy) to a person catching the imam in prostration: the start is valid even if the performed actions are not counted. This proves the latecomer's takbir is validly initiated even if not counted.
The dalil is implicit: 'كمن أدرك الإمام في السجود'.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa held that the latecomer should wait (and if he misses all four takbirs, the prayer is missed). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (with al-Shafi'i) held he should start immediately. The text declares the latter as mufta bihi ('وعليه الفتوى').
The ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi and also cross-madhhab.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
According to the relied-upon view, the latecomer makes takbir upon arrival and follows the imam for subsequent takbirs; after the imam's taslim, he makes up the missed takbirs in order without supplication.
5
Handle supplementary scenarios
The supplement (tamama) provides specific cases: if he catches the first takbir but does not say it, he says it alone; if he misses the first, he joins the imam's current takbir and makes up after taslim; if he misses all four, he can make opening takbir before imam's taslim and then complete three takbirs quickly before the bier is lifted.
Abu Hanifa's alternate view: if he misses all four takbirs without making any, the prayer is lost.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينتظر المسبوق ولو لم ينتظر وكبر لا يفسد تكبيره عند الطرفين، لكن ما أداه غير معتبر، ويكون شارعاً، وعدم اعتبار المؤدى لا ينافي صحة الشروع بوجه، ولا يلزم من اعتبار شروعه اعتبار ما أداه كمن أدرك الإمام في السجود صح شروعه مع أنه لا يعتبر ما أداه من السجود مع الإمام، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي: يكبر حين يحضر، وعليه الفتوى، وقضى المسبوق ما بقي سبقاً بغير دعاء؛ لأنه لو قضى به ترفع الجنازة فتبطل الصلاة. (فتح) تتمة: رجل أدرك أول التكبير من صلاة الجنازة ولم يكبر كبر هو ولا ينتظر التكبيرة الثانية؛ لأن محلها قائم، فإن لم يكبر حتى كبر الإمام الثانية كبر الثانية مع الإمام ولم يكبر الأولى حتى يسلم الإمام؛ لأنه لو كبر للأولى كان قضاء، والمقتدي لا يشتغل بقضاء ما سبق قبل فراغ الإمام، وإن لم يكبر مع الإمام حتى كبر الإمام أربعاً، كبر هو للافتتاح قبل أن يسلم الإمام ثم يكبر ثلاثا قبل أن ترفع الجنازة متتابعاً لا دعاء فيها، فإذا رفعت الجنازة من الأرض يقطع، وعن أبي حنيفة: إذا لم يكبر حتى كبر الإمام أربعاً فاتته صلاة الجنازة وإن كبر مع الإمام التكبيرة الأولى :
The latecomer waits. Even if he does not wait and makes takbir, his takbir is not invalidated according to both parties, but what he performed is not considered, and he becomes a starter. The non-consideration of what he performed does not contradict the validity of the start; just as one who catches the imam in prostration, his start is valid even though what he performed in prostration with the imam is not considered. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: He makes takbir when he arrives; and this is the fatwa. The latecomer makes up what he missed in order without supplication, because if he makes it with supplication, the bier will be lifted and the prayer invalidated. (Fath) Supplement: A man catches the first takbir of the funeral prayer but does not make takbir; he should make takbir himself and not wait for the second takbir, because its place is standing. If he does not make takbir until the imam makes the second, he makes the second with the imam and does not make the first until the imam makes taslim, because if he made the first it would be qada, and the follower does not busy himself with qada before the imam finishes. If he does not make takbir with the imam until the imam has made four, he makes the opening takbir before the imam's taslim, then makes three takbirs in succession before the bier is lifted, without supplication. When the bier is lifted from the ground, he stops. From Abu Hanifa: If he does not make takbir until the imam has made four, he has missed the funeral prayer, even if he makes the first takbir with the imam.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage provides detailed fiqh for a latecomer (masbuq) to the funeral prayer. The key rule: the latecomer should not perform missed takbirs (qada) until after the imam's taslim. If he does perform them earlier, his action is not counted. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is from Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i: he should start takbir immediately upon arrival. The 'tamama' gives scenario-based guidance: if he catches the first takbir but does not say it, he must say it himself. If he delays, he joins the imam at the current takbir and makes up the missed ones after taslim without supplication (to avoid the bier being lifted). If he misses all four takbirs, some say he has missed the prayer entirely; other views allow him to make the opening takbir before imam's taslim and then complete the remaining three quickly.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joins the funeral prayer late and misses some takbirs.
القضاء (al-qada): Making up missed parts of the prayer after the imam completes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He cannot pray at all
B) He should make the opening takbir before the imam's taslim, then make three takbirs quickly without supplication
C) He should wait until the bier is lifted and then pray
D) He should follow the imam's extra takbirs

Key Takeaway
The latecomer's best practice is to start takbir immediately upon arrival; missed takbirs are made up after the imam's taslim without supplication.

Raising Hands and the Four Takbirs in Funeral Prayer
Detailed exposition of funeral prayer actions and the hand-raising debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of funeral prayer, identify the ruling on raising hands, and explain the evidence from hadith and disagreement with Shafi'i.

Core Idea
In Hanafi funeral prayer, hands raised only in first takbir; proof: Prophet's practice at Najashi funeral.

The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) has a specific sequence of four takbirs with distinct recitations. One of the key differences between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools is whether to raise hands in each takbir or only the first. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, its evidence, and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The funeral prayer is fard kifayah; the described method (four takbirs, specific recitations, hands raised only in first) is sunnah muakkadah. Your task is to note the mandatory and recommended elements.
The prayer itself is obligatory on the community, but the specific procedure is established by sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith from Ibn Abbas and Abu Hurayra narrated by al-Daraqutni: the Prophet raised hands only in the first takbir. Identify the hadith text and its source.
The hadith is ahad but considered qati' al-dalala in meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit action (رفع يديه في أول تكبيرة ثم لا يعود) directly shows that raising hands is confined to the first takbir. Understand how this phrase provides the proof.
The phrase 'then does not return' negates any later raising.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hands are raised at every takbir, based on the practice of Ibn 'Umar and analogy to other prayers. Compare the opposing evidence.
The Hanafi response is that the specific hadith takes precedence over general analogy.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi because the Prophet's practice at the Najashi funeral with four takbirs abrogated earlier practices, and the direct hadith is stronger. Understand why this view is chosen.
The masbuq (latecomer) should wait and give salam with the imam, not prematurely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصلاة على الصبي بعد الأولى، وصلاة على النبي عليه بعد الثانية، ودعاء بعد الثالثة، وتسليمتين بعد التكبيرة الأولى كما في التشهد التكبيرة الثانية التكبيرة الثالثة الرابعة، فلو كبر خمسا لم يُتبع، ولا يستغفر الصبي، ويقول: "اللهم اجعله لنا فرَطا، واجعله لنا أجرا وذخرا ، واجعله لنا شافعا ومشفعا"، وينتظر المسبوق. بعد الأولى: أي التكبيرة الأولى، ويرفع يديه في هذه فقط، وقال الشافعي يقرأ الفاتحة عقب الثناء. (مسكين) ودعاء بأمور الآخرة، والمأثور حسن وهو: "اللهم اغفر لحينا وميتنا وشاهدنا وغائبنا وصغيرنا وكبيرنا وذكرنا وأنثانا، اللهم من أحييته منا فأحيه على الإسلام ومن توفيته منا فتوفه على الإيمان". (مسكين) وتسليمتين وليس بعدها دعاء سوى السلام وقيل يقول: "اللهم ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة، وفي الآخرة حسنة، وقنا برحمتك عذاب القبر وعذاب النار"، وعند الشافعي يسلم تسليمة واحدة وقوله : فلو كبر خمسا لم يتبع؛ لأنه عليه حين صلى على النجاشي كبر أربع تكبيرات، وثبت عليها إلى أن توفي، فنسخت ما قبلها، وقيد بالخمس؛ لأنه لو كبر ستاً لا يتبع ،اتفاقاً، خلافاً لزفر قياساً على تكبيرات الزوائد في العيد، وعن أبي حنيفة يسلم حين اشتغل إمامه بالخطأ، وعنه أنه ينتظر سلام الإمام يسلم معه وهو المختار، ولا يرفع يديه إلا في التكبيرة الأولى خلافاً للشافعي، فإنه يرفع في كل تكبيرة؛ لأن ابن عمر لما كان يفعل ذلك، ولنا: ما رواه الدار قطني عن ابن عباس وأبي هريرة أنه عليه كان إذا صلى على جنازة رفع يديه في أول تكبيرة ثم لا يعود. (فتح)
The funeral prayer for a child: after the first takbir, and sending blessings on the Prophet after the second, and supplication after the third, and two taslims after the fourth takbir, as in the tashahhud. The second takbir, the third takbir, the fourth. So if he says five takbirs, he is not followed, and one does not ask forgiveness for the child, and he says: 'O Allah, make him a precursor for us, and make him a reward and treasure for us, and make him an intercessor and accepted intercessor for us.' And the latecomer waits. After the first: meaning the first takbir, and he raises his hands in this one only. Al-Shafi'i said: recite al-Fatihah after the praise. And supplication for matters of the Hereafter, and the transmitted supplication is good: 'O Allah, forgive our living and our dead, our present and our absent, our young and our old, our male and our female. O Allah, whoever You give life from us, give him life upon Islam, and whoever You take death from us, take him in faith.' And two taslims and there is no supplication after them except the salam. And it was said: he says: 'O Allah our Lord, give us in this world good, and in the Hereafter good, and protect us by Your mercy from the torment of the grave and the torment of the Fire.' And according to al-Shafi'i, he gives one taslim. And his saying: if he says five, it is not followed; because he (peace be upon him) when he prayed over al-Najashi said four takbirs, and persisted upon them until he died, so it abrogated what was before it. And it is restricted to five; because if he said six, he is not followed, by agreement, contrary to Zufar, by analogy to the extra takbirs in the Eid prayer. And from Abu Hanifa: he gives salam when his imam occupies himself with a mistake; and from him: he waits for the imam's salam and gives salam with him, and this is the chosen opinion. And he does not raise his hands except in the first takbir, contrary to al-Shafi'i, for he raises in every takbir; because Ibn 'Umar used to do that. And for us: what al-Daraqutni narrated from Ibn 'Abbas and Abu Hurayra that he (peace be upon him) when he prayed over a funeral, he raised his hands in the first takbir then did not repeat. (Fath)
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage details the Hanafi method of funeral prayer. The prayer consists of four takbirs. After the first, praise (thana) is recited; after the second, blessings on the Prophet; after the third, dua for the deceased; after the fourth, two salams. The hands are raised only in the first takbir, based on a hadith from Ibn Abbas and Abu Hurayra reported by al-Daraqutni. Al-Shafi'i differs: he recites Fatiha after the first takbir and raises hands at each takbir. The Hanafi proof is the Prophet's practice at the funeral of al-Najashi, where he said four takbirs and did not change, abrogating the previous practice of more. If someone says five, the follower should not follow but wait. The latecomer (masbuq) should wait, according to the chosen view, though Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i say he should start immediately.

Key Terms
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbirat al-ihram): The first takbir that commences the funeral prayer, after which hands are raised.
تسليمة (taslimah): The greeting of peace at the end of the prayer; Hanafi observes two taslims, Shafi'i one.
فرط (farat): A precursor who goes ahead to prepare a place in the afterlife for his family.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in the funeral prayer, in which takbir does the imam raise his hands?
A) In the first takbir only
B) In all four takbirs
C) In the first and third takbirs
D) In none of them

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the funeral prayer has four takbirs with hands raised only in the first, based on the Prophet's established practice.

Funeral Prayer for a Child: The Special Supplication
Specifies rulings and supplication for a child's funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the structure of the funeral prayer for a child and recite the prescribed supplication, distinguishing it from the adult version.

Core Idea
A child's funeral prayer omits istighfar and uses a unique dua of intercession and reward.

The funeral prayer for a child follows the same four-takbir structure as for an adult, but the supplication is different. This reflects the Islamic belief that children who die before puberty are sinless. Instead of seeking forgiveness, we ask Allah to make the child a precursor and intercessor for the parents. This lesson presents that specific dua and its meaning.

Guided Path
1
Recall the standard funeral prayer sequence
Review the four takbirs with specific actions after each: after first takbir recite Sana, after second send blessings on the Prophet, after third make dua, after fourth say salam.
This sequence is identical for adults and children.
2
Identify the difference for a child
After the third takbir, instead of asking forgiveness (istighfar), recite the prescribed dua that asks Allah to make the child a precursor, reward, treasure, and intercessor.
Istighfar is omitted because the child died before puberty and has no sins.
3
Memorize the prescribed dua
Learn the Arabic: 'اللهم اجعله لنا فرطا، واجعله لنا أجرا وذخرا، واجعله لنا شافعا ومشفعا' and its meaning.
Break it into phrases: farat (precursor), ajran wa dhukhran (reward and treasure), shafi'an wa mushaffa'an (intercessor and accepted intercessor).
4
Understand the key terms
Farat: one who goes ahead to prepare a place for family in Paradise. Mushaffa': one whose intercession is accepted. These highlight the child's blessings for parents.
These terms are specific to the child's dua; for adults, we say 'ghufran' (forgiveness).
5
Apply the ruling
Practice leading the funeral prayer for a child, ensuring you use the correct dua and avoid istighfar.
The same ruling applies to an insane or mentally disabled person who died before adulthood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصلاة على الصبي بعد الأولى، وصلاة على النبي عليه بعد الثانية، ودعاء بعد الثالثة، وتسليمتين بعد التكبيرة الأولى كما في التشهد التكبيرة الثانية التكبيرة الثالثة الرابعة، فلو كبر خمسا لم يُتبع، ولا يستغفر الصبي، ويقول: "اللهم اجعله لنا فرَطا، واجعله لنا أجرا وذخرا ، واجعله لنا شافعا ومشفعا"
The funeral prayer for a child: after the first takbir, and sending blessings on the Prophet after the second, and supplication after the third, and two taslims after the fourth takbir, as in the tashahhud. The second takbir, the third takbir, the fourth. So if he says five takbirs, he is not followed, and one does not ask forgiveness for the child, and he says: 'O Allah, make him a precursor for us, and make him a reward and treasure for us, and make him an intercessor and accepted intercessor for us.'
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage gives the specific rulings for the funeral prayer on a child. The structure is the same as for an adult: four takbirs with specific actions after each. However, the supplication after the third takbir is different: instead of asking for forgiveness, the imam prays that the child be a precursor (farat), reward, treasure, and intercessor. This is because a child who died before puberty has no sins, so istighfar is inappropriate. The same applies to the insane and mentally disabled. The specific dua is mentioned.

Key Terms
فرط (farat): One who goes ahead to prepare a place in Paradise for his family.
مشفع (mushaffa'): One whose intercession is accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is istighfar (asking forgiveness) not recited in the funeral prayer for a child?
A) Because children are not Muslim
B) Because children are sinless and do not need forgiveness
C) Because children are not considered deceased
D) Because the dua is too long

Key Takeaway
In the funeral prayer for a child, instead of seeking forgiveness, we ask Allah to make the child a precursor and intercessor for the parents.

The Masbuq in Funeral Prayer: Wait or Start Immediately?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on masbuq in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the masbuq in funeral prayer and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The masbuq should start immediately, then make up missed takbirs without dua.

When you arrive late for a funeral prayer, should you wait for the imam or start right away? The Hanafi school has two views, and knowing which one is relied upon for fatwa is essential for correct practice. This lesson examines the evidence and the preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the passage addresses the masbuq in funeral prayer: whether he should wait or start immediately.
2
State the two Hanafi views
Abu Hanifa (and early Hanafi) says wait; Abu Yusuf (and later fatwa) says start immediately. Know the difference.
Abu Yusuf's view is mufta bihi.
3
Analyze the analogy (qiyas)
The passage compares the masbuq to one who catches the imam in sujud: his start is valid but performed actions are not counted. Understand the illa (effective cause).
The illa is that the action is performed before the proper alignment with the imam.
4
Understand the tarjih mechanism
Note why Abu Yusuf's view is preferred: it is easier in practice and avoids the risk of the funeral being lifted.
The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view.
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical outcome: under Abu Hanifa, you wait and then pray alone; under Abu Yusuf, you join immediately and make up later.
This difference affects how latecomers act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينتظر المسبوق ولو لم ينتظر وكبر لا يفسد تكبيره عند الطرفين، لكن ما أداه غير معتبر، ويكون شارعاً، وعدم اعتبار المؤدى لا ينافي صحة الشروع بوجه، ولا يلزم من اعتبار شروعه اعتبار ما أداه كمن أدرك الإمام في السجود صح شروعه مع أنه لا يعتبر ما أداه من السجود مع الإمام، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي: يكبر حين يحضر، وعليه الفتوى، وقضى المسبوق ما بقي سبقاً بغير دعاء؛ لأنه لو قضى به ترفع الجنازة فتبطل الصلاة. (فتح)
The latecomer waits. And if he does not wait and says takbir, his takbir does not invalidate according to both parties, but what he performed is not considered, and he is considered as starting. The non-consideration of what he performed does not contradict the validity of starting; nor does consideration of his starting necessitate consideration of what he performed, like the case of one who catches the imam in sujud: his starting is valid though his performed sujud with the imam is not considered. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: he says takbir when he arrives, and upon that is the fatwa. The latecomer makes up what he missed without supplication, because if he supplicates the funeral will be lifted and the prayer invalidated. (Fath)
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage discusses the masbuq (latecomer) in funeral prayer. The Hanafi position (from Abu Hanifa) is that the masbuq should not start immediately but wait and join the imam at whatever stage he finds him, then after the imam's salam, he makes up the missed takbirs without dua. If he does start earlier, his prayer is valid in terms of initiation, but his performed actions are not counted. This is analogous to catching the imam in sujud: the latecomer starts with the imam but his sujud is not considered separate. Abu Yusuf disagreed, saying he should start immediately, and that view is considered the mufta bihi. The reason for not making dua when making up missed takbirs is the risk that the bier will be lifted, invalidating the prayer.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): One who arrives late and misses part of the prayer with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wait for the imam to finish and then pray alone
B) Start immediately and then make up missed takbirs without supplication
C) Leave and not pray
D) Recite only the first takbir

Key Takeaway
The masbuq in funeral prayer should start immediately (per the mufta bihi view) and make up missed takbirs without supplication.

Position of Imam in Funeral Prayer
States the recommended position for the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the imam's placement relative to the deceased and identify the views of other schools.

Core Idea
Imam stands opposite the chest for both male and female deceased.

In the funeral prayer, the imam's position relative to the body is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation. The Hanafi school has a specific view that differs from other madhahib. This lesson clarifies where the imam should stand and briefly notes the differences to help you avoid confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the imam's standing position during janazah prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that it is sunnah (recommended) to stand opposite the chest.
This applies to both male and female deceased.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi variation
There is a weak riwayah from Abu Hanifa that suggests opposite the head for a man and opposite the middle for a woman, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is opposite the chest for both.
The majority of Hanafi scholars prefer the chest.
3
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school says opposite the head (man) and opposite the shoulder (woman); the Maliki school says opposite the middle; the Hanbali school says chest for man, middle for woman.
These are legitimate differences of ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقوم للرجل والمرأة بحذاء الصدر، ولم يصلوا ركبانا ولا في مسجد، وعند الشافعي بحذاء رأسه وبحذاء مالك بحذاء وسطه، وبحذاء منكبها، وعند أحمد بحذاء الصدر له وعند الوسط لها
And he stands for the man and the woman opposite the chest. And they do not pray on horseback nor in a mosque. According to al-Shafi'i, opposite the head, and according to Malik, opposite the middle, and opposite the shoulder, and according to Ahmad, opposite the chest for him and opposite the middle for her.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage gives the recommended position for the imam relative to the body. The Hanafi view is that for both man and woman, the imam stands at the chest area, near the heart. For a man, it is the chest; for a woman, the same. The preferred arrangement of rows is three rows if possible, based on a hadith. Other schools differ: Shafi'i says for man opposite head, for woman opposite shoulders; Malik says opposite middle for both; Ahmad says chest for man and middle for woman. The passage also mentions that one should not pray on horseback or inside a mosque, which is covered in a separate lesson.

Key Terms
بحذاء الصدر (bihidha' al-sadr): Opposite the chest, the recommended position for the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Opposite the chest

Key Takeaway
The imam stands opposite the chest for both male and female deceased in the Hanafi school.

Prohibition of Funeral Prayer on Horseback and in Mosque
Explains two prohibitions in funeral prayer and an inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on funeral prayer on horseback and in mosque, and explain the inter-madhhab dispute regarding mosque prayer.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer on horseback is invalid unless excused; in a mosque it is disliked (makruh) without excuse.

This passage addresses two specific prohibitions in funeral prayer: performing it while riding and performing it inside a mosque. While the first is governed by necessity and istihsan, the second sparks an inter-madhhab dispute. We will examine the Hanafi position, the evidence from hadith, and the counterarguments from the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibitions
The passage begins with the ruling on riding (rukbanan) and then moves to the ruling on mosques (la fi masjid). Separate the two issues.
Both are discussed sequentially in the source.
2
Analyze the riding prohibition
Note that funeral prayer while riding is normally invalid because standing is a requirement. However, istihsan permits it if dismounting is impossible due to mud or rain. Also note the intra-Hanafi dispute about following a sitting imam.
The passage mentions the opinion of the two shaykhs vs. Muhammad.
3
Evaluate the mosque prohibition and its evidence
The Hanafi school considers it makruh (disliked) to pray funeral prayer in a mosque without excuse, based on the hadith 'Whoever prays over a deceased in the mosque has no reward.' Understand the reasoning: mosques are for obligatory prayers and there is risk of soiling.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud.
4
Compare with the opposing school's evidence
The Shafi'i and Hanbali schools permit it, citing the Prophet's prayer over Suhayl ibn Bayda' in the mosque and the nature of funeral prayer as supplication. The Hanafi response explains that incident as an exception due to i'tikaf or rain.
This is the core of the inter-madhhab dispute.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: Hanafis avoid mosques for funeral prayers unless the mosque is built for that purpose. The mufta bihi is makruh tahrimi without excuse.
Some later scholars say makruh tanzihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ركبانا: لأنها صلاة من وجه لوجود التحريمة، ولو تعذر النزول بطين أو مطر جاز الركوب فيها، وفي القياس لا يجوز؛ لأنه دعاء، وعدم الجواز استحسانا اعتبارا لوجه الصلاة، فإنها لا تجوز إلا قياما، وأشار إلى أنها لا تجوز القدرة على القيام، ولو كان الإمام مريضا فصلى قاعدا والناس خلفه قياما أجزأهم في قول الشيخين، وقال محمد: يجزئ الإمام، ولا يجزئ المأموم بناء على اقتداء القائم بالقاعد، ويسقط فرض الصلاة بصلاته إجماعا، ولا تجوز أيضا لو كان الميت على الدابة أو على أيدي الناس على المختار. (فتح، عيني) ولا في مسجد [ أي لا يصلي في مسجد جماعة على جنازة؛ فإنه مكروه بلا عذر تحريما، وقيل تنزيها، وعند الشافعي لا يكره. (مسكين] أي الصلاة على الجنازة في مسجد جماعة مكروه؛ لقوله عليه: "من صلى في المسجد على ميت فلا أجر له" وفي رواية فلا شيء له، رواه أبو داود، وأما المسجد الذي بني للصلاة عليها فلا يكره فيه، وعند الشافعي وأحمد: لا بأس بها في مسجد جماعة أيضا؛ لأن رسول الله صلى على جنازة سهيل بن بيضاء في المسجد؛ ولأنها دعاء وصلاة فالمسجد أولى، ولنا ما روينا؛ ولأنه لأداء المكتوبات فيه، ويحتمل تلويث المسجد، وتأويل ما رواه أنه عليه صلى عليه في المسجد بعذر الاعتكاف، وقيل: للمطر. (عيني، مستخلص)
On horseback: because it is a prayer in a certain sense due to the presence of the opening takbir. If alighting is impossible due to mud or rain, riding becomes permissible. In qiyas it is not permissible because it is supplication, and non-permissibility is by istihsan considering the aspect of prayer, for it is not permissible except while standing. And it indicates that it is not permissible when able to stand. If the imam is sick and prays sitting while people behind him stand, it suffices them according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: it suffices the imam but not the follower based on the principle of the standing following the sitting. The obligation of prayer is removed by his prayer by consensus. It is also not permissible if the deceased is on an animal or on people's hands according to the chosen view. (Fath, 'Ayni) And not in a mosque: meaning they should not pray in a mosque collectively over a funeral; for it is prohibitively disliked without an excuse, and some say merely disliked. According to al-Shafi'i, it is not disliked. (Miskin) That is, the funeral prayer in a mosque in congregation is disliked, due to his saying: 'Whoever prays over a deceased in the mosque has no reward' and in another version 'nothing for him', reported by Abu Dawud. As for a mosque built for the purpose (of funeral prayers), it is not disliked. According to al-Shafi'i and Ahmad: there is no harm in it even in a mosque, because the Prophet prayed over the funeral of Suhayl ibn Bayda' in the mosque, and because it is supplication and prayer, so the mosque is more deserving. For us (Hanafi), we have what we narrated; and because it is for the performance of obligatory prayers, and there is possibility of soiling the mosque, and the interpretation of what he (the narrator) narrated is that he prayed over it in the mosque due to a reason of i'tikaf, and it was said due to rain. (Ayni, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage addresses two prohibitions. First, funeral prayer should not be performed on horseback unless necessary due to mud or rain. If no excuse, it is forbidden because the prayer requires standing. The istihsan allows it when necessary. There is also a dispute about following a sitting imam: the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say it suffices, while Muhammad disagrees. Second, praying in a mosque is disliked (makruh tahrimi or tanzihi) without excuse, based on a hadith from Abu Dawud: the one who prays over a deceased in the mosque has no reward. The Shafi'i and Hanbali schools allow it, citing the Prophet's prayer for Suhayl ibn Bayda' in the mosque. The Hanafi response distinguishes that mosque was built for obligatory prayers, not funerals, and there is risk of soiling. The incident of the Prophet is interpreted as an exception due to i'tikaf or rain. Therefore, the Hanafi rule is to perform funeral prayer in the cemetery or a designated place outside the mosque.

Key Terms
ركبانا (rukbanan): On horseback (or any riding animal); usually prohibited for funeral prayer.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir that makes the prayer valid; it is present in funeral prayer, making it a prayer proper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing funeral prayer inside a mosque without an excuse?
A) Permissible and recommended
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Obligatory

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that funeral prayer on horseback is invalid without necessity, and funeral prayer inside a mosque is disliked (makruh) without excuse, based on a sahih hadith and the principle of preserving the sanctity of mosques.

When the Latecomer Joins the Funeral Prayer
Ruling on the latecomer in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a latecomer starts the funeral prayer and explain the basis for the difference with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
A latecomer must wait for the imam's next takbir, then make up missed takbirs after salam.

The funeral prayer is unique: it consists of four takbirs with no bowing or prostration. When a person arrives late, the question arises: should he start immediately to catch as many takbirs as possible, or should he wait for the imam to lead him? The Hanafi school takes a careful approach, analogizing the follower's entry to regular prayer. This lesson dissects the rules for the masbuq in janazah prayer.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
The passage presents: (a) a follower already in prayer whose imam omitted some takbirs — he says them and follows; (b) a latecomer arriving after the imam has started — he must wait for the imam's next takbir. Identify which scenario applies to a masbuq.
The latecomer scenario is the main focus of this lesson.
2
State the relied-upon Hanafi position
According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the mufta bihi position), the latecomer must wait until the imam says the next takbir. He then says his opening takbir with the imam, follows for the remaining takbirs, and after the imam's salam makes up the missed takbirs before the bier is lifted.
This is the view preferred by Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.
3
Compare alternative views
Abu Hanifa: entry only if you catch the imam before the fourth takbir. Abu Yusuf: entry as long as salam not said. Al-Shafi'i: say takbir immediately upon arrival. Understand the differences and their practical consequences.
Al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf share a similar immediate-entry view, but for different reasons.
4
Understand the basis (dalil)
The Hanafi position is based on qiyas (analogy) to regular prayer: the follower must enter with the imam's takbir to maintain connection. The funeral prayer, though a supplication, still has the structure of prayer (takbirs, salam). Thus, the same principle applies.
The text states: 'the principle is that the follower enters with the imam's takbir'.
5
Apply the exception: person present but heedless
If someone was present in the row and forgot to say the opening takbir, he says it immediately without waiting, because he is not a latecomer. This shows the importance of the tahrimah timing.
This exception is by agreement (ittifaqan).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لم يكبر الثانية والثالثة يكبرهما ثم يكبر مع الإمام، وإذا كبر الإمام على جنازة تكبيرة أو تكبيرتين، فجاء رجل لا يكبر هذا الرجل حتى يكبر الإمام، فيكبر تكبيرة الافتتاح، ويكون مسبوقا بما كبر به الإمام قبله بخلاف كان حاضراً قائما في الصف ولم يكبر للافتتاح مع الإمام تغافلا، فإنه يكبر ولا ينتظر تكبيرة الإمام، والأصل عندهما أن المقتدي يدخل في تكبيرة الإمام، فإذا فرغ الإمام من الرابعة تعذر عليه الدخول، وعند أبي يوسف: يدخل إذا بقيت التحريمة أي إلى ما قبل السلام. (فتح) لا من: أي لو سبق بتكبيرة أو بتكبيرتين ينتظر حتى يكبر الإمام فيكبر معه، فإذا سلم قضى ما بقي عليه قبل رفع الجنازة، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي: يكبر حين يحضر. (مسكين) حاضرا أي في حال التحريمة فلم يكبر مع الإمام لا ينتظر تكبيرة الإمام الثانية بل يكبر حين أراد اتفاقاً، ومن حضر بعد الرابعة قبل السلام فاتته الصلاة. (مسكين)
If the imam did not say the second and third takbir, the follower says them and then says takbir with the imam. If the imam says one or two takbirs over a janaza and a man arrives, that man does not say takbir until the imam says takbir; then he says the opening takbir and is considered a latecomer for what the imam said before him. However, if he was present standing in the row and did not say the opening takbir with the imam out of heedlessness, he says takbir and does not wait for the imam's takbir. The principle according to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the follower enters with the imam's takbir. When the imam finishes the fourth, it becomes impossible for him to enter. According to Abu Yusuf: he enters as long as the opening takbir remains, i.e., before the salam. (Fath) 'Not from' meaning: if he missed one or two takbirs, he waits until the imam says takbir and says takbir with him. When the imam says salam, he makes up what remained before the janaza is lifted. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: he says takbir when he arrives. (Miskin) 'present' meaning at the time of the opening takbir and did not say takbir with the imam, he does not wait for the second takbir of the imam but says takbir when he wants by agreement. Whoever arrives after the fourth before the salam has missed the prayer.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the latecomer (masbuq) in funeral prayer. The funeral prayer consists of four takbirs without ruku or sujud. The text begins by stating that if a person missed the second and third takbirs, he should say them and then say takbir with the imam. If the imam has already said one or two takbirs when the latecomer arrives, the latecomer must wait until the imam says the next takbir before starting. He then says his opening takbir (tahrimah) and becomes a latecomer, meaning he must make up the missed takbirs after the imam's salam. However, if he was present in the row but forgot to say the opening takbir with the imam due to heedlessness, he should say it immediately without waiting for the imam's next takbir. The principle according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is that the follower enters the prayer with the imam's takbir; once the imam has finished the fourth takbir, entry is no longer possible. Abu Yusuf allows entry as long as the imam has not yet said salam. The text then presents a difference: according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, if a person arrives after the imam has started, he says takbir immediately and does not wait. But the relied-upon Hanafi position, from Kanz al-Daqaiq, is that he must wait for the imam to say the next takbir. After the imam's salam, he completes any missed takbirs before the janaza is lifted. If someone arrives after the fourth takbir but before salam, he has missed the entire funeral prayer.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer after the imam has already started, missing part of the prayer.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir that makes actions of prayer forbidden (haram) until salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man arrives at the funeral prayer after the imam has already said two takbirs. According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what should he do?
A) He should immediately say the opening takbir and then say takbir with the imam.
B) He should wait until the imam says the third takbir, then say the opening takbir and continue with the imam.
C) He should not join because he missed the first two takbirs.
D) He should wait until the imam finishes the prayer and then repeat the entire funeral prayer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a latecomer to the funeral prayer must wait for the imam's next takbir before joining, and then complete missed takbirs after the imam's salam.

Imam's Position and Row Count in Funeral Prayer
Rulings on imam's position and row count in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on where the imam stands relative to the deceased and the recommended number of rows, and distinguish them from other schools.

Core Idea
Imam stands opposite the chest; three rows are recommended for forgiveness.

In the funeral prayer, specific etiquettes are recommended for the imam's position and the congregation's arrangement. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq outlines the preferred position of the imam relative to the deceased and the ideal number of rows. While these are not obligatory, they carry great reward and reflect the sunnah. Understanding these details helps you perform the funeral prayer in a manner that aligns with the Hanafi school while being aware of valid differences among the schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage covers two distinct but related rulings: the imam's standing position and the number of rows. Keep them separate in your mind.
2
Understand the recommended position
The imam should stand opposite the chest of the deceased. This is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib. Any alignment with a part of the body suffices for validity.
The chest is chosen because it is the seat of faith (iman) and intercession (shafa'ah).
3
Understand the number of rows
It is recommended to form at least three rows. Even if only six men are present, they should arrange as three, then two, then one. The hadith promises forgiveness for the deceased if three rows pray.
This applies regardless of size of congregation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab differences
Abu Hanifa has narrations varying the position by gender, but the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is opposite the chest for all. Other schools differ: Shafi'i prefers head, Maliki prefers middle, Hanbali differentiates by gender.
These are legitimate ikhtilafat; all are valid but the Hanafi position is as stated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقوم للرجل والمرأة بحذاء الصدر. بحذاء الصدر أي قريب منه؛ لأنه محل الإيمان والشفاعة لأجله، وهذا على سبيل الاستحباب، وإلا فمحاذاة جزء من الميت لابد منه. والأفضل أن تكون الصفوف ثلاثة حتى لو كانوا ستة رجال اصطف ثلاثة ثم اثنان ثم واحد؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: 'من اصطف عليه ثلاثة صفوف من المسلمين غفر له'. وعن أبي حنيفة في رواية: أنه يقوم للرجل بحذاء رأسه، وللمرأة بحذاء وسطها، وفي رواية بحذاء الوسط فيهما. وعند الشافعي بحذاء رأسه، وعند مالك بحذاء وسطه، وعند أحمد بحذاء الصدر للرجل والوسط للمرأة.
He stands for the man and the woman opposite the chest. 'Opposite the chest' means close to it, because it is the place of faith and intercession for him, and this is on the basis of recommendation, otherwise alignment with a part of the deceased is necessary. The best is that the rows be three, so that if there are six men, they line up three, then two, then one, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever has three rows of Muslims lined up over him will be forgiven.' And from Abu Hanifa in one narration: he stands for the man opposite his head, and for the woman opposite her middle, and in another narration opposite the middle for both. According to al-Shafi'i: opposite the head; according to Malik: opposite the middle; and according to Ahmad: opposite the chest for a man and the middle for a woman.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings: (1) the imam's standing position relative to the deceased, and (2) the recommended number of rows. For the position, the imam stands facing the chest of the deceased for both men and women. This is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory; any alignment that includes a part of the deceased is sufficient. There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa that he stands opposite the head for a man and the middle for a woman, but the preferred view is the chest. The passage then contrasts other schools: al-Shafi'i prefers opposite the head, Malik opposite the middle, and Ahmad opposite the chest for a man and the middle for a woman. As for rows, it is recommended that the congregation form three rows. Even if only six men are present, they should arrange themselves into three rows of three, two, and one. The hadith states that praying over a deceased person with three rows ensures forgiveness. This applies to all participants in the funeral prayer.

Key Terms
بحذاء الصدر (bihidha' al-sadr): Facing the chest of the deceased; the imam stands so that his chest aligns with the chest of the deceased.
صفوف ثلاثة (sufuf thalath): Three rows of mourners in the funeral prayer; the minimum recommended number for the crowd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, where should the imam stand for the funeral prayer of a woman?
A) Opposite her head
B) Opposite her chest
C) Opposite her middle
D) Opposite her feet

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends the imam stand opposite the chest and the congregation form three rows; these are sunnah, not obligatory.
